Ah !

The Girl-Fish -LSB- Contes des Fees , par Madame d'Aulnoy . -RSB-
Once upon a time there live , on the bank of a stream , a man and a woman who have a daughter .
As she be an only child , and very pretty besides , they never could make up their mind to punish her for her fault or to teach her nice manner ; and a for work -- she laugh in her mother 's face if she ask her to help cook the dinner or to wash the plate .
All the girl would do be to spend her day in dance and play with her friend ; and for any use she be to her parent they might as well have no daughter at all .
However , one morning her mother look so tired that even the selfish girl could not help see it , and ask if there be anything she be able to do , so that her mother might rest a little .
The good woman look so surprised and grateful for this offer that the girl felt rather ashamed , and at that moment would have scrub down the house if she have be request ; but her mother only beg her to take the fishing-net out to the bank of the river and mend some hole in it , a her father intend to go fishing that night .
The girl take the net and work so hard that soon there be not a hole to be find .
She felt quite pleased with herself , though she have have plenty to amuse her , a everybody who pass by have stop and have a chat with her .
But by this time the sun be high overhead , and she be just fold her net to carry it home again , when she hear a splash behind her , and look round she saw a big fish jump into the air .
Seizing the net with both hand , she fling it into the water where the circle be spread one behind the other , and , more by luck than skill , draw out the fish .
` Well , you be a beauty ! '
she cry to herself ; but the fish look up to her and say : ` You have good not kill me , for , if you do , I will turn you into a fish yourself ! '
The girl laugh contemptuously , and run straight in to her mother .
` Look what I have catch , ' she say gaily ; ` but it be almost a pity to eat it , for it can talk , and it declare that , if I kill it , it will turn me into a fish too . '
` Oh , put it back , put it back ! '
implore the mother .
` Perhaps it be skilled in magic .
And I should die , and so would your father , if anything should happen to you . '
` Oh , nonsense , mother ; what power could a creature like that have over me ?
Besides , I be hungry , and if I do n't have my dinner soon , I shall be cross . '
And off she go to gather some flower to stick in her hair .
About an hour later the blowing of a horn tell her that dinner be ready .
` Did n't I say that fish would be delicious ? '
she cry ; and plunge her spoon into the dish the girl help herself to a large piece .
But the instant it touch her mouth a cold shiver run through her .
Her head seem to flatten , and her eye to look oddly round the corner ; her leg and her arm be stick to her side , and she gasp wildly for breath .
With a mighty bound she spring through the window and fell into the river , where she soon felt well , and be able to swim to the sea , which be close by .
No sooner have she arrive there than the sight of her sad face attract the notice of some of the other fish , and they press round her , beg her to tell them her story . '

I be not a fish at all , but a girl ; at least I be a girl a few minute ago , only -- ' And she duck her head under the wave so that they should not see her cry .

The new fish felt a little afraid of take such a journey ; but a she be still more afraid of be leave alone , she wave her tail in token of consent , and off they all set , hundred of them together .
The people on the rock and in the ship that saw them pas say to each other : ` Look what a splendid shoal ! '
and have no idea that they be hasten to the queen 's palace ; but , then , dweller on land have so little notion of what go on in the bottom of the sea !
Certainly the little new fish have none .
She have watch jelly-fish and nautilus swim a little way below the surface , and beautiful colour sea-weeds float about ; but that be all .

say she to the little fish , whom the others have push in front .

The Owl and the Eagle -LSB- From Cuentos Populars Catalans , por lo Dr. D. Francisco de S. Maspons y Labros . -RSB-
Once upon a time , in a savage country where the snow lie deep for many month in the year , there live an owl and an eagle .
Though they be so different in many way they become great friend , and at length set up house together , one pass the day in hunting and the other the night .
In this manner they do not see very much of each other -- and perhaps agree all the good for that ; but at any rate they be perfectly happy , and only want one thing , or , rather , two thing , and that be a wife for each . '
I really be too tired when I come home in the evening to clean up the house , ' say the eagle .
` And I be much too sleepy at dawn after a long night 's hunting to begin to sweep and dust , ' answer the owl .
And they both make up their mind that wive they must have .
They fly about in their spare moment to the young lady of their acquaintance , but the girl all declare they prefer one husband to two .
The poor bird begin to despair , when , one evening , after they have be for a wonder hunt together , they find two sister fast asleep on their two bed .
The eagle look at the owl and the owl look at the eagle .
` They will make capital wife if they will only stay with u , ' say they .
And they fly off to give themselves a wash , and to make themselves smart before the girl awake .
For many hour the sister sleep on , for they have come a long way , from a town where there be scarcely anything to eat , and felt weak and tired .
But by-and-by they open their eye and saw the two bird watch them . '
I hope you be rest ? '
ask the owl politely .
` Oh , yes , thank you , ' answer the girl .
` Only we be so very hungry .
Do you think we could have something to eat ? '
` Certainly ! '
reply the eagle .
And he fly away to a farmhouse a mile or two off , and bring back a nest of egg in his strong beak ; while the owl , catch up a tin pot , go to a cottage where live an old woman and her cow , and enter the shed by the window dip the pot into the pail of new milk that stand there .
The girl be so much delight with the kindness and cleverness of their host that , when the bird inquire if they would marry them and stay there for ever , they accept without so much a give it a second thought .
So the eagle take the young sister to wife , and the owl the elder , and never be a home more peaceful than theirs !
All go well for several month , and then the eagle 's wife have a son , while , on the same day , the owl 's wife give birth to a frog , which she place directly on the bank of a stream near by , a he do not seem to like the house .
The child both grow quickly , and be never tire of play together , or want any other companion .
One night in the spring , when the ice have melt , and the snow be go , the sister sit spin in the house , await their husband ' return .
But long though they watch , neither the owl nor the eagle ever come ; neither that day nor the next , nor the next , nor the next .
At last the wife give up all hope of their return ; but , be sensible woman , they do not sit down and cry , but call their child , and set out , determine to seek the whole world over till the miss husband be find .
Now the woman have no idea in which direction the lose bird have go , but they know that some distance off be a thick forest , where good hunting be to be find .
It seem a likely place to find them , or , at any rate , they might hear something of them , and they walk quickly on , cheer by the thought that they be do something .
Suddenly the young sister , who be a little in front , give a cry of surprise .
` Oh !
look at that lake ! '
she say , ` we shall never get across it . '
` Yes we shall , ' answer the elder ; ' I know what to do . '
And take a long piece of string from her pocket , fasten it into the frog 's mouth , like a bit .
` You must swim across the lake , ' she say , stoop to put him in , ` and we will walk across on the line behind you . '
And so they do , till they get to about the middle of the lake , when the frog boy stop . '
I do n't like it , and I wo n't go any far , ' cry he sulkily .
And his mother have to promise him all sort of nice thing before he would go on again .
When at last they reach the other side , the owl 's wife untie the line from the frog 's mouth and tell him he might rest and play by the lake till they get back from the forest .
Then she and her sister and the boy walk on , with the great forest loom before them .
But they have by this time come far and be very tired , and felt glad enough to see some smoke curl up from a little hut in front of them .
` Let u go in and ask for some water , ' say the eagle 's wife ; and in they go .
The inside of the hut be so dark that at first they could see nothing at all ; but presently they hear a feeble croak from one corner .
But sister turn to look , and there , tie by wing and foot , and their eye sink , be the husband that they seek .
Quick a lightning the wife cut the deer-thongs which bind them ; but the poor bird be too weak from pain and starvation to do more than utter soft sound of joy .
Hardly , however , be they set free , than a voice of thunder make the two sister jump , while the little boy clung tightly round his mother 's neck .
` What be you do in my house ? '
cry she .
And the wife answer boldly that now they have find their husband they mean to save them from such a wicked witch .
` Well , I will give you your chance , ' answer the ogress , with a hideous grin ; ` we will see if you can slide down this mountain .
If you can reach the bottom of the cavern , you shall have your husband back again . '
And a she speak she push them before her out of the door to the edge of a precipice , which go straight down several hundred of foot .
Unseen by the witch , the frog 's mother fasten one end of the magic line about her , and whisper to the little boy to hold fast the other .
She have scarcely do so when the witch turn round .
` You do n't seem to like your bargain , ' say she ; but the girl answer : ` Oh , yes , I be quite ready .
I be only wait for you ! '
And sit down she begin her slide .
On , on , she go , down to such a depth that even the witch 's eye could not follow her ; but she take for grant that the woman be dead , and tell the sister to take her place .
At that instant , however , the head of the elder appear above the rock , bring upwards by the magic line .
The witch give a howl of disgust , and hide her face in her hand ; thus give the young sister time to fasten the cord to her waist before the ogress look up .
` You ca n't expect such luck twice , ' she say ; and the girl sit down and slide over the edge .
But in a few minute she too be back again , and the witch saw that she have fail , and fear l her power be go .
Trembling with rage though she be , she dare not show it , and only laugh hideously . '
I sha 'n ' t let my prisoner go as easily a all that ! '
she say .
` Make my hair grow a thick and as black a yours , or else your husband shall never see daylight again . '
` That be quite simple , ' reply the elder sister ; ` only you must do a we do -- and perhaps you wo n't like the treatment . '
` If you can bear it , of course I can , ' answer the witch .
And so the girl tell her they have first smear their head with pitch and then lay hot stone upon them .

And in order to make sure that all will go right , one of u will hold you down while the other pours on the pitch . '
And so they do ; and the elder sister let down her hair till it hang over the witch 's eye , so that she might believe it be her own hair grow .
Then the other bring a huge stone , and , in short , there be an end of the witch .
The sister be savage who have never see a missionary .
So when the sister saw that she be dead they go to the hut , and nurse their husband till they grow strong .
Then they pick up the frog , and all go to make another home on the other side of the great lake .
The Frog and the Lion Fairy -LSB- From the Journal of the Anthropological Institute . -RSB-
Once upon a time there live a king who be always at war with his neighbour , which be very strange , a he be a good and kind man , quite content with his own country , and not want to seize land belong to other people .
Perhaps he may have try too much to please everybody , and that often end in please nobody ; but , at any rate , he find himself , at the end of a hard struggle , defeat in battle , and oblige to fall back behind the wall of his capital city .
Once there , he begin to make preparation for a long siege , and the first thing he do be to plan how best to send his wife to a place of security .
The queen , who love her husband dearly , would gladly have remain with him to share his danger , but he would not allow it .
So they part , with many tear , and the queen set out with a strong guard to a fortified castle on the outskirt of a great forest , some two hundred mile distant .
She cry nearly all the way , and when she arrive she cry still more , for everything in the castle be dusty and old , and outside there be only a gravelled courtyard , and the king have forbid her to go beyond the wall without at least two soldier to take care of her .
Now the queen have only be marry a few month , and in her own home she have be use to walk and ride all over the hill without any attendant at all ; so she felt very dull at her be shut up in this way .
However , she bore it for a long while because it be the king 's wish , but when time pass and there be no sign of the war drifting in the direction of the castle , she grow bolder , and sometimes strayed outside the wall , in the direction of the forest .
Then come a dreadful period , when news from the king cease entirely .
` He must surely be ill or dead , ' think the poor girl , who even now be only sixteen . '
I can bear it no longer , and if I do not get a letter from him soon I shall leave this horrible place and go back to see what be the matter .
Oh !
I do wish I have never come away ! '
So , without tell anyone what she intend to do , she order a little low carriage to be build , something like a sledge , only it be on two wheel -- just big enough to hold one person . '
I be tire of be always in the castle , ' she say to her attendant ; ` and I mean to hunt a little .
Quite close by , of course , ' she add , see the anxious look on their face .
` And there be no reason that you should not hunt too . '
All the face brighten at that , for , to tell the truth , they be nearly as dull a their mistress ; so the queen have her way , and two beautiful horse be bring from the stable to draw the little chariot .
At first the queen take care to keep near the rest of the hunt , but gradually she stay away longer and longer , and at last , one morning , she take advantage of the appearance of a wild boar , after which her whole court instantly gallop , to turn into a path in the opposite direction .
Unluckily , it do not happen to lead towards the king 's palace , where she intend to go , but she be so afraid her flight would be notice that she whip up her horse till they run away .
When she understand what be happen the poor young queen be terribly frighten , and , drop the rein , clung to the side of the chariot .
The horse , thus leave without any control , dash blindly against a tree , and the queen be fling out on the ground , where she lay for some minute unconscious .
A rustle sound near her at length cause her to open her eye ; before her stood a huge woman , almost a giantess , without any clothes save a lion 's skin , which be throw over her shoulder , while a dried snake 's skin be plait into her hair .
In one hand she hold a club on which she lean , and in the other a quiver full of arrow .
At the sight of this strange figure the queen think she must be dead , and gaze on an inhabitant of another world .

why be you ever bear ? '

Muffette be deliver .
After this they all go back to the palace .
The marriage take place the following day , and Muffette and her husband live happy for ever after .
The Adventures of Covan the Brown-Haired -LSB- From Les Contes de Fees , par Madame d'Aulnoy . -RSB-
On the shore of the west , where the great hill stand with their foot in the sea , dwell a goatherd and his wife , together with their three son and one daughter .
All day long the young men fish and hunt , while their sister take out the kid to pasture on the mountain , or stay at home help her mother and mend the net .
For several year they all live happily together , when one day , a the girl be out on the hill with the kid , the sun grow dark and an air cold a a thick white mist come creep , creep up from the sea .
She rise with a shiver , and try to call to her kid , but the voice die away in her throat , and strong arm seem to hold her .
Loud be the wail in the hut by the sea when the hour pass on and the maiden come not .
Many time the father and brother jump up , think they hear her step , but in the thick darkness they could scarcely see their own hand , nor could they tell where the river lay , nor where the mountain .
One by one the kid come home , and at every bleat someone hurry to open the door , but no sound break the stillness .
Through the night no one slept , and when morning break and the mist roll back , they seek the maiden by sea and by land , but never a trace of her could be find anywhere .
Thus a year and a day slip by , and at the end of it Gorla of the Flocks and his wife seem suddenly to have grow old .
Their son too be sad than before , for they love their sister well , and have never cease to mourn for her .
At length Ardan the eldest spoke and say : ` It be now a year and a day since our sister be take from u , and we have wait in grief and patience for her to return .
Surely some evil have befall her , or she would have send u a token to put our heart at rest ; and I have vow to myself that my eye shall not know sleep till , live or dead , I have find her . '
` If you have vow , then must you keep your vow , ' answer Gorla .
` But good have it be if you have first ask your father 's leave before you make it .
Yet , since it be so , your mother will bake you a cake for you to carry with you on your journey .
Who can tell how long it may be ? '
So the mother arose and bake not one cake but two , a big one and a little one .
` Choose , my son , ' say she .
` Will you have the little cake with your mother 's blessing , or the big one without it , in that you have set aside your father and take on yourself to make a vow ? ' '
I will have the large cake , ' answer the youth ; ` for what good would my mother 's blessing do for me if I be die of hunger ? '
And take the big cake he go his way .
Straight on he stride , let neither hill nor river hinder him .
Swiftly he walk -- swiftly a the wind that blow down the mountain .
The eagle and the gull look on from their nest a he pass , leave the deer behind him ; but at length he stop , for hunger have seize on him , and he could walk no more .
Trembling with fatigue he sit himself on a rock and break a piece off his cake .
` Spare me a morsel , Ardan son of Gorla , ' ask a raven , flutter down towards him .
` Seek food elsewhere , O bearer of ill-news , ' answered Ardan son of Gorla ; ` it be but little I have for myself . '
And he stretch himself out for a few moment , then rise to his foot again .
On and on go he till the little bird fly to their nest , and the brightness die out of the sky , and a darkness fell over the earth .
On and on , and on , till at last he saw a beam of light stream from a house and hasten towards it .
The door be open and he enter , but pause when he behold an old man lie on a bench by the fire , while seat opposite him be a maiden combing out the lock of her golden hair with a comb of silver .
` Welcome , fair youth , ' say the old man , turn his head .
` Sit down and warm yourself , and tell me how fare the outer world .
It be long since I have see it . '
` All my news be that I be seek service , ' answered Ardan son of Gorla ; ' I have come from far since sunrise , and glad be I to see the ray of your lamp stream into the darkness . ' '
I need someone to herd my three dun cow , which be hornless , ' say the old man .
` If , for the space of a year , you can bring them back to me each even before the sun set , I will make you payment that will satisfy your soul . '
But here the girl look up and answer quickly : ` Ill will come of it if he listen to your offer . '
` Counsel unsought be worth nothing , ' reply , rudely , Ardan son of Gorla .
` It would be little indeed that I be fit for if I can not drive three cow out to pasture and keep them safe from the wolf that may come down from the mountain .
Therefore , good father , I will take service with you at daybreak , and ask no payment till the new year dawn . '
Next morning the bell of the deer be not hear amongst the fern before the maiden with the hair of gold have milk the cow , and lead them in front of the cottage where the old man and Ardan son of Gorla await them .
` Let them wander where they will , ' he say to his servant , ` and never seek to turn them from their way , for well they know the field of good pasture .
But take heed to follow always behind them , and suffer nothing that you see , and nought that you hear , to draw you into leave them .
Now go , and may wisdom go with you . '
As he cease speak he touch one of the cow on her forehead , and she step along the path , with the two others one on each side .
As he have be bid , behind them come Ardan son of Gorla , rejoice in his heart that work so easy have fall to his lot .
At the year 's end , think he , enough money would lie in his pocket to carry him into far country where his sister might be , and , in the meanwhile , someone might come past who could give him tidings of her .
Thus he speak to himself , when his eye fell on a golden cock and a silver hen run swiftly along the grass in front of him .
In a moment the word that the old man have utter vanish from his mind and he give chase .
They be so near that he could almost seize their tail , yet each time he felt sure he could catch them his finger close on the empty air .
At length he could run no more , and stop to breathe , while the cock and hen go on a before .
Then he remember the cow , and , somewhat frighten , turn back to seek them .
Luckily they have not stray far , and be quietly feed on the thick green grass .
Ardan son of Gorla be sit under a tree , when he behold a staff of gold and a staff of silver double themselves in strange way on the meadow in front of him , and start up he hasten towards them .
He follow them till he be tire , but he could not catch them , though they seem ever within his reach .
When at last he give up the quest his knee tremble beneath him for very weariness , and glad be he to see a tree grow close by lade with fruit of different sort , of which he eat greedily .
The sun be by now low in the heaven , and the cow leave off feeding , and turn their face home again , follow by Ardan son of Gorla .
At the door of their stable the maiden stood await them , and say nought to their herd , she sit down and begin to milk .
But it be not milk that flow into her pail ; instead it be fill with a thin stream of water , and a she rise up from the last cow the old man appear outside .
` Faithless one , you have betray your trust ! '
he say to Ardan son of Gorla .
` Not even for one day could you keep true !
Well , you shall have your reward at once , that others may take warn from you . '
And wave his wand he touch with it the chest of the youth , who become a pillar of stone .
Now Gorla of the Flocks and his wife be full of grief that they have lose a son as well a a daughter , for no tidings have come to them of Ardan their eldest bear .
At length , when two year and two day have pass since the maiden have lead her kid to fee on the mountain and have be see no more , Ruais , second son of Gorla , rise up one morning , and say : ` Time be long without my sister and Ardan my brother .
So I have vow to seek them wherever they may be . '
And his father answer : ` Better it have be if you have first ask my consent and that of your mother ; but a you have vow so must you do . '
Then he bid his wife make a cake , but instead she make two , and offer Ruais his choice , a she have do to Ardan .
Like Ardan , Ruais choose the large , unblessed cake , and set forth on his way , do always , though he know it not , that which Ardan have do ; so , needle be it to tell what befall him till he too stand , a pillar of stone , on the hill behind the cottage , so that all men might see the fate that await those who break their faith .
Another year and a day pass by , when Covan the Brown-haired , young son of Gorla of the Flocks , one morning spake to his parent , say : ` It be more than three year since my sister leave u .
My brother have also go , no one know whither , and of u four none remain but I . No , therefore , I long to seek them , and I pray you and my mother to place no hindrance in my way . '
And his father answer : ` Go , then , and take our bless with you . '
So the wife of Gorla of the Flocks bake two cake , one large and one small ; and Covan take the small one , and start on his quest .
In the wood he felt hungry , for he have walk far , and he sit down to eat .
Suddenly a voice behind him cry : ' A bit for me !
a bit for me ! '
And look round he behold the black raven of the wilderness .
` Yes , you shall have a bit , ' say Covan the Brown-haired ; and break off a piece he stretch it upwards to the raven , who eat it greedily .
Then Covan arose and go forward , till he saw the light from the cottage stream before him , and glad be he , for night be at hand .
` Maybe I shall find some work there , ' he think , ` and at least I shall gain money to help me in my search ; for who know how far my sister and my brother may have wander ? '
The door stand open and he enter , and the old man give him welcome , and the golden-haired maiden likewise .
As happen before , he be offer by the old man to herd his cow ; and , a she have do to his brother , the maiden counsel him to leave such work alone .
But , instead of answer rudely , like both Ardan and Ruais , he thank her , with courtesy , though he have no mind to heed her ; and he listen to the warning and word of his new master .
Next day he set forth at dawn with the dun cow in front of him , and follow patiently wherever they might lead him .
On the way he saw the gold cock and silver hen , which run even closer to him than they have do to his brother .
Sorely tempt , he long to give them chase ; but , remember in time that he have be bid to look neither to the right nor to the left , with a mighty effort he turn his eye away .
Then the gold and silver staff seem to spring from the earth before him , but this time also he overcame ; and though the fruit from the magic tree almost touch his mouth , he brush it aside and go steadily on .
That day the cow wander father than ever they have do before , and never stop till they have reach a moor where the heather be burn .
The fire be fierce , but the cow take no heed , and walk steadily through it , Covan the Brown-haired follow them .
Next they plunge into a foaming river , and Covan plunge in after them , though the water come high above his waist .
On the other side of the river lay a wide plain , and here the cow lay down , while Covan look about him .
Near him be a house built of yellow stone , and from it come sweet song , and Covan listen , and his heart grow light within him .
While he be thus wait there run up to him a youth , scarcely able to speak so swiftly have he speed ; and he cry aloud : ` Hasten , hasten , Covan the Brown-haired , for your cow be in the corn , and you must drive them out ! '
` Nay , ' say Covan smiling , ` it have be easier for you to have drive them out than to come here to tell me . '
And he go on listen to the music .
Very soon the same youth return and cry with pant breath : ` Out upon you , Covan son of Gorla , that you stand there agape .
For our dog be chase your cow , and you must drive them off ! '
` Nay , then , ' answered Covan a before , ` it have be easier for you to call off your dog than to come here to tell me . '
And he stay where he be till the music cease .
Then he turn to look for the cow , and find them all lie in the place where he have leave them ; but when they saw Covan they rise up and walked homewards , take a different path to that they have tread in the morning .
This time they pass over a plain so bare that a pin could not have lain there unnoticed , yet Covan beheld with surprise a foal and it mother feeding there , both as fat a if they have pasture on the rich grass .
Further on they cross another plain , where the grass be thick and green , but on it be feed a foal and it mother , so lean that you could have count their rib .
And far again the path lead them by the shore of a lake whereon be float two boat ; one full of gay and happy youth , journey to the land of the Sun , and another with grim shape clothe in black , travel to the land of Night .
` What can these thing mean ? '
say Covan to himself , a he follow his cow .
Darkness now fell , the wind howl , and torrent of rain pour upon them .
Covan know not how far they might yet have to go , or indeed if they be on the right road .
He could not even see his cow , and his heart sank l , after all , he should have fail to bring them safely back .
What be he to do ?
He wait thus , for he could go neither forward nor backwards , till he felt a great friendly paw lay on his shoulder .
` My cave be just here , ' say the Dog of Maol-mor , of whom Covan son of Gorla have hear much .
` Spend the night here , and you shall be feed on the flesh of lamb , and shall lay aside three-thirds of thy weariness . '
And Covan enter , and sup , and slept , and in the morning rise up a new man .
` Farewell , Covan , ' say the Dog of Maol-mor .
` May success go with you , for you take what I have to give and do not mock me .
So , when danger be your companion , wish for me , and I will not fail you . '
At these word the Dog of Maol-mor disappear into the forest , and Covan go to seek his cow , which be stand in the hollow where the darkness have come upon them .
At the sight of Covan the Brown-haired they walk onwards , Covan follow ever behind them , and look neither to the right nor to the left .
All that day they walk , and when night fell they be in a barren plain , with only rock for shelter .
` We must rest here as best we can , ' speak Covan to the cow .
And they bow their head and lay down in the place where they stand .
Then come the black raven of Corri-nan-creag , whose eye never close , and whose wing never tire ; and he flutter before the face of Covan and tell him that he know of a cranny in the rock where there be food in plenty , and soft moss for a bed .
` Go with me thither , ' he say to Covan , ` and you shall lay aside three-thirds of your weariness , and depart in the morning refresh , ' and Covan listen thankfully to his word , and at dawn he rise up to seek his cow .
` Farewell ! '
cry the black raven .
` You trust me , and take all I have to offer in return for the food you once give me .
So if in time to come you need a friend , wish for me , and I will not fail you . '
As before , the cow be stand in the spot where he have leave them , ready to set out .
All that day they walk , on and on , and on , Covan son of Gorla walk behind them , till night fell while they be on the bank of a river .
` We can go no far , ' spake Covan to the cow .
And they begin to eat the grass by the side of the stream , while Covan listen to them and long for some supper also , for they have travel far , and his limb be weak under him .
Then there be a swish of water at his foot , and out peep the head of the famous otter Doran-donn of the stream .
` Trust to me and I will find you warmth and shelter , ' say Doran-donn ; ` and for food fish in plenty . '
And Covan go with him thankfully , and ate and rest , and lay aside three-thirds of his weariness .
At sunrise he leave his bed of dried sea-weed , which have float up with the tide , and with a grateful heart bade farewell to Doran-donn .
` Because you trust me and take what I have to offer , you have make me your friend , Covan , ' say Doran-donn .
` And if you should be in danger , and need help from one who can swim a river or dive beneath a wave , call to me and I will come to you . '
Then he plunge into the stream , and be see no more .
The cow be stand ready in the place where Covan have leave them , and they journey on all that day , till , when night fell , they reach the cottage .
Joyful indeed be the old man a the cow go into their stable , and he behold the rich milk that flow into the pail of the golden-haired maiden with the silver comb .
` You have do well indeed , ' he say to Covan son of Gorla .
` And now , what would you have a a reward ? ' '
I want nothing for myself , ' answer Covan the Brown-haired ; ` but I ask you to give me back my brother and my sister who have be lose to u for three year past .
You be wise and know the lore of fairy and of witch ; tell me where I can find them , and what I must do to bring them to life again . '
The old man look grave at the word of Covan .
` Yes , truly I know where they be , ' answer he , ` and I say not that they may not be bring to life again .
But the peril be great -- too great for you to overcome . '
` Tell me what they be , ' say Covan again , ` and I shall know good if I may overcome them . '
` Listen , then , and judge .
In the mountain yonder there dwell a roe , white of foot , with horn that branch like the antler of a deer .
On the lake that lead to the land of the Sun float a duck whose body be green and whose neck be of gold .
In the pool of Corri-Bui swim a salmon with a skin that shin like silver , and whose gill be red -- bring them all to me , and then you shall know where dwell your brother and your sister ! '
` To-morrow at cock-crow I will begone ! '
answer Covan .
The way to the mountain lay straight before him , and when he have climb high he catch sight of the roe with the white foot and the spotted side , on the peak in front .
Full of hope he set out in pursuit of her , but by the time he have reach that peak she have leave it and be to be see on another .
And so it always happen , and Covan 's courage have well-nigh fail him , when the thought of the Dog of Maol-mor dart into his mind .
` Oh , that he be here ! '
he cry .
And look up he saw him .
` Why do you summon me ? '
ask the Dog of Maol-mor .
And when Covan have tell him of his trouble , and how the roe always lead him far and far , the Dog only answer : ` Fear nothing ; I will soon catch her for you . '
And in a short while he lay the roe unhurt at Covan 's foot .
` What will you wish me to do with her ? '
say the Dog .
And Covan answer : ` The old man bid me bring her , and the duck with the golden neck , and the salmon with the silver side , to his cottage ; if I shall catch them , I know not .
But carry you the roe to the back of the cottage , and tether her so that she can not escape . '
` It shall be do , ' say the Dog of Maol-mor .
Then Covan speed to the lake which lead to the land of the Sun , where the duck with the green body and the golden neck be swim among the water-lilies .
` Surely I can catch him , good swimmer a I be , ' to himself .
But , if he could swim well , the duck could swim good , and at length his strength fail him , and he be force to seek the land .
` Oh that the black raven be here to help me ! '
he think to himself .
And in a moment the black raven be perch on his shoulder .
` How can I help you ? '
ask the raven .
And Covan answer : ` Catch me the green duck that float on the water . '
And the raven fly with his strong wing and pick him up in his strong beak , and in another moment the bird be lay at the foot of Covan .
This time it be easy for the young man to carry his prize , and after give thanks to the raven for his aid , he go on to the river .
In the deep dark pool of which the old man have speak the silver-sided salmon be lie under a rock .
` Surely I , good fisher a I be , can catch him , ' say Covan son of Gorla .
And cut a slender pole from a bush , he fasten a line to the end of it .
But cast with what skill he might , it avail nothing , for the salmon would not even look at the bait . '
I be beat at last , unless the Doran-donn can deliver me , ' he cry .
And a he speak there be a swish of the water , and the face of the Doran-donn look up at him . '
O catch me , I pray you , that salmon under the rock ! '
say Covan son of Gorla .
And the Doran-donn dive , and lay hold of the salmon by his tail , bore it back to the place where Covan be stand .
` The roe , and the duck , and the salmon be here , ' say Covan to the old man , when he reach the cottage .
And the old man smile on him and bid him eat and drink , and after he hunger no more , he would speak with him .
And this be what the old man say : ` You begin well , my son , so thing have go well with you .
You set store by your mother 's blessing , therefore you have be blest .
You give food to the raven when it hunger , you be true to the promise you have make to me , and do not suffer yourself to be turn aside by vain show .
You be skilled to perceive that the boy who tempt you to leave the temple be a teller of false tale , and take with a grateful heart what the poor have to offer you .
Last of all , difficulty give you courage , instead of lending you despair .
And now , a to your reward , you shall in truth take your sister home with you , and your brother I will restore to life ; but idle and unfaithful a they be their lot be to wander for ever .
And so farewell , and may wisdom be with you . '
` First tell me your name ? '
ask Covan softly . '
I be the Spirit of Age , ' say the old man .
The Princess Bella-Flor -LSB- Taken from a Celtic Story .
Translated by Doctor Macleod Clarke . -RSB-
Once upon a time there live a man who have two son .
When they grow up the elder go to seek his fortune in a far country , and for many year no one heard anything about him .
Meanwhile the young son stay at home with his father , who die at last in a good old age , leave great rich behind him .
For some time the son who stay at home spend his father 's wealth freely , believe that he alone remain to enjoy it .
But , one day , a he be come down stairs , he be surprised to see a stranger enter the hall , look about a if the house belong to him .
` Have you forget me ? '
ask the man . '
I ca n't forget a person I have never know , ' be the rude answer . '
I be your brother , ' reply the stranger , ` and I have return home without the money I hop to have make .
And , what be bad , they tell me in the village that my father be dead .
I would have count my lose gold a nothing if I could have see him once more . '
` He die six month ago , ' say the rich brother , ` and he leave you , a your portion , the old wooden chest that stand in the loft .
You have good go there and look for it ; I have no more time to waste . '
And he go his way .
So the wanderer turn his step to the loft , which be at the top of the storehouse , and there he find the wooden chest , so old that it look a if it be drop to piece .
` What use be this old thing to me ? '
he say to himself .
` Oh , well , it will serve to light a fire at which I can warm myself ; so thing might be bad after all . '
Placing the chest on his back , the man , whose name be Jose , set out for his inn , and , borrow a hatchet , begin to chop up the box .
In do so he discover a secret drawer , and in it lay a paper .
He open the paper , not know what it might contain , and be astonish to find that it be the acknowledgment of a large debt that be owe to his father .
Putting the precious writing in his pocket , he hastily inquire of the landlord where he could find the man whose name be write inside , and he run out at once in search of him .
The debtor prove to be an old miser , who live at the other end of the village .
He have hop for many month that the paper he have write have be lose or destroy , and , indeed , when he saw it , be very unwilling to pay what he owe .
However , the stranger threaten to drag him before the king , and when the miser saw that there be no help for it he count out the coin one by one .
The stranger pick them up and put them in his pocket , and go back to his inn feeling that he be now a rich man .
A few week after this he be walk through the street of the near town , when he meet a poor woman cry bitterly .
He stop and ask her what be the matter , and she answer between her sob that her husband be die , and , to make matter bad , a creditor whom he could not pay be anxious to have him take to prison .
` Comfort yourself , ' say the stranger kindly ; ` they shall neither send your husband to prison nor sell your good .
I will not only pay his debt but , if he die , the cost of his burial also .
And now go home , and nurse him as well a you can . '
And so she do ; but , in spite of her care , the husband die , and be bury by the stranger .
But everything cost more than he expect , and when all be pay he find that only three gold piece be leave .
` What be I to do now ? '
say he to himself . '
I think I have well go to court , and enter into the service of the king . '
At first he be only a servant , who carry the king the water for his bath , and saw that his bed be make in a particular fashion .
But he do his duty so well that his master soon take notice of him , and in a short time he rise to be a gentleman of the bedchamber .
Now , when this happen the young brother have spend all the money he have inherit , and do not know how to make any for himself .
He then bethink him of the king 's favourite , and go whine to the palace to beg that his brother , whom he have so ill-used , would give him his protection , and find him a place .
The elder , who be always ready to help everyone spoke to the king on his behalf , and the next day the young man take up be work at court .
Unfortunately , the new-comer be by nature spiteful and envious , and could not bear anyone to have good luck than himself .
By dint of spy through keyhole and listen at door , he learn that the king , old and ugly though he be , have fall in love with the Princess Bella-Flor , who would have nothing to say to him , and have hide herself in some mountain castle , no one knew where .
` That will do nicely , ' think the scoundrel , rub his hand .
` It will be quite easy to get the king to send my brother in search of her , and if he return without find her , his head will be the forfeit .
Either way , he will be out of MY path . '
So he go at once to the Lord High Chamberlain and crave an audience of the king , to whom he declare he wish to tell some news of the high importance .
The king admit him into the presence chamber without delay , and bid him state what he have to say , and to be quick about it .
` Oh , sire !
the Princess Bella-Flor -- ' answer the man , and then stop a if afraid .
` What of the Princess Bella-Flor ? '
ask the king impatiently . '
I have hear -- it be whisper at court -- that your majesty desire to know where she lie in hide . ' '
I would give half my kingdom to the man who will bring her to me , ' cry the king , eagerly .
` Speak on , knave ; have a bird of the air reveal to you the secret ? '
` It be not I , but my brother , who know , ' reply the traitor ; ` if your majesty would ask him -- ' But before the word be out of his mouth the king have strike a blow with his sceptre on a golden plate that hung on the wall .
` Order Jose to appear before me instantly , ' he shout to the servant who run to obey his order , so great be the noise his majesty have make ; and when Jose enter the hall , wonder what in the world could be the matter , the king be nearly dumb from rage and excitement .
` Bring me the Princess Bella-Flor this moment , ' stammer he , ` for if you return without her I will have you drown ! '
And without another word he leave the hall , leave Jose star with surprise and horror .
` How can I find the Princess Bella-Flor when I have never even see her ? '
thought he .
` But it be no use stay here , for I shall only be put to death . '
And he walk slowly to the stable to choose himself a horse .
There be row upon row of fine beast with their name write in gold above their stall , and Jose be look uncertainly from one to the other , wonder which he should choose , when an old white horse turn it head and sign to him to approach .
` Take me , ' it say in a gentle whisper , ` and all will go well . '
Jose still felt so bewilder with the mission that the king have give him that he forget to be astonish at hear a horse talk .
Mechanically he lay his hand on the bridle and lead the white horse out of the stable .
He be about to mount on his back , when the animal spoke again : ` Pick up those three loaf of bread which you see there , and put them in your pocket . '
Jose do a he be tell , and be in a great hurry to get away , ask no question , but swing himself into the saddle .
They ride far without meet any adventure , but at length they come to an ant-hill , and the horse stop .
` Crumble those three loaf for the ant , ' he say .
But Jose hesitate .
` Why , we may want them ourselves ! '
answer he .
` Never mind that ; give them to the ant all the same .
Do not lose a chance of help others . '
And when the loaf lay in crumb on the road , the horse gallop on .
By-and-by they enter a rocky pas between two mountain , and here they saw an eagle which have be catch in a hunter 's net .
` Get down and cut the mesh of the net , and set the poor bird free , ' say the horse .
` But it will take so long , ' object Jose , ` and we may miss the princess . '
` Never mind that ; do not lose a chance of help others , ' answer the horse .
And when the mesh be cut , and the eagle be free , the horse gallop on .
The have ride many mile , and at last they come to a river , where they behold a little fish lie gasp on the sand , and the horse say : ` Do you see that little fish ?
It will die if you do not put it back in the water . '
` But , really , we shall never find the Princess Bella-Flor if we waste our time like this ! '
cry Jose .
` We never waste time when we be help others , ' answer the horse .
And soon the little fish be swim happily away .
A little while after they reach a castle , which be build in the middle of a very thick wood , and right in front be the Princess Bella-Flor feed her hen .
` Now listen , ' say the horse . '
I be go to give all sort of little hop and skip , which will amuse the Princess Bella-Flor .
Then she will tell you that she would like to ride a little way , and you must help her to mount .
When she be seat I shall begin to neigh and kick , and you must say that I have never carry a woman before , and that you have good get up behind so a to be able to manage me .
Once on my back we will go like the wind to the king 's palace . '
Jose do exactly a the horse tell him , and everything fell out a the animal prophesy ; so that it be not until they be gallop breathlessly towards the palace that the princess know that she be take captive .
She say nothing , however , but quietly open her apron which contain the bran for the chicken , and in a moment it lay scatter on the ground .
` Oh , I have let fall my bran ! '
cry she ; ` please get down and pick it up for me . '
But Jose only answer : ` We shall find plenty of bran where we be go . '
And the horse gallop on .
They be now pass through a forest , and the princess take out her handkerchief and throw it upwards , so that it stick in one of the topmost branch of a tree .
` Dear me ; how stupid !
I have let my handkerchief blow away , ' say she .
` Will you climb up and get it for me ? '
But Jose answer : ` We shall find plenty of handkerchief where we be go . '
And the horse gallop on .
After the wood they reach a river , and the princess slip a ring off her finger and let it roll into the water .
` How careless of me , ' gasp she , begin to sob . '
I have lose my favourite ring ; DO stop for a moment and look if you can see it . '
But Jose answer : ` You will find plenty of ring where you be go . '
And the horse gallop on .
At last they enter the palace gate , and the king 's heart bound with joy at behold his beloved Princess Bella-Flor .
But the princess brush him aside a if he have be a fly , and lock herself into the near room , which she would not open for all his entreaty .
` Bring me the three thing I lose on the way , and perhaps I may think about it , ' be all she would say .
And , in despair , the king be drive to take counsel of Jose .
` There be no remedy that I can see , ' say his majesty , ` but that you , who know where they be , should go and bring them back .
And if you return without them I will have you drown . '
Poor Jose be much trouble at these word .
He think that he have do all that be require of him , and that his life be safe .
However , he bow low , and go out to consult his friend the horse .
` Do not vex yourself , ' say the horse , when he have hear the story ; ` jump up , and we will go and look for the thing . '
And Jose mount at once .
They ride on till they come to the ant-hill , and then the horse ask : ` Would you like to have the bran ? '
` What be the use of like ? '
answer Jose .
` Well , call the ant , and tell them to fetch it for you ; and , if some of it have be scatter by the wind , to bring in it stead the grain that be in the cake you give them . '
Jose listen in surprise .
He do not much believe in the horse 's plan ; but he could not think of anything well , so he call to the ant , and bid them collect the bran as fast a they could .
Then he saw under a tree and wait , while his horse crop the green turf .
` Look there ! '
say the animal , suddenly raise it head ; and Jose look behind him and saw a little mountain of bran , which he put into a bag that be hang over his saddle .
` Good deed bear fruit sooner or later , ' observe the horse ; ` but mount again , a we have far to go . '

cry he ; ` why I should need Jacob 's ladder ! '

ask Jose .

Well pleased with all he have do , Jose return to the palace ; but when the king take the precious object to Bella-Flor , she declare that she would never open her door till the bandit who have carry her off have be fry in oil . '

` Do not be frighten , ' say the horse .
` Get on my back , and I will gallop till my whole body be wet with perspiration , then rub it all over your skin , and no matter how hot the oil may be you will never feel it . '
Jose do not ask any more question , but do a the horse bid him ; and men wonder at his cheerful face a they lower him into the caldron of boil oil .
He be leave there till Bella-Flor cry that he must be cook enough .
Then out come a youth so young and handsome , that everyone fell in love with him , and Bella-Flor most of all .
As for the old king , he saw that he have lose the game ; and in despair he fling himself into the caldron , and be fry instead of Jose .
Then Jose be proclaim king , on condition that he marry Bella-Flor which he promise to do the next day .
But first he go to the stable and seek out the horse , and say to him : ` It be to you that I owe my life and my crown .
Why have you do all this for me ? '
And the horse answer : ' I be the soul of that unhappy man for whom you spend all your fortune .
And when I saw you in danger of death I beg that I might help you , a you have help me .
For , a I tell you , Good deed bear their own fruit ! '
The Bird of Truth -LSB- From Cuentos , Oraciones , y Adivinas , por Fernan Caballero . -RSB-
Once upon a time there live a poor fisher who build a hut on the bank of a stream which , shun the glare of the sun and the noise of the town , flow quietly past tree and under bush , listen to the song of the bird overhead .
One day , when the fisherman have go out as usual to cast his net , he saw borne towards him on the current a cradle of crystal .
Slipping his net quickly beneath it he draw it out and lift the silk coverlet .
Inside , lie on a soft bed of cotton , be two baby , a boy and a girl , who open their eye and smile at him .
The man be fill with pity at the sight , and throw down his line he take the cradle and the baby home to his wife .
The good woman fling up her hand in despair when she behold the content of the cradle .
` Are not eight child enough , ' she cry , ` without bring u two more ?
How do you think we can fee them ? '
` You would not have have me leave them to die of hunger , ' answer he , ` or be swallow up by the wave of the sea ?
What be enough for eight be also enough for ten . '
The wife say no more ; and in truth her heart yearn over the little creature .
Somehow or other food be never lack in the hut , and the child grow up and be so good and gentle that , in time , their foster-parent love them as well or good than their own , who be quarrelsome and envious .
It do not take the orphan long to notice that the boy do not like them , and be always play trick on them , so they use to go away by themselves and spend whole hour by the bank of the river .
Here they would take out the bit of bread they have save from their breakfast and crumble them for the bird .
In return , the bird teach them many thing : how to get up early in the morning , how to sing , and how to talk their language , which very few people know .
But though the little orphan do their best to avoid quarrel with their foster-brother , it be very difficult always to keep the peace .
Matters get bad and bad till , one morning , the eldest boy say to the twin : ` It be all very well for you to pretend that you have such good manner , and be so much good than we , but we have at least a father and mother , while you have only get the river , like the toad and the frog . '
The poor child do not answer the insult ; but it make them very unhappy .
And they tell each other in whisper that they could not stay there any long , but must go into the world and seek their fortune .
So next day they arise as early a the bird and stole downstairs without anybody hear them .
One window be open , and they creep softly out and run to the side of the river .
Then , feel a if they have find a friend , they walk along it bank , hop that by-and-by they should meet some one to take care of them .
The whole of that day they go steadily on without see a living creature , till , in the evening , weary and footsore , they saw before them a small hut .
This raise their spirit for a moment ; but the door be shut , and the hut seem empty , and so great be their disappointment that they almost cry .
However , the boy fight down his tear , and say cheerfully : ` Well , at any rate here be a bench where we can sit down , and when we be rest we will think what be best to do next . '
Then they sit down , and for some time they be too tired even to notice anything ; but by-and-by they saw that under the tile of the roof a number of swallow be sit , chatter merrily to each other .
Of course the swallow have no idea that the child understand their language , or they would not have talk so freely ; but , a it be , they say whatever come into their head .
` Good evening , my fine city madam , ' remark a swallow , whose manner be rather rough and countryfied to another who look particularly distinguish .
` Happy , indeed , be the eye that behold you !
Only think of your have return to your long-forgotten country friend , after you have live for year in a palace ! ' '
I have inherit this nest from my parent , ' reply the other , ` and a they leave it to me I certainly shall make it my home .
But , ' she add politely , ' I hope that you and all your family be well ? '
` Very well indeed , I be glad to say .
But my poor daughter have , a short time ago , such bad inflammation in her eye that she would have go blind have I not be able to find the magic herb , which cure her at once . '
` And how be the nightingale singing ?
Does the lark soar as high a ever ?
And do the linnet dress herself a smartly ? '
But here the country swallow draw herself up . '
I never talk gossip , ' she say severely .
` Our people , who be once so innocent and well-behaved , have be corrupt by the bad example of men .
It be a thousand pity . '
` What !
innocence and good behaviour be not to be meet with among bird , nor in the country !
My dear friend , what be you say ? '
` The truth and nothing more .
Imagine , when we return here , we meet some linnet who , just a the spring and the flower and the long day have come , be set out for the north and the cold ?
Out of pure compassion we try to persuade them to give up this folly ; but they only reply with the utmost insolence . '
` How shocking ! '
exclaim the city swallow .
` Yes , it be .
And bad than that , the crested lark , that be formerly so timid and shy , be now no good than a thief , and steal maize and corn whenever she can find them . ' '
I be astonish at what you say . '
` You will be more astonished when I tell you that on my arrival here for the summer I find my nest occupy by a shameless sparrow !
`` This be my nest , '' I say .
`` Yours ? ''
he answer , with a rude laugh .
`` Yes , mine ; my ancestor be bear here , and my son will be bear here also . ''
And at that my husband set upon him and throw him out of the nest .
I be sure nothing of this sort ever happen in a town . '
` Not exactly , perhaps .
But I have see a great deal -- if you only know ! '
` Oh !
do tell u !
do tell u ! '
cry they all .
And when they have settle themselves comfortably , the city swallow begin : ` You must know , then that our king fell in love with the young daughter of a tailor , who be as good and gentle a she be beautiful .
His noble hop that he would have choose a queen from one of their daughter , and try to prevent the marriage ; but the king would not listen to them , and it take place .
Not many month later a war break out , and the king ride away at the head of his army , while the queen remain behind , very unhappy at the separation .
When peace be make , and the king return , he be tell that his wife have have two baby in his absence , but that both be dead ; that she herself have go out of her mind and be oblige to be shut up in a tower in the mountain , where , in time , the fresh air might cure her . '
` And be this not true ? '
ask the swallow eagerly .
` Of course not , ' answer the city lady , with some contempt for their stupidity .
` The child be alive at that very moment in the gardener 's cottage ; but at night the chamberlain come down and put them in a cradle of crystal , which he carry to the river .
` For a whole day they float safely , for though the stream be deep it be very still , and the child take no harm .
In the morning -- so I be tell by my friend the kingfisher -- they be rescue by a fisherman who live near the river bank . '

say the eye of one to the eye of the other .

` That be indeed good fortune ! '

`` And where can this bird be find ? ''
I ask . '
`` It be shut up in a castle guard by a fierce giant , who only sleep one quarter of an hour out of the whole twenty-four , '' reply the cuckoo .

inquire the country swallow , who , like all the rest , and the child most of all , have be listen with deep attention .

'

ask the country swallow .

So that even if the prince do succeed in get there , he could never understand what the owl say .
But , look , the sun be sink to his nest in the depth of the sea , and I must go to mine .
Good-night , friends , good-night ! '
Then the swallow fly away , and the child , who have forget both hunger and weariness in the joy of this strange news , rise up and follow in the direction of her flight .
After two hour ' walking , they arrive at a large city , which they felt sure must be the capital of their father 's kingdom .
Seeing a good-natured look woman stand at the door of a house , they ask her if she would give them a night 's lodging , and she be so pleased with their pretty face and nice manner that she welcome them warmly .

This so delighted her that she beg the child to stay with her altogether , and the boy answer that he would leave his sister with her gladly , but that he himself have serious business on hand and must not linger in pursuit of it .
So he bid them farewell and set out .
For three day he wander by the most out-of-the-way path , but no sign of a tower be to be see anywhere .
On the fourth morning it be just the same , and , fill with despair , he fling himself on the ground under a tree and hide his face in his hand .
In a little while he hear a rustling over his head , and look up , he saw a turtle dove watch him with her bright eye .
` Oh dove ! '
cry the boy , address the bird in her own language , ` Oh dove !
tell me , I pray you , where be the castle of Come-and-never-go ? '
` Poor child , ' answer the dove , ` who have send you on such a useless quest ? '
` My good or evil fortune , ' reply the boy , ' I know not which . '
` To get there , ' say the dove , ` you must follow the wind , which to-day be blow towards the castle . '
The boy thank her , and follow the wind , fear all the time that it might change it direction and lead him astray .
But the wind seem to feel pity for him and blow steadily on .
With each step the country become more and more dreary , but at nightfall the child could see behind the dark and bare rock something darker still .
This be the tower in which dwell the witch ; and seize the knocker he give three loud knock , which be echo in the hollow of the rock around .

cry she .
` Be quick and tell me what you want , or it will be the bad for you . '

` Very good , ' reply the witch , with something that she mean for a smile , ` but to-day it be late .
To-morrow you shall go .
Now enter , and you shall sleep with my lizard . ' '
I can not stay , ' say he . '
I must go back at once , so a to reach the road from which I start before day dawn . '
` If I tell you , will you promise me that you will bring me this jar full of the many-coloured water from the spring in the court-yard of the castle ? '
ask she .
` If you fail to keep your word I will change you into a lizard for ever . ' '
I promise , ' answer the boy .
Then the old woman call to a very thin dog , and say to him : ` Conduct this pig of a child to the castle of Come-and-never-go , and take care that you warn my friend of his arrival . '

cross ! '
answer a voice .

Afterwards , go into the aviary opposite the great door , but be careful not to touch any of the bright-plumaged bird contain in it , which will cry to you , each one , that he be the Bird of Truth .
Choose only a small white bird that be hide in a corner , which the others try incessantly to kill , not know that it can not die .
And , be quick !
-- for at this very moment the giant have fall asleep , and you have only a quarter of an hour to do everything . '

He pass by the many-coloured water without cast a glance at it , and fill the jar from the fountain whose water be clear and pure .
He next hasten to the aviary , and be almost deafen by the clamour that rise a he shut the door behind him .
Voices of peacock , voice of raven , voice of magpie , each claiming to be the Bird of Truth .
With steadfast face the boy walk by them all , to the corner , where , hem in by a hand of fierce crow , be the small white bird he seek .
Putting her safely in his breast , he pass out , follow by the scream of the bird of Bad Faith which he leave behind him .
Once outside , he run without stop to the witch 's tower , and hand to the old woman the jar she have give him .
` Become a parrot ! '
cry she , fling the water over him .
But instead of lose his shape , a so many have do before , he only grow ten time handsomer ; for the water be enchant for good and not ill .

When the witch saw what be happen , she take a broomstick and fly away .

They get ready weapon that be sharpen , and weapon that be poison ; they send for eagle and falcon to hunt her down , and construct cage and box in which to shut her up if they be not able to kill her .
They declare that her white plumage be really put on to hide her black feather -- in fact there be nothing they do not do in order to prevent the king from see the bird or from pay attention to her word if he do .
As often happen in these case , the courtier bring about that which they fear .
They talk so much about the Bird of Truth that at last the king heard of it , and express a wish to see her .
The more difficulty that be put in his way the strong grow his desire , and in the end the king publish a proclamation that whoever find the Bird of Truth should bring her to him without delay .
As soon a he saw this proclamation the boy call his sister , and they hasten to the palace .
The bird be button inside his tunic , but , a might have be expect , the courtier bar the way , and tell the child that he could not enter .

` Who be you ? '

` If it please your majesty , the Bird of Truth will explain that herself , ' answer the boy .
