They all return in state to the city , where great rejoicing be hold .
The wicked courtier have their head cut off , and all their property be take away .
As for the good old couple , they be give rich and honour , and be love and cherish to the end of their life .
The Mink and the Wolf -LSB- From Cuentos , Oraciones y Adivinas , por Fernan Caballero . -RSB-
In a big forest in the north of America live a quantity of wild animal of all sort .
They be always very polite when they meet ; but , in spite of that , they keep a close watch one upon the other , a each be afraid of be kill and eat by somebody else .
But their manner be so good that no one would ever have guess that .
One day a smart young wolf go out to hunt , promise his grandfather and grandmother that he would be sure to be back before bedtime .
He trot along quite happily through the forest till he come to a favourite place of his , just where the river run into the sea .
There , just a he have hop , he saw the chief mink fishing in a canoe . '
I want to fish too , ' cry the wolf .
But the mink say nothing and pretend not to hear . '
I wish you would take me into your boat ! '
shout the wolf , loud than before , and he continue to beseech the mink so long that at last he grow tire of it , and paddle to the shore close enough for the wolf to jump in .
` Sit down quietly at that end or we shall be upset , ' say the mink ; ` and if you care about sea-urchins ' egg , you will find plenty in that basket .
But be sure you eat only the white one , for the red one would kill you . '
So the wolf , who be always hungry , begin to eat the egg greedily ; and when he have finish he tell the mink he think he would have a nap .
` Well , then , stretch yourself out , and rest your head on that piece of wood , ' say the mink .
And the wolf do a he be bid , and be soon fast asleep .
Then the mink creep up to him and stab him to the heart with his knife , and he die without move .
After that he land on the beach , skin the wolf , and take the skin to his cottage , he hang it up before the fire to dry .
Not many day later the wolf 's grandmother , who , with the help of her relation , have be search for him everywhere , enter the cottage to buy some sea-urchins ' egg , and saw the skin , which she at once guess to be that of her grandson . '
I know he be dead -- I know it !
I know it ! '
she cry , weep bitterly , till the mink tell her rudely that if she want to make so much noise she have well do it outside a he like to be quiet .
So , half-blinded by her tear , the old woman go home the way she have come , and run in at the door , she fling herself down in front of the fire .
` What be you cry for ? '
ask the old wolf and some friend who have be spend the afternoon with him . '
I shall never see my grandson any more ! '
answer she .
` Mink have kill him , oh !
oh ! '
And put her head down , she begin to weep as loudly a ever .
` There !
there ! '
say her husband , lay his paw on her shoulder .
` Be comfort ; if he IS dead , we will avenge him . '
And call to the others they proceed to talk over the best plan .
It take them a long time to make up their mind , a one wolf propose one thing and one another ; but at last it be agree that the old wolf should give a great feast in his house , and that the mink should be invite to the party .
And in order that no time should be lose it be far agree that each wolf should bear the invitation to the guest that live near to him .
Now the wolf think they be very cunning , but the mink be more cunning still ; and though he send a message by a white hare , that be go that way , say he should be delight to be present , he determine that he would take his precaution .
So he go to a mouse who have often do him a good turn , and greet her with his best bow . '
I have a favour to ask of you , friend mouse , ' say he , ` and if you will grant it I will carry you on my back every night for a week to the patch of maize right up the hill . '
` The favour be mine , ' answer the mouse .
` Tell me what it be that I can have the honour of do for you . '
` Oh , something quite easy , ' reply the mink . '
I only want you -- between to-day and the next full moon -- to gnaw through the bow and paddle of the wolf people , so that directly they use them they will break .
But of course you must manage it so that they notice nothing . '
` Of course , ' answer the mouse , ` nothing be easy ; but a the full moon be to-morrow night , and there be not much time , I have well begin at once . '
Then the mink thank her , and go his way ; but before he have go far he come back again .
` Perhaps , while you be about the wolf 's house seeing after the bow , it would do no harm if you be to make that knot-hole in the wall a little big , ' say he .
` Not large enough to draw attention , of course ; but it might come in handy . '
And with another nod he leave her .
The next evening the mink wash and brush himself carefully and set out for the feast .
He smile to himself a he look at the dusty track , and perceive that though the mark of wolf ' foot be many , not a single guest be to be see anywhere .
He know very well what that meant ; but he have take his precaution and be not afraid .
The house door stand open , but through a crack the mink could see the wolf crowd in the corner behind it .
However , he enter boldly , and as soon a he be fairly inside the door be shut with a bang , and the whole herd sprang at him , with their red tongue hang out of their mouth .
Quick a they be they be too late , for the mink be already through the knot-hole and race for his canoe .
The knot-hole be too small for the wolf , and there be so many of them in the hut that it be some time before they could get the door open .
Then they seize the bow and arrow which be hang on the wall and , once outside , aim at the fly mink ; but a they pull the bow break in their paw , so they throw them away , and bound to the shore , with all their speed , to the place where their canoe be draw up on the beach .
Now , although the mink could not run as fast a the wolf , he have a good start , and be already afloat when the swift among them throw themselves into the near canoe .
They push off , but a they dip the paddle into the water , they snap a the bow have do , and be quite useless . '
I know where there be some new one , ' cry a young fellow , leap on shore and rush to a little cave at the back of the beach .
And the mink 's heart smite him when he hear , for he have not know of this secret store .
After a long chase the wolf manage to surround their prey , and the mink , see it be no good resist any more , give himself up .
Some of the elder wolf bring out some cedar band , which they always carry wound round their body , but the mink laugh scornfully at the sight of them .
` Why I could snap those in a moment , ' say he ; ` if you want to make sure that I can not escape , good take a line of kelp and bind me with that . '
` You be right , ' answer the grandfather ; ` your wisdom be great than ours . '
And he bid his servant gather enough kelp from the rock to make a line , a they have bring none with them .
` While the line be be make you might as well let me have one last dance , ' remark the mink .
And the wolf reply : ` Very good , you may have your dance ; perhaps it may amuse u as well a you . '
So they bring two canoe and place them one beside the other .
The mink stand up on his hind leg and begin to dance , first in one canoe and then in the other ; and so graceful be he , that the wolf forget they be go to put him to death , and howl with pleasure .
` Pull the canoe a little apart ; they be too close for this new dance , ' he say , pause for a moment .
And the wolf separate them while he give a series of little spring , sometime pirouette while he stand with one foot on the prow of both .
` Now near , now far apart , ' he would cry a the dance go on .
` No !
far still . '
And spring into the air , amidst howl of applause , he come down head-foremost , and dive to the bottom .
And through the wolf , whose howl have now change into those of rage , seek him everywhere , they never find him , for he hide behind a rock till they be out of sight , and then make his home in another forest .
Adventures of an Indian Brave -LSB- From the Journal of the Anthropological Institute . -RSB-
A long , long way off , right away in the west of America , there once live an old man who have one son .
The country round be cover with forest , in which dwell all kind of wild beast , and the young man and his companion use to spend whole day in hunt them , and he be the fine hunter of all the tribe .
One morning , when winter be come on , the youth and his companion set off a usual to bring back some of the mountain goat and deer to be salt down , a he be afraid of a snow-storm ; and if the wind blew and the snow drift the forest might be impassable for some week .
The old man and the wife , however , would not go out , but remain in the wigwam making bow and arrow .
It soon grow so cold in the forest that at last one of the men declare they could walk no more , unless they could manage to warm themselves .
` That be easily do , ' say the leader , give a kick to a large tree .
Flames break out in the trunk , and before it have burn up they be as hot a if it have be summer .
Then they start off to the place where the goat and deer be to be find in the great number , and soon have kill as many a they want .
But the leader kill most , a he be the best shot .
` Now we must cut up the game and divide it , ' say he ; and so they do , each one take his own share ; and , walk one behind the other , set out for the village .
But when they reach a great river the young man do not want the trouble of carry his pack any further , and leave it on the bank . '
I be go home another way , ' he tell his companion .
And take another road he reach the village long before they do .
` Have you return with empty hand ? '
ask the old man , a his son open the door .
` Have I ever do that , that you put me such a question ? '
ask the youth .
` No ; I have slay enough to feast u for many moon , but it be heavy , and I leave the pack on the bank of the great river .
Give me the arrow , I will finish make them , and you can go to the river and bring home the pack ! '
So the old man rise and go , and strap the meat on his shoulder ; but a he be cross the ford the strap break and the pack fell into the river .
He stoop to catch it , but it swirl past him .
He clutch again ; but in do so he over-balanced himself and be hurry into some rapid , where he be knock against some rock , and he sink and be drown , and his body be carry down the stream into smooth water when it rise to the surface again .
But by this time it have lose all likeness to a man , and be change into a piece of wood .
The wood float on , and the river get big and big and enter a new country .
There it be bear by the current close to the shore , and a woman who be down there wash her clothes catch it a it pass , and draw it out , say to herself : ` What a nice smooth plank !
I will use it a a table to put my food upon . '
And gather up her clothes she take the plank with her into her hut .
When her supper time come she stretch the board across two string which hang from the roof , and set upon it the pot contain a stew that smelt very good .
The woman have be work hard all day and be very hungry , so she take her big spoon and plunge it into the pot .
But what be her astonishment and disgust when both pot and food vanished instantly before her !
` Oh , you horrid plank , you have bring me ill-luck ! '
she cry .
And take it up she fling it away from her .
The woman have be surprise before at the disappearance of her food , but she be more astonished still when , instead of the plank , she behold a baby .
However , she be fond of child and have none of her own , so she make up her mind that she would keep it and take care of it .
The baby grow and thrive a no baby in that country have ever do , and in four day he be a man , and a tall and strong a any brave of the tribe .
` You have treat me well , ' he say , ` and meat shall never fail to your house .
But now I must go , for I have much work to do . '
Then he set out for his home .
It take him many day to get there , and when he saw his son sit in his place his anger be kindle , and his heart be stir to take vengeance upon him .
So he go out quickly into the forest and shed tear , and each tear become a bird .
` Stay there till I want you , ' say he ; and he return to the hut . '
I saw some pretty new bird , high up in a tree yonder , ' he remark .
And the son answer : ` Show me the way and I will get them for dinner . '
The two go out together , and after walk for about half an hour they old man stop .
` That be the tree , ' he say .
And the son begin to climb it .
Now a strange thing happen .
The high the young man climb the high the bird seem to be , and when he look down the earth below appear no big than a star .
Sill he try to go back , but he could not , and though he could not see the bird any longer he felt a if something be drag him up and up .
He think that he have be climb that tree for day , and perhaps he have , for suddenly a beautiful country , yellow with field of maize , stretch before him , and he gladly leave the top of the tree and enter it .
He walk through the maize without know where he be go , when he hear a sound of knocking , and saw two old blind woman crush their food between two stone .
He creep up to them on tiptoe , and when one old woman pass her dinner to the other he hold out his hand and take it and eat if for himself .
` How slow you be knead that cake , ' cry the other old woman at last .
` Why , I have give you your dinner , and what more do you want ? '
reply the second .
` You do n't ; at least I never get it , ' say the other . '
I certainly think you take it from me ; but here be some more . '
And again the young man stretch out his hand ; and the two old woman fell to quarrel afresh .
But when it happen for the third time the old woman suspect some trick , and one of them exclaim : ' I be sure there be a man here ; tell me , be you not my grandson ? '
` Yes , ' answer the young man , who wish to please her , ` and in return for your good dinner I will see if I can not restore your sight ; for I be teach in the art of healing by the best medicine man in the tribe . '
And with that he leave them , and wander about till he find the herb which he want .
Then he hasten back to the old woman , and beg them to boil him some water , he throw the herb in .
As soon a the pot begin to sing he take off the lid , and sprinkle the eye of the woman , and sight come back to them once more .
There be no night in that country , so , instead of go to bed very early , a he would have do in his own hut , the young man take another walk .
A splash noise near by drew him down to a valley through which run a large river , and up a waterfall some salmon be leap .
How their silver side glisten in the light , and how he long to catch some of the great fellow !
But how could he do it ?
He have behold no one except the old woman , and it be not very likely that they would be able to help him .
So with a sigh he turn away and go back to them , but , a he walk , a thought struck him .
He pull out one of his hair which hang nearly to his waist , and it instantly become a strong line , nearly a mile in length .
` Weave me a net that I may catch some salmon , ' say he .
And they weave him the net he ask for , and for many week he watch by the river , only go back to the old woman when he want a fish cooked .
At last , one day , when he be eat his dinner , the old woman who always speak first , say to him : ` We have be very glad to see you , grandson , but now it be time that you go home . '
And push aside a rock , he saw a deep hole , so deep that he could not see to the bottom .
Then they drag a basket out of the house , and tie a rope to it .
` Get in , and wrap this blanket round your head , ' say they ; ` and , whatever happen , do n't uncover it till you get to the bottom . '
Then they bid him farewell , and he curl himself up in the basket .
Down , down , down he go ; would he ever stop go ?
But when the basket do stop , the young man forget what he have be tell , and put his head out to see what be the matter .
In an instant the basket move , but , to his horror , instead of go down , he felt himself be draw upwards , and shortly after he behold the face of the old woman .
` You will never see your wife and son if you will not do a you be bid , ' say they .
` Now get in , and do not stir till you hear a crow call . '
This time the young man be wise , and though the basket often stop , and strange creature seem to rest on him and to pluck at his blanket , he hold it tight till he hear the crow call .
Then he fling off the blanket and sprang out , while the basket vanish in the sky .
He walk on quickly down the track that lead to the hut , when , before him , he saw his wife with his little son on her back .
` Oh !
there be father at last , ' cry the boy ; but the mother bid him cease from idle talk .
` But , mother , it be true ; father be come ! '
repeat the child .
And , to satisfy him , the woman turn round and perceive her husband .
Oh , how glad they all be to be together again !
And when the wind whistle through the forest , and the snow stood in great bank round the door , the father use to take the little boy on his knee and tell him how he catch salmon in the Land of the Sun .
How the Stalos Were Tricked -LSB- From the Journal of the Anthropological Institute . -RSB-
` Mother , I have see such a wonderful man , ' say a little boy one day , a he enter a hut in Lapland , bearing in his arm the bundle of stick he have be send out to gather .
` Have you , my son ; and what be he like ? '
ask the mother , a she take off the child 's sheepskin coat and shake it on the doorstep .
` Well , I be tire of stoop for the stick , and be lean against a tree to rest , when I hear a noise of ` sh - ` sh , among the dead leaf .
I think perhaps it be a wolf , so I stand very still .
But soon there come past a tall man -- oh !
twice as tall a father -- with a long red beard and a red tunic fasten with a silver girdle , from which hang a silver-handled knife .
Behind him follow a great dog , which look strong than any wolf , or even a bear .
But why be you so pale , mother ? '
` It be the Stalo , ' reply she , her voice tremble ; ` Stalo the man-eater !
You do well to hide , or you might never have come back .
But , remember that , though he be so tall and strong , he be very stupid , and many a Lapp have escape from his clutch by play him some clever trick . '
Not long after the mother and son have hold this talk , it begin to be whisper in the forest that the child of an old man call Patto have vanish one by one , no one know whither .
The unhappy father search the country for mile round without be able to find as much a a shoe or a handkerchief , to show him where they have pass , but at length a little boy come with news that he have see the Stalo hiding behind a well , near which the child use to play .
The boy have wait behind a clump of bush to see what would happen , and by-and-by he notice that the Stalo have lay a cunning trap in the path to the well , and that anybody who fell over it would roll into the water and drown there .
And , a he watch , Patto 's young daughter run gaily down the path , till her foot caught in the string that be stretch across the steep place .
She slip and fell , and in another instant have roll into the water within reach of the Stalo .
As soon a Patto hear this tale his heart be fill with rage , and he vow to have his revenge .
So he straightway take an old fur coat from the hook where it hang , and put it on go out into the forest .
When he reach the path that lead to the well he look hastily round to be sure that no one be watch him , then lay himself down as if he have be catch in the snare and have roll into the well , though he take care to keep his head out of the water .
Very soon he hear a ` sh - ` sh of the leaf , and there be the Stalo push his way through the undergrowth to see what chance he have of a dinner .
At the first glimpse of Patto 's head in the well he laugh loudly , cry : ` Ha !
ha !
This time it be the old as !
I wonder how he will taste ? '
And draw Patto out of the well , he fling him across his shoulder and carry him home .
Then he tie a cord round him and hang him over the fire to roast , while he finish a box that he be make before the door of the hut , which he mean to hold Patto 's flesh when it be cook .
In a very short time the box be so nearly do that it only want a little more chip out with an axe ; but this part of the work be easy accomplished indoors , and he call to one of his son who be lounge inside to bring him the tool .
The young man look everywhere , but he could not find the axe , for the very good reason that Patto have manage to pick it up and hide it in his clothes .
` Stupid fellow !
what be the use of you ? '
grumble his father angrily ; and he bid first one and then another of his son to fetch him the tool , but they have no good success than their brother . '
I must come myself , I suppose ! '
say Stalo , put aside the box .
But , meanwhile , Patto have slip from the hook and conceal himself behind the door , so that , a Stalo step in , his prisoner raise the axe , and with one blow the ogre 's head be roll on the ground .
His son be so frighten at the sight that they all run away .
And in this manner Patto avenge his dead child .
But though Stalo be dead , his three son be still live , and not very far off either .
They have go to their mother , who be tend some reindeer on the pasture , and tell her that by some magic , they know not what , their father 's head have roll from his body , and they have be so afraid that something dreadful would happen to them that they have come to take refuge with her .
The ogress say nothing .
Long ago she have find out how stupid her son be , so she just send them out to milk the reindeer , while she return to the other house to bury her husband 's body .
Now , three day ' journey from the hut on the pasture two brother Sodno dwelt in a small cottage with their sister Lyma , who tend a large herd of reindeer while they be out hunting .
Of late it have be whisper from one to another that the three young Stalos be to be see on the pasture , but the Sodno brother do not disturb themselves , the danger seem too far away .
Unluckily , however , one day , when Lyma be leave by herself in the hut , the three Stalos come down and carry her and the reindeer off to their own cottage .
The country be very lonely , and perhaps no one would have know in which direction she have go have not the girl manage to tie a ball of thread to the handle of a door at the back of the cottage and let it trail behind her .
Of course the ball be not long enough to go all the way , but it lay on the edge of a snowy track which lead straight to the Stalos ' house .
When the brother return from their hunting they find both the hut and the shed empty .
Loudly they cry : ` Lyma !
Lyma ! '
But no voice answer them ; and they fell to search all about , l perchance their sister might have drop some clue to guide them .
At length their eye drop on the thread which lay on the snow , and they set out to follow it .
On and on they go , and when at length the thread stop the brother know that another day 's journey would bring them to the Stalos ' dwelling .
Of course they do not dare to approach it openly , for the Stalos have the strength of giant , and besides , there be three of them ; so the two Sodnos climb into a big bushy tree which overhang a well .
` Perhaps our sister may be send to draw water here , ' they say to each other .
But it be not till the moon have rise that the sister come , and a she let down her bucket into the well , the leaf seem to whisper ` Lyma !
Lyma ! '
The girl start and look up , but could see nothing , and in a moment the voice come again .
` Be careful -- take no notice , fill your bucket , but listen carefully all the while , and we will tell you what to do so that you may escape yourself and set free the reindeer also . '
So Lyman bent over the well low than before , and seem busy than ever .
` You know , ' say her brother , ` that when a Stalo find that anything have be drop into his food he will not eat a morsel , but throw it to his dog .
Now , after the pot have be hang some time over the fire , and the broth be nearly cook , just rake up the log of wood so that some of the ash fly into the pot .
The Stalo will soon notice this , and will call you to give all the food to the dog ; but , instead , you must bring it straight to u , a it be three day since we have eat or drink .
That be all you need do for the present . '
Then Lyma take up her bucket and carry them into the house , and do a her brother have tell her .
They be so hungry that they eat the food up greedily without speaking , but when there be nothing left in the pot , the eldest one say : ` Listen carefully to what I have to tell you .
After the eldest Stalo have cook and eat a fresh supper , he will go to bed and sleep so soundly that not even a witch could wake him .
You can hear him snore a mile off , and then you must go into his room and pull off the iron mantle that cover him , and put it on the fire till it be almost red hot .
When that be do , come to u and we will give you further direction . ' '
I will obey you in everything , dear brother , ' answered Lyman ; and so she do .
It have happen that on this very even the Stalos have drive in some of the reindeer from the pasture , and have tie them up to the wall of the house so that they might be handy to kill for next day 's dinner .
The two Sodnos have see what they be do , and where the beast be secure ; so , at midnight , when all be still , they creep down from their tree and seize the reindeer by the horn which be lock together .
The animal be frighten , and begin to neigh and kick , a if they be fight together , and the noise become so great that even the eldest Stalo be awaken by it , and that be a thing which have never occur before .
Raising himself in his bed , he call to his young brother to go out and separate the reindeer or they would certainly kill themselves .
The young Stalo do a he be bid , and leave the house ; but no sooner be he out of the door than he be stab to the heart by one of the Sodnos , and fell without a groan .
Then they go back to worry the reindeer , and the noise become as great a ever , and a second time the Stalo awoke .
` The boy do not seem to be able to part the beast , ' he cry to his second brother ; ` go and help him , or I shall never get to sleep . '
So the brother go , and in an instant be strike dead a he leave the house by the sword of the eldest Sodno .
The Stalo wait in bed a little long for thing to get quiet , but a the clatter of the reindeer 's horn be as bad a ever , he rise angrily from his bed mutter to himself : ` It be extraordinary that they can not unlock themselves ; but a no one else seem able to help them I suppose I must go and do it . '
Rubbing his eye , he stand up on the floor and stretch his great arm and give a yawn which shake the wall .
The Sodnos hear it below , and post themselves , one at the big door and one at the little door at the back , for they do not know what their enemy would come out at .
The Stalo put out his hand to take his iron mantle from the bed , where it always lay , but the mantle be no there .
He wonder where it could be , and who could have move it , and after search through all the room , he find it hang over the kitchen fire .
But the first touch burnt him so badly that he let it alone , and go with nothing , except a stick in his hand , through the back door .
The young Sodno be stand ready for him , and a the Stalo pass the threshold strike him such a blow on the head that he roll over with a crash and never stir again .
The two Sodnos do not trouble about him , but quickly strip the young Stalos of their clothes , in which they dress themselves .
Then they sit still till the dawn should break and they could find out from the Stalos ' mother where the treasure be hide .
With the first ray of the sun the young Sodno go upstairs and enter the old woman 's room .
She be already up and dress , and sit by the window knitting , and the young man crept in softly and crouch down on the floor , lay his head on her lap .
For a while he keep silence , then he whisper gently : ` Tell me , dear mother , where do my eldest brother conceal his rich ? '
` What a strange question !
Surely you must know , ' answer she .
` No , I have forget ; my memory be so bad . '
` He dig a hole under the doorstep and place it there , ' say she .
And there be another pause .
By-and-by the Sodno ask again : ` And where may my second brother 's money be ? '
` Do n't you know that either ? '
cry the mother in surprise .
` Oh , yes ; I do once .
But since I fell upon my head I can remember nothing . '
` It be behind the oven , ' answer she .
And again be silence .
` Mother , dear mother , ' say the young man at last , ' I be almost afraid to ask you ; but I really have grow so stupid of late .
Where do I hide my own money ? '
But at this question the old woman fly into a passion , and vow that if she could find a rod she would bring his memory back to him .
Luckily , no rod be within her reach , and the Sodno manage , after a little , to coax her back into good humour , and at length she tell him that the young Stalo have bury his treasure under the very place where she be sit .
` Dear mother , ' say Lyman , who have come in unseen , and be kneel in front of the fire .
` Dear mother , do you know who it be you have be talk with ? '
The old woman start , but answer quietly : ` It be a Sodno , I suppose ? '
` You have guess right , ' reply Lyma .
The mother of the Stalos look round for her iron cane , which she always use to kill her victim , but it be not there , for Lyma have put it in the fire .
` Where be my iron cane ? '
ask the old woman .
` There ! '
answer Lyma , point to the flame .
The old woman sprang forward and seize it , but her clothes catch fire , and in a few minute she be burn to ash .
So the Sodno brother find the treasure , and they carry it , and their sister and the reindeer , to their own home , and be the rich men in all Lapland .
Andras Baive -LSB- From Lapplandische Marchen , J. C. Poestion . -RSB-
Once upon a time there live in Lapland a man who be so very strong and swift of foot that nobody in his native town of Vadso could come near him if they be run race in the summer evening .
The people of Vadso be very proud of their champion , and think that there be no one like him in the world , till , by-and-by , it come to their ear that there dwell among the mountain a Lapp , Andras Baive by name , who be say by his friend to be even strong and swift than the bailiff .
Of course not a creature in Vadso believe that , and declare that if it make the mountaineer happier to talk such nonsense , why , let them !
The winter be long and cold , and the thought of the villager be much busy with wolf than with Andras Baive , when suddenly , on a frosty day , he make his appearance in the little town of Vadso .
The bailiff be delight at this chance of try his strength , and at once go out to seek Andras and to coax him into give proof of his vigour .
As he walk along his eye fell upon a big eight-oared boat that lay upon the shore , and his face shone with pleasure .
` That be the very thing , ' laugh he , ' I will make him jump over that boat . '
Andras be quite ready to accept the challenge , and they soon settle the term of the wager .
He who could jump over the boat without so much a touch it with his heel be to be the winner , and would get a large sum of money a the prize .
So , follow by many of the villager , the two men walk down to the sea .
An old fisherman be choose to stand near the boat to watch fair play , and to hold the stake , and Andras , a the stranger be tell to jump first .
Going back to the flag which have be stick into the sand to mark the starting place , he run forward , with his head well throw back , and clear the boat with a mighty bound .
The lookers-on cheer him , and indeed he well deserve it ; but they wait anxiously all the same to see what the bailiff would do .
On he come , taller than Andras by several inch , but heavy of build .
He too sprang high and well , but a he come down his heel just graze the edge of the boat .
Dead silence reign amidst the townsfolk , but Andras only laugh and say carelessly : ` Just a little too short , bailiff ; next time you must do good than that . '
The bailiff turn red with anger at his rival 's scornful word , and answer quickly : ` Next time you will have something hard to do . '
And turn his back on his friend , he go sulkily home .
Andras , put the money he have earn in his pocket , go home also .
The following spring Andras happen to be drive his reindeer along a great fiord to the west of Vadso .
A boy who have meet him hasten to tell the bailiff that his enemy be only a few mile off ; and the bailiff , disguise himself a a Stalo , or ogre , call his son and his dog and row away across the fiord to the place where the boy have meet Andras .
Now the mountaineer be lazily walk along the sand , thinking of the new hut that he be build with the money that he have win on the day of his lucky jump .
He wander on , his eye fix on the sand , so that he do not see the bailiff drive his boat behind a rock , while he change himself into a heap of wreckage which float in on the wave .
A stumble over a stone recall Andras to himself , and look up he behold the mass of wreckage .
` Dear me !
I may find some use for that , ' he say ; and hasten down to the sea , wait till he could lay hold of some stray rope which might float towards him .
Suddenly -- he could not have tell why -- a nameless fear seize upon him , and he flee away from the shore a if for his life .
As he run he hear the sound of a pipe , such a only ogre of the Stalo kind be wont to use ; and there flash into his mind what the bailiff have say when they jump the boat : ` Next time you will have something hard to do . '
So it be no wreckage after all that he have see , but the bailiff himself .
It happen that in the long summer night up in the mountain , where the sun never set , and it be very difficult to get to sleep , Andras have spend many hour in the study of magic , and this stand him in good stead now .
The instant he hear the Stalo music he wish himself to become the foot of a reindeer , and in this guise he gallop like the wind for several mile .
Then he stop to take breath and find out what his enemy be do .
Nothing he could see , but to his ear the note of a pipe float over the plain , and ever , a he listen , it draw nearer .
A cold shiver shook Andras , and this time he wish himself the foot of a reindeer calf .
For when a reindeer calf have reach the age at which he begin first to lose his hair he be so swift that neither beast nor bird can come near him .
A reindeer calf be the swift of all thing live .
Yes ; but not so swift a a Stalo , a Andras find out when he stop to rest , and hear the pipe playing !
For a moment his heart sank , and he give himself up for dead , till he remember that , not far off , be two little lake join together by a short though very broad river .
In the middle of the river lay a stone that be always cover by water , except in dry season , and a the winter rain have be very heavy , he felt quite sure that not even the top of it could be see .
The next minute , if anyone have be look that way , he would have behold a small reindeer calf speeding northward , and by-and-by give a great spring , which land him in the midst of the stream .
But , instead of sink to the bottom , he pause a second to steady himself , then give a second spring which land him on the further shore .
He next ran on to a little hill where he saw down and begin to neigh loudly , so that the Stalo might know exactly where he be .
` Ah !
There you be , ' cry the Stalo , appear on the opposite bank ; ` for a moment I really think I have lose you . '
` No such luck , ' answered Andras , shake his head sorrowfully .
By this time he have take his own shape again .
` Well , but I do n't see how I be to get to you , ' say the Stalo , look up and down .
` Jump over , a I do , ' answered Andras ; ` it be quite easy . '
` But I could not jump this river ; and I do n't know how you do , ' reply the Stalo . '
I should be ashamed to say such thing , ' exclaim Andras .
` Do you mean to tell me that a jump , which the weak Lapp boy would make nothing of , be beyond your strength ? '
The Stalo grow red and angry when he hear these word , just a Andras mean him to do .
He bound into the air and fell straight into the river .
Not that that would have matter , for he be a good swimmer ; but Andras draw out the bow and arrow which every Lapp carry , and take aim at him .
His aim be good , but the Stalo sprang so high into the air that the arrow fly between his foot .
A second shot , direct at his forehead , fare no good , for this time the Stalo jump so high to the other side that the arrow pass between his finger and thumb .
Then Andras aim his third arrow a little over the Stalo 's head , and when he spring up , just an instant too soon , it hit him between the rib .
Mortally wound a he be , the Stalo be not yet dead , and manage to swim to the shore .
Stretching himself on the sand , he say slowly to Andras : ` Promise that you will give me an honourable burial , and when my body be lay in the grave go in my boat across the fiord , and take whatever you find in my house which belong to me .
My dog you must kill , but spare my son , Andras . '
Then he die ; and Andras sail in his boat away across the fiord and find the dog and boy .
The dog , a fierce , wicked-looking creature , he slew with one blow from his fist , for it be well know that if a Stalo 's dog lick the blood that flow from his dead master 's wound the Stalo come to life again .
That be why no REAL Stalo be ever see without his dog ; but the bailiff , be only half a Stalo , have forget him , when he go to the little lake in search of Andras .
Next , Andras put all the gold and jewel which he find in the boat into his pocket , and bid the boy get in , push it off from the shore , leave the little craft to drift a it would , while he himself run home .
With the treasure he possess he be able to buy a great herd of reindeer ; and he soon marry a rich wife , whose parent would not have him a a son-in-law when he be poor , and the two live happy for ever after .
The White Slipper -LSB- From Lapplandische Mahrchen , J. C. Poestion . -RSB-
Once upon a time there live a king who have a daughter just fifteen year old .
And what a daughter !
Even the mother who have daughter of their own could not help allow that the princess be much more beautiful and graceful than any of them ; and , a for the father , if one of them ever behold her by accident he could talk of nothing else for a whole day afterwards .
Of course the king , whose name be Balancin , be the complete slave of his little girl from the moment he lift her from the arm of her dead mother ; indeed , he do not seem to know that there be anyone else in the world to love .
Now Diamantina , for that be her name , do not reach her fifteenth birthday without proposal for marriage from every country under heaven ; but be the suitor who he might , the king always say him nay .
Behind the palace a large garden stretch away to the foot of some hill , and more than one river flow through .
Hither the princess would come each evening towards sunset , attend by her lady , and gather herself the flower that be to adorn her room .
She also bring with her a pair of scissors to cut off the dead bloom , and a basket to put them in , so that when the sun rise next morning he might see nothing unsightly .
When she have finish this task she would take a walk through the town , so that the poor people might have a chance of speak with her , and tell her of their trouble ; and then she would seek out her father , and together they would consult over the best mean of give help to those who need it .
But what have all this to do with the White Slipper ?
my reader will ask .
Have patience , and you will see .
Next to his daughter , Balancin love hunting , and it be his custom to spend several morning every week chase the boar which abound in the mountain a few mile from the city .
One day , rush downhill as fast a he could go , he put his foot into a hole and fell , roll into a rocky pit of bramble .
The king 's wound be not very severe , but his face and hand be cut and tear , while his foot be in a bad plight still , for , instead of proper hunt boot , he only wear sandal , to enable him to run more swiftly .
In a few day the king be as well a ever , and the sign of the scratch be almost go ; but one foot still remain very sore , where a thorn have pierce deeply and have fester .
The best doctor in the kingdom treat it with all their skill ; they bath , and poultice , and bandage , but it be in vain .
The foot only grow bad and bad , and become daily more swollen and painful .
After everyone have try his own particular cure , and find it fail , there come news of a wonderful doctor in some distant land who have heal the most astonishing disease .
On inquiring , it be find that he never leave the wall of his own city , and expect his patient to come to see him ; but , by dint of offer a large sum of money , the king persuade the famous physician to undertake the journey to his own court .
On his arrival the doctor be lead at once into the king 's presence , and make a careful examination of his foot .
` Alas !
your majesty , ' he say , when he have finish , ` the wound be beyond the power of man to heal ; but though I can not cure it , I can at least deaden the pain , and enable you to walk without so much suffering . '
` Oh , if you can only do that , ' cry the king , ' I shall be grateful to you for life !
Give your own order ; they shall be obey . '
` Then let your majesty bid the royal shoemaker make you a shoe of goat-skin very loose and comfortable , while I prepare a varnish to paint over it of which I alone have the secret ! '
So say , the doctor bow himself out , leave the king more cheerful and hopeful than he have be for long .
The day pass very slowly with him during the making of the shoe and the preparation of the varnish , but on the eighth morning the physician appear , bring with him the shoe in a case .
He draw it out to slip on the king 's foot , and over the goat-skin he have rub a polish so white that the snow itself be not more dazzling .
` While you wear this shoe you will not feel the slight pain , ' say the doctor .
` For the balsam with which I have rub it inside and out have , besides it healing balm , the quality of strengthen the material it touch , so that , even be your majesty to live a thousand year , you would find the slipper just a fresh at the end of that time a it be now . '
The king be so eager to put it on that he hardly give the physician time to finish .
He snatch it from the case and thrust his foot into it , nearly weep for joy when he find he could walk and run as easily a any beggar boy .
` What can I give you ? '
he cry , hold out both hand to the man who have work this wonder .
` Stay with me , and I will heap on you riches great than ever you dream of . '
But the doctor say he would accept nothing more than have be agree on , and must return at once to his own country , where many sick people be await him .
So king Balancin have to content himself with order the physician to be treat with royal honour , and desire that an escort should attend him on his journey home .
For two year everything go smoothly at court , and to king Balancin and his daughter the sun no sooner rise than it seem time for it to set .
Now , the king 's birthday fell in the month of June , and a the weather happen to be unusually fine , he tell the princess to celebrate it in any way that please her .
Diamantina be very fond of be on the river , and she be delight at this chance of delight her taste .
She would have a merry-making such a never have be see before , and in the evening , when they be tire of sailing and rowing , there should be music and dancing , play and firework .
At the very end , before the people go home , every poor person should be give a loaf of bread and every girl who be to be marry within the year a new dress .
The great day appear to Diamantina to be long in coming , but , like other day , it come at last .
Before the sun be fairly up in the heaven the princess , too full of excitement to stay in the palace , be walk about the street so covered with precious stone that you have to shade your eye before you could look at her .
By-and-by a trumpet sound , and she hurry home , only to appear again in a few moment walk by the side of her father down to the river .
Here a splendid barge be wait for them , and from it they watch all sort of race and feat of swimming and diving .
When these be over the barge proceed up the river to the field where the dancing and concert be to take place , and after the prize have be give away to the winner , and the loaf and the dress have be distribute by the princess , they bid farewell to their guest , and turn to step into the barge which be to carry them back to the palace .
Then a dreadful thing happen .
As the king step on board the boat one of the sandal of the white slipper , which have get loose , catch in a nail that be stick out , and cause the king to stumble .
The pain be great , and unconsciously he turn and shake his foot , so that the sandal give way , and in a moment the precious shoe be in the river .
It have all occur so quickly that nobody have notice the loss of the slipper , not even the princess , whom the king 's cry speedily bring to his side .
` What be the matter , dear father ? '
ask she .
But the king could not tell her ; and only manage to gasp out : ` My shoe !
my shoe ! '
While the sailor stand round staring , think that his majesty have suddenly go mad .
Seeing her father 's eye fix on the stream , Diamantina look hastily in that direction .
There , dance on the current , be the point of something white , which become more and more distant the longer they watch it .
The king could bear the sight no more , and , besides , now that the heal ointment in the shoe have be remove the pain in his foot be as bad a ever ; he give a sudden cry , stagger , and fell over the bulwark into the water .
In an instant the river be cover with bob head all swim their fast towards the king , who have be carry far down by the swift current .
At length one swimmer , strong than the rest , seize hold of his tunic , and draw him to the bank , where a thousand eager hand be ready to haul him out .
He be carry , unconscious , to the side of his daughter , who have faint with terror on see her father disappear below the surface , and together they be place in a coach and driven to the palace , where the best doctor in the city be await their arrival .
In a few hour the princess be as well a ever ; but the pain , the wetting , and the shock of the accident , all tell severely on the king , and for three day he lay in a high fever .
Meanwhile , his daughter , herself nearly mad with grief , give order that the white slipper should be seek for far and wide ; and so it be , but even the clever diver could find no trace of it at the bottom of the river .
When it become clear that the slipper must have be carry out to sea by the current , Diamantina turn her thought elsewhere , and send messenger in search of the doctor who have bring relief to her father , beg him to make another slipper as fast a possible , to supply the place of the one which be lose .
But the messenger return with the sad news that the doctor have die some week before , and , what be bad , his secret have die with him .
In his weakness this intelligence have such an effect on the king that the physician fear he would become as ill a before .
He could hardly be persuade to touch food , and all night long he lay moan , partly with pain , and partly over his own folly in not have beg the doctor to make him several dozen of white slipper , so that in case of accident he might always have one to put on .
However , by-and-by he saw that it be no use weep and wailing , and command that they should search for his lost treasure more diligently than ever .
What a sight the river bank present in those day !
It seem a if all the people in the country be gather on them .
But this second search be no more fortunate than the first , and at last the king issue a proclamation that whoever find the miss slipper should be make heir to the crown , and should marry the princess .
Now many daughter would have rebel at be dispose of in the manner ; and it must be admit that Diamantina 's heart sank when she hear what the king have do .
Still , she love her father so much that she desire his comfort more than anything else in the world , so she say nothing , and only bow her head .
Of course the result of the proclamation be that the river bank become more crowded than before ; for all the princess 's suitor from distant land flock to the spot , each hoping that he might be the lucky finder .
Many time a shin stone at the bottom of the stream be take for the slipper itself , and every evening saw a band of drip downcast men return homewards .
But one youth always linger long than the rest , and night would still see him engage in the search , though his clothes stick to his skin and his teeth chatter .
One day , when the king be lie on his bed rack with pain , he hear the noise of a scuffle go on in his antechamber , and ring a golden bell that stood by his side to summon one of his servant .
` Sire , ' answer the attendant , when the king inquire what be the matter , ` the noise you hear be cause by a young man from the town , who have have the impudence to come here to ask if he may measure your majesty 's foot , so a to make you another slipper in place of the lost one . '
` And what have you do to the youth ? '
say the king .
` The servant push him out of the palace , and , add a few blow to teach him not to be insolent , ' reply the man .
` Then they do very ill , ' answer the king , with a frown .
` He come here from kindness , and there be no reason to maltreat him . '
` Oh , my lord , he have the audacity to wish to touch your majesty 's sacred person -- he , a good-for-nothing boy , a mere shoemaker 's apprentice , perhaps !
And even if he could make shoe to perfection they would be no use without the soothing balsam . '
The king remain silent for a few moment , then he say : ` Never mind .
Go and fetch the youth and bring him to me .
I would gladly try any remedy that may relieve my pain . '
So , soon afterwards , the youth , who have not go far from the palace , be catch and usher into the king 's presence .
He be tall and handsome and , though he profess to make shoe , his manner be good and modest , and he bow low a he beg the king not only to allow him to take the measure of his foot , but also to suffer him to place a healing plaster over the wound .

So he stretch out his bad foot which the youth examine with great attention , and then gently lay on the plaster .
Very shortly the ointment begin to soothe the sharp pain , and the king , whose confidence increase every moment , beg the young man to tell him his name . '
I have no parent ; they die when I be six , sire , ' reply the youth , modestly .
` Everyone in the town call me Gilguerillo , because , when I be little , I go sing through the world in spite of my misfortune .
Luckily for me I be bear to be happy . '
` And you really think you can cure me ? '
ask the king .
` Completely , my lord , ' answer Gilguerillo .
` And how long do you think it will take ? '
` It be not an easy task ; but I will try to finish it in a fortnight , ' reply the youth .
A fortnight seem to the king a long time to make one slipper .
But he only say : ` Do you need anything to help you ? '
` Only a good horse , if your majesty will be kind enough to give me one , ' answer Gilguerillo .
And the reply be so unexpected that the courtier could hardly restrain their smile , while the king star silently .
` You shall have the horse , ' he say at last , ` and I shall expect you back in a fortnight .
If you fulfil your promise you know your reward ; if not , I will have you flog for your impudence . '
Gilguerillo bow , and turn to leave the palace , follow by the jeer and scoff of everyone he meet .
But he pay no heed , for he have get what he want .
He wait in front of the gate till a magnificent horse be lead up to him , and vault into the saddle with an ease which rather surprise the attendant , ride quickly out of the town amidst the jest of the assembled crowd , who have heard of his audacious proposal .
And while he be on his way let u pause for a moment and tell who he be .
Both father and mother have die before the boy be six year old ; and he have live for many year with his uncle , whose life have be pass in the study of chemistry .
He could leave no money to his nephew , a he have a son of his own ; but he teach him all he know , and at his dead Gilguerillo enter an office , where he work for many hour daily .
In his spare time , instead of play with the other boy , he pass hour pore over book , and because he be timid and like to be alone he be hold by everyone to be a little mad .
Therefore , when it become known that he have promise to cure the king 's foot , and have ride away -- no one knew where -- a roar of laughter and mockery rang through the town , and jeer and scoff word be send after him .
But if they have only know what be Gilguerillo 's thought they would have think him madder than ever .
The real truth be that , on the morning when the princess have walk through the street before make holiday on the river Gilguerillo have see her from his window , and have straightway fall in love with her .
Of course he felt quite hopeless .
It be absurd to imagine that the apothecary 's nephew could ever marry the king 's daughter ; so he do his best to forget her , and study hard than before , till the royal proclamation suddenly fill him with hope .
When he be free he no longer spend the precious moment pore over book , but , like the rest , he might have be see wander along the bank of the river , or dive into the stream after something that lay glisten in the clear water , but which turn out to be a white pebble or a bit of glass .
And at the end he understand that it be not by the river that he would win the princess ; and , turn to his book for comfort , he study hard than ever .
There be an old proverb which say : ` Everything come to him who know how to wait . '
It be not all men who know hot to wait , any more than it be all men who can learn by experience ; but Gilguerillo be one of the few and instead of think his life waste because he could not have the thing he want most , he try to busy himself in other direction .
So , one day , when he expect it least , his reward come to him .
He happen to be read a book many hundred of year old , which tell of remedy for all kind of disease .
Most of them , he know , be merely invent by old woman , who seek to prove themselves wise than other people ; but at length he come to something which cause him to sit up straight in his chair , and make his eye brighten .
This be the description of a balsam -- which would cure every kind of sore or wound -- distil from a plant only to be find in a country so distant that it would take a man on foot two month to go and come back again .
When I say that the book declare that the balsam could heal every sort of sore or wound , there be a few against which it be powerless , and it give certain sign by which these might be know .
This be the reason why Gilguerillo demand to see the king 's foot before he would undertake to cure it ; and to obtain admittance he give out that he be a shoemaker .
However , the dreaded sign be absent , and his heart bound at the thought that the princess be within his reach .
Perhaps she be ; but a great deal have to be accomplish yet , and he have allow himself a very short time in which to do it .
He spar his horse only so much a be needful , yet it take him six day to reach the spot where the plant grow .
A thick wood lay in front of him , and , fasten the bridle tightly to a tree , he fling himself on his hand and knee and begin to hunt for the treasure .
Many time he fancy it be close to him , and many time it turn out to be something else ; but , at last , when light be fading , and he have almost give up hope , he come upon a large bed of the plant , right under his foot !
Trembling with joy , he pick every scrap he could see , and place it in his wallet .
Then , mount his horse , he gallop quickly back towards the city .
It be night when he enter the gate , and the fifteen day allot be not up till the next day .
His eye be heavy with sleep , and his body ache with the long strain , but , without pause to rest , he kindle a fire on be hearth , and quickly fill a pot with water , throw in the herb and leave them to boil .
After that he lay down and slept soundly .
The sun be shin when he awake , and he jump up and run to the pot .
The plant have disappear and in it stead be a thick syrup , just a the book have say there would be .
He lift the syrup out with a spoon , and after spread it in the sun till it be partly dry , pour it into a small flask of crystal .
He next wash himself thoroughly , and dress himself , in his best clothes , and put the flask in his pocket , set out for the palace , and beg to see the king without delay .
Now Balancin , whose foot have be much less painful since Gilguerillo have wrap it in the plaster , be count the day to the young man 's return ; and when he be tell Gilguerillo be there , order him to be admit at once .
As he enter , the king raise himself eagerly on his pillow , but his face fell when he saw no sign of a slipper .
` You have fail , then ? '
he say , throw up his hand in despair . '
I hope not , your majesty ; I think not , ' answer the youth .
And draw the flask from his pocket , he pour two or three drop on the wound .
` Repeat this for three night , and you will find yourself cure , ' say he .
And before the king have time to thank him he have bow himself out .
Of course the news soon spread through the city , and men and woman never tire of call Gilguerillo an impostor , and prophesy that the end of the three day would see him in prison , if not on the scaffold .
But Gilguerillo pay no heed to their hard word , and no more do the king , who take care that no hand but his own should put on the healing balsam .
On the fourth morning the king awoke and instantly stretch out his wounded foot that he might prove the truth or falsehood of Gilguerillo 's remedy .
The wound be certainly cure on that side , but how about the other ?
Yes , that be cure also ; and not even a scar be leave to show where it have be !
Was ever any king so happy a Balancin when he satisfy himself of this ?
Lightly a a deer he jump from his bed , and begin to turn head over heel and to perform all sort of antic , so a to make sure that his foot be in truth as well a it look .
And when he be quite tired he send for his daughter , and bid the courtier bring the lucky young man to his room .
` He be really young and handsome , ' say the princess to herself , heave a sigh of relief that it be not some dreadful old man who have heal her father ; and while the king be announce to his courtier the wonderful cure that have be make , Diamantina be think that if Gilguerillo look so well in his common dress , how much improve by the splendid garment of a king ' son .
However , she hold her peace , and only watch with amusement when the courtier , know there be no help for it , do homage and obeisance to the chemist 's boy .
Then they bring to Gilguerillo a magnificent tunic of green velvet border with gold , and a cap with three white plume stick in it ; and at the sight of him so arrayed , the princess fell in love with him in a moment .
The wedding be fix to take place in eight day , and at the ball afterwards nobody dance so long or so lightly a king Balancin .
The Magic Book -LSB- From Capullos de Rosa , por D. Enrique Ceballos Quintana . -RSB-
-LSB- From AEventyr fra Zylland samlede og optegnede af Tang Kristensen .
Translated from the Danish by Mrs. Skavgaard-Pedersen . -RSB-
There be once an old couple name Peder and Kirsten who have an only son call Hans .
From the time he be a little boy he have be tell that on his sixteenth birthday he must go out into the world and serve his apprenticeship .
So , one fine summer morning , he start off to seek his fortune with nothing but the clothes he wear on his back .
For many hour he trudge on merrily , now and then stop to drink from some clear spring or to pick some ripe fruit from a tree .
The little wild creature peep at him from beneath the bush , and he nod and smile , and wish them ` Good-morning . '
After he have be walk for some time he meet an old white-bearded man who be come along the footpath .
The boy would not step aside , and the man be determine not to do so either , so they run against one another with a bump .
` It seem to me , ' say the old fellow , ` that a boy should give way to an old man . '
` The path be for me as well a for you , ' answered young Hans saucily , for he have never be taught politeness .
` Well , that 's true enough , ' answer the other mildly .
` And where be you go ? ' '
I be go into service , ' say Hans .
` Then you can come and serve me , ' reply the man .
Well , Hans could do that ; but what would his wage be ?
` Two pound a year , and nothing to do but keep some room clean , ' say the new-comer .
This seem to Hans to be easy enough ; so he agree to enter the old man 's service , and they set out together .
On their way they cross a deep valley and come to a mountain , where the man open a trapdoor , and bidding Hans follow him , he creep in and begin to go down a long flight of step .
When they get to the bottom Hans saw a large number of room light by many lamp and full of beautiful thing .
While he be look round the old man say to him : ` Now you know what you have to do .
You must keep these room clean , and strew sand on the floor every day .
Here be a table where you will always find food and drink , and there be your bed .
You see there be a great many suit of clothes hang on the wall , and you may wear any you please ; but remember that you be never to open this locked door .
If you do ill will befall you .
Farewell , for I be go away again and can not tell when I may return .
No sooner have the old man disappear than Hans sit down to a good meal , and after that go to bed and slept until the morning .
At first he could not remember what have happen to him , but by-and-by he jump up and go into all the room , which he examine carefully .
` How foolish to bid me to put sand on the floor , ' he think , ` when there be nobody here by myself !
I shall do nothing of the sort . '
And so he shut the door quickly , and only clean and set in order his own room .
And after the first few day he felt that that be unnecessary too , because no one come there to see if the room where clean or not .
At last he do no work at all , but just sit and wonder what be behind the locked door , till he determine to go and look for himself .
The key turn easily in the lock .
Hans enter , half frighten at what he be do , and the first thing he behold be a heap of bone .
That be not very cheerful ; and he be just go out again when his eye fell on a shelf of book .
Here be a good way of pass the time , he think , for he be fond of reading , and he take one of the book from the shelf .
It be all about magic , and tell you how you could change yourself into anything in the world you like .
Could anything be more exciting or more useful ?
So he put it in his pocket , and run quickly away out of the mountain by a little door which have be leave open .
When he get home his parent ask him what he have be do and where he have get the fine clothes he wear .
` Oh , I earn them myself , ' answer he .
` You never earn them in this short time , ' say his father .
` Be off with you ; I wo n't keep you here .
I will have no thief in my house ! '
` Well I only come to help you , ' reply the boy sulkily .
` Now I 'll be off , a you wish ; but to-morrow morning when you rise you will see a great dog at the door .
Do not drive it away , but take it to the castle and sell it to the duke , and they will give you ten dollar for it ; only you must bring the strap you lead it with , back to the house . '
Sure enough the next day the dog be stand at the door wait to be let in .
The old man be rather afraid of get into trouble , but his wife urge him to sell the dog a the boy have bid him , so he take it up to the castle and sell it to the duke for ten dollar .
But he do not forget to take off the strap with which he have lead the animal , and to carry it home .
When he get there old Kirsten meet him at the door .
` Well , Peder , and have you sell the dog ? '
ask she .
` Yes , Kirsten ; and I have bring back ten dollar , a the boy tell u , ' answered Peder .
` Ay !
but that 's fine ! '
say his wife .
` Now you see what one get by do a one be bid ; if it have not be for me you would have drive the dog away again , and we should have lose the money .
After all , I always know what be best . '
` Nonsense ! '
say her husband ; ` woman always think they know best .
I should have sell the dog just the same whatever you have tell me .
Put the money away in a safe place , and do n't talk so much . '
The next day Hans come again ; but though everything have turn out a he have foretell , he find that his father be still not quite satisfied .
` Be off with you ! '
say he , ` you 'll get u into trouble . ' '
I have n't help you enough yet , ' reply the boy .
` To-morrow there will come a great fat cow , as big a the house .
Take it to the king 's palace and you 'll get as much a a thousand dollar for it .
Only you must unfasten the halter you lead it with and bring it back , and do n't return by the high road , but through the forest . '
The next day , when the couple rise , they saw an enormous head look in at their bedroom window , and behind it be a cow which be nearly as big a their hut .
Kirsten be wild with joy to think of the money the cow would bring them .
` But how be you go to put the rope over her head ? '
ask she .
` Wait and you 'll see , mother , ' answer her husband .
Then Peder take the ladder that lead up to the hayloft and set it against the cow 's neck , and he climb up and slip the rope over her head .
When he have make sure that the noose be fast they start for the palace , and meet the king himself walk in his ground . '
I hear that the princess be go to be marry , ' say Peder , ` so I 've bring your majesty a cow which be big than any cow that be ever see .
Will your majesty deign to buy it ? '
The king have , in truth , never see so large a beast , and he willingly pay the thousand dollar , which be the price demand ; but Peder remember to take off the halter before he leave .
After he be go the king sent for the butcher and tell him to kill the animal for the wedding feast .
The butcher get ready his pole-axe ; but just a he be go to strike , the cow change itself into a dove and fly away , and the butcher stand star after it a if he be turn to stone .
However , a the dove could not be find , he be oblige to tell the king what have happen , and the king in his turn despatch messenger to capture the old man and bring him back .
But Peder be safe in the wood , and could not be find .
When at last he felt the danger be over , and he might go home , Kirsten nearly faint with joy at the sight of all the money he bring with him .
` Now that we be rich people we must build a big house , ' cry she ; and be vex to find that Peder only shake his head and say : ` No ; if they do that people would talk , and say they have get their wealth by ill-doing . '
A few morning later Hans come again .
` Be off before you get u into trouble , ' say his father .
` So far the money have come right enough , but I do n't trust it . '
` Do n't worry over that , father , ' say Hans .
` To-morrow you will find a horse outside by the gate .
Ride it to market and you will get a thousand dollar for it .
Only do n't forget to loosen the bridle when you sell it . '

` Take care it do n't hurt you , Peder , ' say she .
` Nonsense , wife , ' answer he crossly .
` When I be a lad I live with horse , and could ride anything for twenty mile round . '
But that be not quite the truth , for he have never mount a horse in his life .
Still , the animal be quiet enough , so Peder get safely to market on it back .
There he meet a man who offer nine hundred and ninety-nine dollar for it , but Peder would take nothing less than a thousand .
At last there come an old , grey-bearded man who look at the horse and agree to buy it ; but the moment he touch it the horse begin to kick and plunge . '
I must take the bridle off , ' say Peder .
` It be not to be sell with the animal a be usually the case . '
` I 'll give you a hundred dollar for the bridle , ' say the old man , take out his purse .
` No , I ca n't sell it , ' reply Hans 's father .
` Five hundred dollar ! '
` No . ' '
A thousand ! '
At this splendid offer Peder 's prudence give way ; it be a shame to let so much money go .
So he agree to accept it .
But he could hardly hold the horse , it become so unmanageable .
So he give the animal in charge to the old man , and go home with his two thousand dollar .
Kirsten , of course , be delight at this new piece of good fortune , and insist that the new house should be build and land buy .
This time Peder consent , and soon they have quite a fine farm .
Meanwhile the old man ride off on his new purchase , and when he come to a smithy he ask the smith to forge shoe for the horse .
The smith propose that they should first have a drink together , and the horse be tie up by the spring whilst they go indoors .
The day be hot , and both men be thirsty , and , besides , they have much to say ; and so the hour slip by and find them still talk .
Then the servant girl come out to fetch a pail of water , and , be a kind-hearted lass , she give some to the horse to drink .
What be her surprise when the animal say to her : ` Take off my bridle and you will save my life . ' '
I dare not , ' say she ; ` your master will be so angry . '
` He can not hurt you , ' answer the horse , ` and you will save my life . '
At that she take off the bridle ; but nearly faint with astonishment when the horse turn into a dove and fly away just a the old man come out of the house .
Directly he saw what have happen he change himself into a hawk and flew after the dove .
Over the wood and field they go , and at length they reach a king 's palace surround by beautiful garden .
The princess be walk with her attendant in the rise garden when the dove turn itself into a gold ring and fell at her foot .
` Why , here be a ring ! '
she cry , ` where could it have come from ? '
And pick it up she put it on her finger .
As she do so the hill-man lose his power over Hans -- for of course you understand that it be he who have be the dog , the cow , the horse and the dove .
` Well , that be really strange , ' say the princess .
` It fit me a though it have be make for me ! '
Just at that moment up come the king .
` Look at what I have find ! '
cry his daughter .
` Well , that be not worth much , my dear , ' say he .
` Besides , you have ring enough , I should think . '
` Never mind , I like it , ' reply the princess .
But as soon a she be alone , to her amazement , the ring suddenly leave her finger and become a man .
You can imagine how frightened she be , a , indeed , anybody would have be ; but in an instant the man become a ring again , and then turn back to a man , and so it go on for some time until she begin to get use to these sudden change . '
I be sorry I frighten you , ' say Hans , when he think he could safely speak to the princess without make her scream . '
I take refuge with you because the old hill-man , whom I have offend , be try to kill me , and here I be safe . '
` You have good stay here then , ' say the princess .
So Hans stay , and he and she become good friend ; though , of course , he only become a man when no one else be present .
This be all very well ; but , one day , a they be talk together , the king happen to enter the room , and although Hans quickly change himself into a ring again it be too late .
The king be terribly angry .
` So this be why you have refuse to marry all the king and prince who have seek your hand ? '
he cry .
And , without wait for her to speak , he command that his daughter should be wall up in the summer-house and starve to death with her lover .
That even the poor princess , still wear her ring , be put into the summer-house with enough food to last for three day , and the door be bricked up .
But at the end of a week or two the king think it be time to give her a grand funeral , in spite of her bad behaviour , and he have the summer-house open .
He could hardly believe his eye when he find that the princess be not there , nor Hans either .
Instead , there lay at his foot a large hole , big enough for two people to pass through .
Now what have happen be this .
When the princess and Hans have give up hope , and cast themselves down on the ground to die , they fell down this hole , and right through the earth as well , and at last they tumble into a castle built of pure gold at the other side of the world , and there they live happily .
But of this , of course , the king know nothing .
` Will anyone go down and see where the passage lead to ? '
he ask , turn to his guard and courtier . '
I will reward splendidly the man who be brave enough to explore it . '
For a long time nobody answer .
The hole be dark and deep , and if it have a bottom no one could see it .

But in a moment he , too , fell down , down , down .

` You be the man , ' say he ; ` and I be he who love your daughter , and become a gold ring on her finger .
She be safe , and wait not far from here ; but you have pronounce judgment on yourself . '
Then the king fell on his knee and beg for mercy ; and a he have in other respect be a good father , they forgive him .
The wedding of Hans and the princess be celebrate with great festivity which last a month .
As for the hill-man he intend to be present ; but whilst he be walk along a street which lead to the palace a loose stone fell on his head and kill him .

Once upon a time there live a cat of marvellous beauty , with a skin a soft and shin a silk , and wise green eye , that could see even in the dark .
His name be Gon , and he belong to a music teacher , who be so fond and proud of him that he would not have part with him for anything in the world .
Now not far from the music master 's house there dwell a lady who possess a most lovely little pussy cat call Koma .
She be such a little dear altogether , and blink her eye so daintily , and eat her supper so tidily , and when she have finish she lick her pink nose so delicately with her little tongue , that her mistress be never tire of say , ` Koma , Koma , what should I do without you ? '
Well , it happen one day that these two , when out for an evening stroll , meet under a cherry tree , and in one moment fell madly in love with each other .
Gon have long felt that it be time for him to find a wife , for all the lady in the neighbourhood pay him so much attention that it make him quite shy ; but he be not easy to please , and do not care about any of them .
Now , before he have time to think , Cupid have entangle him in his net , and he be fill with love towards Koma .
She fully return his passion , but , like a woman , she saw the difficulty in the way , and consult sadly with Gon a to the mean of overcome them .
Gon entreat his master to set matter right by buy Koma , but her mistress would not part from her .
Then the music master be ask to sell Gon to the lady , but he decline to listen to any such suggestion , so everything remain a before .
At length the love of the couple grow to such a pitch that they determine to please themselves , and to seek their fortune together .
So one moonlight night they steal away , and venture out into an unknown world .
All day long they march bravely on through the sunshine , till they have leave their home far behind them , and towards even they find themselves in a large park .
The wanderer by this time be very hot and tired , and the grass look very soft and inviting , and the tree cast cool deep shadow , when suddenly an ogre appear in this Paradise , in the shape of a big , big dog !
He come spring towards them show all his teeth , and Koma shriek , and rush up a cherry tree .
Gon , however , stand his ground boldly , and prepare to give battle , for he felt that Koma 's eye be upon him , and that he must not run away .
But , ala !
his courage would have avail him nothing have his enemy once touch him , for he be large and powerful , and very fierce .
From her perch in the tree Koma saw it all , and scream with all her might , hop that some one would hear , and come to help .
Luckily a servant of the princess to whom the park belong be walk by , and he drive off the dog , and pick up the trembling Gon in his arm , carry him to his mistress .
So poor little Koma be leave alone , while Gon be bear away full of trouble , not in the least know what to do .

She shriek and throw herself backwards , and Gon , who have be curl up on a stool at her foot , understand her terror , and with one bound seize the snake by his neck .
He give him one bite and one shake , and fling him on the ground , where he lay , never to worry the princess any more .
Then she take Gon in her arm , and praise and caress him , and saw that he have the nice bit to eat , and the soft mat to lie on ; and he would have have nothing in the world to wish for if only he could have see Koma again .
Time pass on , and one morning Gon lay before the house door , bask in the sun .
He look lazily at the world stretch out before him , and saw in the distance a big ruffian of a cat teasing and ill-treating quite a little one .
He jump up , full of rage , and chase away the big cat , and then he turn to comfort the little one , when his heart nearly burst with joy to find that it be Koma .
At first Koma do not know him again , he have grow so large and stately ; but when it dawn upon her who it be , her happiness knew no bound .

By-and-bye the princess herself get marry , and bring a prince to dwell in the palace in the park .
