Once upon a time there live a man who have two son but they do not get on at all well together , for the younger be much handsome than his elder brother who be very jealous of him .
When they grow old , thing become bad and bad , and at last one day a they be walk through a wood the elder youth seize hold of the other , tie him to a tree , and go on his way hop that the boy might starve to death .
However , it happen that an old and humpbacked shepherd pass the tree with his flock , and see the prisoner , he stop and say to him , ` Tell me , my son why be you tie to that tree ? '
` Because I be so crooked , ' answer the young man ; ` but it have quite cure me , and now my back be as straight a can be . ' '
I wish you would bind me to a tree , ' exclaim the shepherd , ` so that my back would get straight . '
` With all the pleasure in life , ' reply the youth .
` If you will loosen these cord I will tie you up with them as firmly a I can . '
This be soon do , and then the young man drive off the sheep , leave their real shepherd to repent of his folly ; and before he have go very far he meet with a horse boy and a driver of ox , and he persuade them to turn with him and to seek for adventure .
By these and many other trick he soon become so celebrate that his fame reach the king 's ear , and his majesty be fill with curiosity to see the man who have manage to outwit everybody .
So he command his guard to capture the young man and bring him before him .
And when the young man stand before the king , the king speak to him and say , ` By your trick and the prank that you have play on other people , you have , in the eye of the law , forfeit your life .
But on one condition I will spare you , and that be , if you will bring me the fly horse that belong to the great dragon .
Fail in this , and you shall be hew in a thousand piece . '
` If that be all , ' say the youth , ` you shall soon have it . '
So he go out and make his way straight to the stable where the fly horse be tether .
He stretch his hand cautiously out to seize the bridle , when the horse suddenly begin to neigh as loud a he could .
Now the room in which the dragon slept be just above the stable , and at the sound of the neighing he wake and cry to the horse , ` What be the matter , my treasure ?
be anything hurt you ? '
After wait a little while the young man try again to loose the horse , but a second time it neigh so loudly that the dragon wake up in a hurry and call out to know why the horse be make such a noise .
But when the same thing happen the third time , the dragon lose his temper , and go down into the stable and take a whip and give the horse a good beating .
This offend the horse and make him angry , and when the young man stretch out his hand to untie his head , he make no further fuss , but suffer himself to be lead quietly away .
Once clear of the stable the young man sprang on his back and gallop off , call over his shoulder , ` Hi !
dragon !
dragon !
if anyone ask you what have become of your horse , you can say that I have get him ! '
But the king say , ` The fly horse be all very well , but I want something more .
You must bring me the cover with the little bell that lie on the bed of the dragon , or I will have you hew into a thousand piece . '
` Is that all ? '
answer the youth .
` That be easily do . '

` So be it , ' say the king .

The Goblin and the Grocer Translated from the German of Hans Andersen .
There be once a hard-working student who live in an attic , and he have nothing in the world of his own .
There be also a hard-working grocer who live on the first floor , and he have the whole house for his own .
The Goblin belong to him , for every Christmas Eve there be wait for him at the grocer 's a dish of jam with a large lump of butter in the middle .
The grocer could afford this , so the Goblin stay in the grocer 's shop ; and this teach u a good deal .
One even the student come in by the back door to buy a candle and some cheese ; he have no one to send , so he come himself .
He get what he want , pay for it , and nod a good evening to the grocer and his wife -LRB- she be a woman who could do more than nod ; she could talk -RRB- .
When the student have say good night he suddenly stand still , read the sheet of paper in which the cheese have be wrap .
It be a leaf tear out of an old book -- a book of poetry ` There 's more of that over there ! '
say the grocer ' I give an old woman some coffee for the book .
If you like to give me twopence you can have the rest . '
` Yes , ' say the student , ` give me the book instead of the cheese .
I can eat my bread without cheese .
It would be a shame to leave the book to be tear up .
You be a clever and practical man , but about poetry you understand as much a that old tub over there ! '
And that sound rude as far a the tub be concern , but the grocer laugh , and so do the student .
It be only say in fun .
But the Goblin be angry that anyone should dare to say such a thing to a grocer who own the house and sell the best butter .
When it be night and the shop be shut , and everyone be in bed except the student , the Goblin go upstairs and take the grocer 's wife 's tongue .
She do not use it when she be asleep , and on whatever object in the room he put it that thing begin to speak , and speak out it thought and feeling just as well a the lady to whom it belong .
But only one thing at a time could use it , and that be a good thing , or they would have all speak together .
The Goblin lay the tongue on the tub in which be the old newspaper .
` Is it true , ' he ask , ' that you know nothing about poetry ? '
` Certainly not ! '
answer the tub .
` Poetry be something that be in the paper , and that be frequently cut out .
I have a great deal more in me than the student have , and yet I be only a small tub in the grocer 's shop . '
And the Goblin put the tongue on the coffee-mill , and how it begin to grind !
He put it on the butter-cask , and on the till , and all be of the same opinion a the waste-paper tub .
and one must believe the majority .
` Now I will tell the student ! '
and with these word he creep softly up the stair to the attic where the student live .
There be a light burning , and the Goblin peep through the key-hole and saw that he be read the torn book that he have buy in the shop .
But how bright it be !
Out of the book shot a streak of light which grow into a large tree and spread it branch far above the student .
Every leaf be alive , and every flower be a beautiful girl 's head , some with dark and shining eye , others with wonderful blue one .
Every fruit be a glittering star , and there be a marvellous music in the student 's room .
The little Goblin have never even dreamt of such a splendid sight , much less see it .
He stand on tiptoe gazing and gazing , till the candle in the attic be put out ; the student have blow it out and have go to bed , but the Goblin remain stand outside listen to the music , which very softly and sweetly be now sing the student a lullaby . '
I have never see anything like this ! '
say the Goblin . '
I never expect this !
I must stay with the student . '
The little fellow think it over , for he be a sensible Goblin .
Then he sigh , ` The student have no jam ! '
And on that he go down to the grocer again .
And it be a good thing that he do go back , for the tub have nearly wear out the tongue .
It have read everything that be inside it , on the one side , and be just go to turn itself round and read from the other side when the Goblin come in and return the tongue to it owner .
But the whole shop , from the till down to the shaving , from that night change their opinion of the tub , and they look up to it , and have such faith in it that they be under the impression that when the grocer read the art and drama critique out of the paper in the evening , it all come from the tub .
But the Goblin could no longer sit quietly listen to the wisdom and intellect downstairs .
No , as soon a the light shone in the evening from the attic it seem to him a though it beam be strong rope drag him up , and he have to go and peep through the key-hole .
There he felt the sort of feeling we have look at the great roll sea in a storm , and he burst into tear .
He could not himself say why he weep , but in spite of his tear he felt quite happy .
How beautiful it must be to sit under that tree with the student , but that he could not do ; he have to content himself with the key-hole and be happy there !
There he stand out on the cold landing , the autumn wind blow through the crack of the floor .
It be cold -- very cold , but he first find it out when the light in the attic be put out and the music in the wood die away .
Ah !
then it freeze him , and he creep down again into his warm corner ; there it be comfortable and cosy .
When Christmas come , and with it the jam with the large lump of butter , ah !
then the grocer be first with him .
But in the middle of the night the Goblin awoke , hear a great noise and knock against the shutter -- people hammer from outside .

or be it at a neighbour 's ?
Where be it ?

and the maid her black silk dress .

I can not quite give up the grocer , because of the jam ! '

The House in the Wood From the German of Grimm .
A poor woodcutter live with his wife and three daughter in a little hut on the border of a great forest .
One morning a he be go to his work , he say to his wife , ` Let our eldest daughter bring me my lunch into the wood ; and so that she shall not lose her way , I will take a bag of millet with me , and sprinkle the seed on the path . '
When the sun have rise high over the forest , the girl set out with a basin of soup .
But the field and wood sparrow , the lark and finch , blackbird and green finch have pick up the millet long ago , and the girl could not find her way .
She go on and on , till the sun set and night come on .
The tree rustle in the darkness , the owl hoot , and she begin to be very much frighten .
Then she saw in tile distance a light that twinkle between the tree .
` There must be people live yonder , ' she think , ` who will take me in for the night , ' and she begin walk towards it .
Not long afterwards she come to a house with light in the window .
She knock at the door , and a gruff voice call , ` Come in ! '
The girl step into the dark entrance , and tap at the door of the room .
` Just walk in , ' cry the voice , and when she open the door there sit an old gray-haired man at the table .
His face be rest on his hand , and his white beard flow over the table almost down to the ground .
By the stove lay three beast , a hen , a cock , and a brindled cow .
The girl tell the old man her story , and ask for a night 's lodging .
The man say : Pretty cock , Pretty hen , And you , pretty brindled cow , What do you say now ?
` Duks , ' answer the beast ; and that must have mean , ` We be quite willing , ' for the old man go on , ` Here be abundance ; go into the back kitchen and cook u a supper . '
The girl find plenty of everything in the kitchen , and cook a good meal , but she do not think of the beast .
She place the full dish on the table , sit down opposite the gray-haired man , and ate till her hunger be appease .
When she be satisfied , she say , ` But now I be so tired , where be a bed in which I can sleep ? '
The beast answer : You have eat with him , You have drink with him , Of u you have not think , Sleep then a you ought !
Then the old man say , ` Go upstairs , and there you will find a bedroom ; shake the bed , and put clean sheet on , and go to sleep . '
The maiden go upstairs , and when she have make the bed , she lay down .
After some time the gray-haired man come , look at her by the light of his candle , and shake his head .
And when he saw that she be sound asleep , he open a trapdoor and let her fall into the cellar .
The woodcutter come home late in the evening , and reproach his wife for leave him all day without food .
` No , I do not , ' she answer ; ` the girl go off with your dinner .
She must have lose her way , but will no doubt come back to-morrow . '
But at daybreak the woodcutter start off into the wood , and this time ask his second daughter to bring his food . '
I will take a bag of lentil , ' say he ; ` they be large than millet , and the girl will see them good and be sure to find her way . '
At midday the maiden take the food , but the lentil have all go ; a on the previous day , the wood bird have eat them all .
The maiden wander about the wood till nightfall , when she come in the same way to the old man 's house , and ask for food and a night 's lodging .
The man with the white hair again ask the beast : Pretty cock , Pretty hen , And you , pretty brindled cow , What do you say now ?
The beast answer , ` Duks , ' and everything happen a on the former day .
The girl cook a good meal , ate and drank with the old man , and do not trouble herself about the animal .
And when she ask for a bed , they reply : You have eat with him You have drink with him , Of u you have not think , Now sleep a you ought !
And when she be asleep , the old man shake his head over her , and let her fall into the cellar .
On the third morning the woodcutter say to his wife , ` Send our young child to-day with my dinner .
She be always good and obedient , and will keep to the right path , and not wander away like her sister , idle drone ! '
But the mother say , ` Must I lose my dear child too ? '
` Do not fear , ' he answer ; ` she be too clever and intelligent to lose her way .
I will take plenty of pea with me and strew them along ; they be even large than lentil , and will show her the way . '
But when the maiden start off with the basket on her arm , the wood pigeon have eat up the pea , and she do not know which way to go .
She be much distress , and think constantly of her poor hungry father and her anxious mother .
At last , when it grow dark , she saw the little light , and come to the house in the wood .
She ask prettily if she might stay there for the night , and the man with the white beard ask his beast again : Pretty cock , Pretty hen , And you , pretty brindled cow , What do you say now ?
` Duks , ' they say .
Then the maiden step up to the stove where the animal be lie , and stroke the cock and the hen , and scratch the brindled cow between it horn .
And when at the bidding of the old man she have prepare a good supper , and the dish be stand on the table , she say , ` Shall I have plenty while the good beast have nothing ?
There be food to spare outside ; I will attend to them first . '
Then she go out and fetch barley and strew it before the cock and hen , and bring the cow an armful of sweet-smelling hay .
` Eat that , dear beast , ' she say , ' and when you be thirsty you shall have a good drink . '
Then she fetch a bowl of water , and the cock and hen fly on to the edge , put their beak in , and then hold up their head a bird do when they drink , and the brindled cow also drink her fill .
When the beast be satisfied , the maiden sit down beside the old man at the table and eat what be leave for her .
Soon the cock and hen begin to tuck their head under their wing , and the brindled cow blink it eye , so the maiden say , ` Shall we not go to rest now ? '
Pretty cock , Pretty hen , And you , pretty brindled cow , What do you say now ?
The animal say , ` Duks : You have eat with u , You have drink with u , You have tend u right , So we wish you good night . '
The maiden therefore go upstairs , make the bed and put on clean sheet and fell asleep .
She sleep peacefully till midnight , when there be such a noise in the house that she awake .
Everything tremble and shake ; the animal spring up and dash themselves in terror against the wall ; the beam sway a if they would be tear from their foundation , it seem a if the stair be tumble down , and then the roof fell in with a crash .
Then all become still , and a no harm come to the maiden she lay down again and fell asleep .
But when she awake again in broad daylight , what a sight meet her eye !
She be lie in a splendid room furnish with royal splendour ; the wall be cover with golden flower on a green ground ; the bed be of ivory and the counterpane of velvet , and on a stool near by lay a pair of slipper stud with pearl .
The maiden think she must be dream , but in come three servant richly dress , who ask what be her command .
` Go , ' say the maiden , ' I will get up at once and cook the old man 's supper for him , and then I will fee the pretty cock and hen and the brindled cow . '
But the door open and in come a handsome young man , who say , ' I be a king 's son , and be condemn by a wicked witch to live a an old man in this wood with no company but that of my three servant , who be transform into a cock , a hen , and a brindled cow .
The spell could only be break by the arrival of a maiden who should show herself kind not only to men but to beast .
You be that maiden , and last night at midnight we be free , and this poor house be again transform into my royal palace .
As they stand there the king 's son tell his three servant to go and fetch the maiden 's parent to be present at the wedding feast .
` But where be my two sister ? '
ask the maid . '
I shut them up in the cellar , but in the morning they shall be lead forth into the forest and shall serve a charcoal burner until they have improve , and will never again suffer poor animal to go hungry . '
Uraschimataro and the Turtle From the Japanische Marchen und Sagen , von David Brauns -LRB- Leipzig : Wilhelm Friedrich -RRB- .
There be once a worthy old couple who live on the coast , and support themselves by fish .
They have only one child , a son , who be their pride and joy , and for his sake they be ready to work hard all day long , and never felt tired or discontent with their lot .
This son 's name be Uraschimataro , which mean in Japanese , ` Son of the island , ' and he be a fine well-grown youth and a good fisherman , mind neither wind nor weather .
Not the brave sailor in the whole village dare venture so far out to sea a Uraschimataro , and many a time the neighbour use to shake their head and say to his parent , ` If your son go on be so rash , one day he will try his luck once too often , and the wave will end by swallow him up . '
But Uraschimataro pay no heed to these remark , and a he be really very clever in manage a boat , the old people be very seldom anxious about him .
One beautiful bright morning , a he be haul his well-filled net into the boat , he saw lie among the fish a tiny little turtle .
He be delight with his prize , and throw it into a wooden vessel to keep till he get home , when suddenly the turtle find it voice , and tremblingly beg for it life .
` After all , ' it say , ` what good can I do you ?
I be so young and small , and I would so gladly live a little long .
Be merciful and set me free , and I shall know how to prove my gratitude . '
Now Uraschimataro be very good-natured , and besides , he could never bear to say no , so he pick up the turtle , and put it back into the sea .
Years fly by , and every morning Uraschimataro sail his boat into the deep sea .
But one day a he be make for a little bay between some rock , there arise a fierce whirlwind , which shatter his boat to piece , and she be suck under by the wave .
Uraschimataro himself very nearly share the same fate .
But he be a powerful swimmer , and struggle hard to reach the shore .
Then he saw a large turtle come towards him , and above the howling of the storm he hear what it say : ' I be the turtle whose life you once save .
I will now pay my debt and show my gratitude .
The land be still far distant , and without my help you would never get there .
Climb on my back , and I will take you where you will . '
Uraschimataro do not wait to be ask twice , and thankfully accept his friend 's help .
But scarcely be he seat firmly on the shell , when the turtle propose that they should not return to the shore at once , but go under the sea , and look at some of the wonder that lay hidden there .
Uraschimataro agree willingly , and in another moment they be deep , deep down , with fathom of blue water above their head .
Oh , how quickly they dart through the still , warm sea !
The young man hold tight , and marvel where they be go and how long they be to travel , but for three day they rush on , till at last the turtle stop before a splendid palace , shin with gold and silver , crystal and precious stone , and deck here and there with branch of pale pink coral and glitter pearl .
But if Uraschimataro be astonish at the beauty of the outside , he be strike dumb at the sight of the hall within , which be light by the blaze of fish scale .
` Where have you bring me ? '
he ask his guide in a low voice .
` To the palace of Ringu , the house of the sea god , whose subject we all be , ' answer the turtle . '
I be the first wait maid of his daughter , the lovely princess Otohime , whom you will shortly see . '
Uraschimataro be still so puzzled with the adventure that have befall him , that he wait in a dazed condition for what would happen next .
But the turtle , who have talk so much of him to the princess that she have express a wish to see him , go at once to make know his arrival .
And directly the princess behold him her heart be set on him , and she beg him to stay with her , and in return promise that he should never grow old , neither should his beauty fade .
` Is not that reward enough ? '
she ask , smile , look all the while as fair a the sun itself .
And Uraschimataro say ` Yes , ' and so he stay there .
For how long ?
That he only know later .
His life pass by , and each hour seem happy than the last , when one day there rush over him a terrible longing to see his parent .
He fought against it hard , know how it would grieve the princess , but it grow on him strong and strong , till at length he become so sad that the princess inquire what be wrong .
Then he tell her of the longing he have to visit his old home , and that he must see his parent once more .
The princess be almost frozen with horror , and implore him to stay with her , or something dreadful would be sure to happen .
` You will never come back , and we shall meet again no more , ' she moan bitterly .
But Uraschimataro stand firm and repeat , ` Only this once will I leave you , and then will I return to your side for ever . '
Sadly the princess shake her head , but she answer slowly , ` One way there be to bring you safely back , but I fear you will never agree to the condition of the bargain . ' '
I will do anything that will bring me back to you , ' exclaim Uraschimataro , look at her tenderly , but the princess be silent : she know too well that when he leave her she would see his face no more .
Then she take from a shelf a tiny golden box , and give it to Uraschimataro , pray him to keep it carefully , and above all thing never to open it .
` If you can do this , ' she say a she bid him farewell , ` your friend the turtle will meet you at the shore , and will carry you back to me . '
Uraschimataro thank her from his heart , and swore solemnly to do her bidding .
He hide the box safely in his garment , seat himself on the back of the turtle , and vanish in the ocean path , wave his hand to the princess .
Three day and three night they swim through the sea , and at length Uraschimataro arrive at the beach which lay before his old home .
The turtle bid him farewell , and be go in a moment .
Uraschimataro draw near to the village with quick and joyful step .
He saw the smoke curl through the roof , and the thatch where green plant have thickly sprout .
He hear the child shout and call , and from a window that he pass come the twang of the koto , and everything seem to cry a welcome for his return .
Yet suddenly he felt a pang at his heart a he wander down the street .
After all , everything be change .
Neither men nor house be those he once know .
Quickly he saw his old home ; yes , it be still there , but it have a strange look .
Anxiously he knock at the door , and ask the woman who open it after his parent .
But she do not know their name , and could give him no news of them .
Still more disturbed , he rush to the burying ground , the only place that could tell him what he wish to know .
Here at any rate he would find out what it all meant .
And he be right .
In a moment he stand before the grave of his parent , and the date write on the stone be almost exactly the date when they have lose their son , and he have forsake them for the Daughter of the Sea .
And so he find that since he have deft his home , three hundred year have pass by .
Shuddering with horror at his discovery he turn back into the village street , hop to meet some one who could tell him of the day of old .
But when the man speak , he know he be not dream , though he felt a if he have lose his sens .
In despair he bethink him of the box which be the gift of the princess .
Perhaps after all this dreadful thing be not true .
He might be the victim of some enchanter 's spell , and in his hand lay the counter-charm .
Almost unconsciously he open it , and a purple vapour come pour out .
He hold the empty box in his hand , and a he look he saw that the fresh hand of youth have grow suddenly shrivel , like the hand of an old , old man .
He run to the brook , which flow in a clear stream down from the mountain .
and saw himself reflect a in a mirror .
It be the face of a mummy which look back at him .
Wounded to death , he creep back through the village , and no man know the old , old man to be the strong handsome youth who have run down the street an hour before .
So he toil wearily back , till he reach the shore , and here he sit sadly on a rock , and call loudly on the turtle .
But she never come back any more , but instead , death come soon , and set him free .
But before that happen , the people who saw him sit lonely on the shore have hear his story , and when their child be restless they use to tell them of the good son who from love to his parent have give up for their sake the splendour and wonder of the palace in the sea , and the most beautiful woman in the world besides .
The Slaying of the Tanuki From the Japanische Murchen und Sagen .
Near a big river , and between two high mountain , a man and his wife live in a cottage a long , long time ago .
A dense forest lay all round the cottage , and there be hardly a path or a tree in the whole wood that be not familiar to the peasant from his boyhood .
In one of his wandering he have make friend with a hare , and many an hour the two pass together , when the man be rest by the roadside , eat his dinner .
Now this strange friendship be observe by the Tanuki , a wicked , quarrelsome beast , who hat the peasant , and be never tire of do him an ill turn .
Again and again he have creep to the hut , and find some choice morsel put away for the little hare , have either eat it if he think it nice , or trample it to piece so that no one else should get it , and at last the peasant lose patience , and make up his mind he would have the Tanuki 's blood .
So for many day the man lay hidden , wait for the Tanuki to come by , and when one morning he march up the road thinking of nothing but the dinner he be go to steal , the peasant throw himself upon him and bind his four leg tightly , so that he could not move .
Then he drag his enemy joyfully to the house , feel that at length he have get the good of the mischievous beast which have do him so many ill turn .
` He shall pay for them with his skin , ' he say to his wife .
` We will first kill him , and then cook him . '
So say , he hang the Tanuki , head downwards , to a beam , and go out to gather wood for a fire .
Meanwhile the old woman be stand at the mortar pound the rise that be to serve them for the week with a pestle that make her arm ache with it weight .
Suddenly she hear something whining and weeping in the corner , and , stop her work , she look round to see what it be .
That be all that the rascal want , and he put on directly his most humble air , and beg the woman in his soft voice to loosen his bond , which her hurt him sorely .
She be fill with pity for him , but do not dare to set him free , a she know that her husband would be very angry .
The Tanuki , however , do not despair , and see that her heart be soften , begin his prayer anew .
` He only ask to have his bond take from him , ' he say .
` He would give his word not to attempt to escape , and if he be once set free he could soon pound her rice for her . '
` Then you can have a little rest , ' he go on , ` for rice pounding be very tiring work , and not at all fit for weak woman . '
These last word melt the good woman completely , and she unfasten the bond that hold him .
Poor foolish creature !
In one moment the Tanuki have seize her , strip off all her clothes , and pop her in the mortar .
In a few minute more she be pound as fine a the rice ; and not content with that , the Tanuki place a pot on the hearth and make ready to cook the peasant a dinner from the flesh of his own wife !
When everything be complete he look out of the door , and saw the old man come from the forest carry a large bundle of wood .
Quick a lightning the Tanuki not only put on the woman 's clothes , but , a he be a magician , assume her form as well .
Then he take the wood , kindle the fire , and very soon set a large dinner before the old man , who be very hungry , and have forget for the moment all about his enemy .
But when the Tanuki saw that he have eat his fill and would be think about his prisoner , he hastily shake off the clothes behind a door and take his own shape .
Then he say to the peasant , ` You be a nice sort of person to seize animal and to talk of kill them !
You be catch in your own net .
It be your own wife that you have eat , and if you want to find her bone you have only to look under the floor . '
With these word he turn and make for the forest .
The old peasant grow cold with horror a he listen , and seem frozen to the place where he stand .
When he have recover himself a little , he collect the bone of his dead wife , bury them in the garden , and swore over the grave to be avenge on the Tanuki .
After everything be do he sit himself down in his lonely cottage and weep bitterly , and the bitter thought of all be that he would never be able to forget that he have eat his own wife .
While he be thus weep and wail his friend the hare pass by , and , hear the noise , prick up his ear and soon recognise the old man 's voice .
He wonder what have happen , and put his head in at the door and ask if anything be the matter .
With tear and groan the peasant tell him the whole dreadful story , and the hare , fill with anger and compassion , comfort him a best he could , and promise to help him in his revenge .
` The false knave shall not go unpunished , ' say he .
So the first thing he do be to search the house for material to make an ointment , which he sprinkle plentifully with pepper and then put in his pocket .
Next he take a hatchet , bade farewell to the old man , and depart to the forest .
He bend his step to the dwelling of the Tanuki and knock at the door .
The Tanuki , who have no cause to suspect the hare , be greatly pleased to see him , for he notice the hatchet at once , and begin to lay plot how to get hold of it .
To do this he think he have well offer to accompany the hare , which be exactly what the hare wish and expect , for he know all the Tanuki 's cunning , and understand his little way .
So he accept the rascal 's company with joy , and make himself very pleasant a they stroll along .
When they be wander in this manner through the forest the hare carelessly raise his hatchet in passing , and cut down some thick bough that be hang over the path , but at length , after cut down a good big tree , which cost him many hard blow , he declare that it be too heavy for him to carry home , and he must just leave it where it be .
This delight the greedy Tanuki , who say that they would be no weight for him , so they collect the large branch , which the hare bound tightly on his back .
Then he trot gaily to the house , the hare follow after with his lighter bundle .
By this time the hare have decide what he would do , and as soon a they arrive , he quietly set on fire the wood on the back of the Tanuki .
The Tanuki , who be busy with something else , observe nothing , and only call out to ask what be the meaning of the crackling that he hear .
` It be just the rattle of the stone which be roll down the side of the mountain , ' the hare say ; and the Tanuki be content , and make no further remark , never notice that the noise really spring from the burn bough on his back , until his fur be in flame , and it be almost too late to put it out .
Shrieking with pain , he let fall the burn wood from his back , and stamp and howl with agony .
But the hare comfort him , and tell him that he always carry with him an excellent plaster in case of need , which would bring him instant relief , and take out his ointment he spread it on a leaf of bamboo , and lay it on the wound .
No sooner do it touch him than the Tanuki leapt yell into the air , and the hare laugh , and run to tell his friend the peasant what a trick he have play on their enemy .
But the old man shake his head sadly , for he know that the villain be only crush for the moment , and that he would shortly be revenge himself upon them .
No , the only way every to get any peace and quiet be to render the Tanuki harmless for ever .
Long do the old man and the hare puzzle together how this be to be do , and at last they decide that they would make two boat , a small one of wood and a large one of clay .
Then they fell to work at once , and when the boat be ready and properly paint , the hare go to the Tanuki , who be still very ill , and invite him to a great fish-catching .
The Tanuki be still feel angry with the hare about the trick he have play him , but he be weak and very hungry , so he gladly accept the proposal , and accompany the hare to the bank of the river , where the two boat be moor , rock by the wave .
They both look exactly alike , and the Tanuki only saw that one be big than the other , and would hold more fish , so he spring into the large one , while the hare climb into the one which be make of wood .
They loosen their mooring , and make for the middle of the stream , and when they be at some distance from the bank , the hare take his oar , and strike such a heavy blow at the other boat , that it break in two .
The Tanuki fell straight into the water , and be hold there by the hare till he be quite dead .
Then he put the body in his boat and row to land , and tell the old man that his enemy be dead at last .
And the old man rejoice that his wife be avenge , and he take the hare into his house , and they live together all their day in peace and quietness upon the mountain .
The Flying Trunk Translated from the German of Hans Andersen .
There be once a merchant who be so rich that he could have pave the whole street , and perhaps even a little side-street besides , with silver .
But he do not do that ; he know another way of spend his money .
If he spend a shilling he get back a florin-such an excellent merchant he be till he die .
Now his son inherit all this money .
He live very merrily ; he go every night to the theatre , make paper kit out of five-pound note , and play duck and drake with sovereigns instead of stone .
In this way the money be likely to come soon to an end , and so it do .
At last he have nothing leave but four shilling , and he have no clothes except a pair of slipper and an old dressing-gown .
His friend do not trouble themselves any more about him ; they would not even walk down the street with him .
But one of them who be rather good-natured send him an old trunk with the message , ` Pack up ! ''
That be all very well , but he have nothing to pack up , so he get into the trunk himself .
It be an enchanted trunk , for as soon a the lock be press it could fly .
He press it , and away he fly in it up the chimney , high into the cloud , further and further away .
But whenever the bottom give a little creak he be in terror lest the trunk should go to piece , for then he would have turn a dreadful somersault-just think of it !
In this way he arrive at the land of the Turks .
He hide the trunk in a wood under some dry leaf , and then walk into the town .
He could do that quite well , for all the Turks be dress just a he was-in a dressing-gown and slipper .
He meet a nurse with a little child .
` Halloa !
you Turkish nurse , ' say he , ` what be that great castle there close to the town ?
The one with the window so high up ? '
` The sultan 's daughter live there , ' she reply .
` It be prophesy that she will be very unlucky in her husband , and so no one be allow to see her except when the sultan and sultana be by . '
` Thank you , ' say the merchant 's son , and he go into the wood , sit himself in his trunk , fly on to the roof , and creep through the window into the princess 's room .
She be lie on the sofa asleep , and be so beautiful that the young merchant have to kiss her .
Then she wake up and be very much frighten , but he say he be a Turkish god who have come through the air to see her , and that please her very much .
They sit close to each other , and he tell her a story about her eye .
They be beautiful dark lake in which her thought swim about like mermaid .
And her forehead be a snowy mountain , grand and shin .
These be lovely story .
Then he ask the princess to marry him , and she say yes at once .
` But you must come here on Saturday , ' she say , ` for then the sultan and the sultana be come to tea with me .
They will be indeed proud that I receive the god of the Turks .
But mind you have a really good story ready , for my parent like them immensely .
My mother like something rather moral and high-flown , and my father like something merry to make him laugh . '
` Yes , I shall only bring a fairy story for my dowry , ' say he , and so they part .
But the princess give him a sabre set with gold piece which he could use .
Then he fly away , buy himself a new dressing-gown , and sit down in the wood and begin to make up a story , for it have to be ready by Saturday , and that be no easy matter .
When he have it ready it be Saturday .
The sultan , the sultana , and the whole court be at tea with the princess .
He be most graciously receive .
` Will you tell u a story ? '
say the sultana ; ` one that be thoughtful and instructive ? '
` But something that we can laugh at , ' say the sultan .
` Oh , certainly , ' he reply , and begin : ` Now , listen attentively .
There be once a box of match which lay between a tinder-box and an old iron pot , and they tell the story of their youth . '
`` We use to be on the green fir-boughs .
Every morning and evening we have diamond-tea , which be the dew , and the whole day long we have sunshine , and the little bird use to tell u story .
We be very rich , because the other tree only dress in summer , but we have green dress in summer and in winter .
Then the woodcutter come , and our family be split up .
We have now the task of make light for the low people .
That be why we grand people be in the kitchen . '' '
`` My fate be quite different , '' say the iron pot , near which the match lay . '
`` Since I come into the world I have be many time scour , and have cook much .
My only pleasure be to have a good chat with my companion when I be lie nice and clean in my place after dinner . '' '
`` Now you be talk too fast , '' splutter the fire . '
`` Yes , let u decide who be the grandest ! ''
say the match . '
`` No , I do n't like talk about myself , '' say the pot . '
`` Let u arrange an evening 's entertainment .
I will tell the story of my life . '
`` On the Baltic by the Danish shore - '' ` What a beautiful beginning ! ''
say all the plate .
`` That 's a story that will please u all . ''
` And the end be just as good a the beginning .
All the plate clatter for joy . '
`` Now I will dance , '' say the tongs , and she dance .
Oh !
how high she could kick !
` The old chair-cover in the corner split when he saw her .
` The urn would have sing but she say she have a cold ; she could not sing unless she boil .
` In the window be an old quill pen .
There be nothing remarkable about her except that she have be dip too deeply into the ink .
But she be very proud of that . '
`` If the urn will not sing , '' say she , `` outside the door hang a nightingale in a cage who will sing . '' '
`` I do n't think it 's proper , '' say the kettle , `` that such a foreign bird should be hear . '' '
`` Oh , let u have some acting , '' say everyone .
`` Do let u ! ''
` Suddenly the door open and the maid come in .
Everyone be quite quiet .
There be not a sound .
But each pot know what he might have do , and how grand he be .
` The maid take the match and light the fire with them .
How they splutter and flame , to be sure !
`` Now everyone can see , '' they think , `` that we be the grandest !
How we sparkle !
What a light - '' ` But here they be burn out . '
` That be a delightful story ! '
say the sultana . '
I quite feel myself in the kitchen with the match .
Yes , now you shall marry our daughter . '
` Yes , indeed , ' say the sultan , ` you shall marry our daughter on Monday . '
And they treat the young man a one of the family .
The wedding be arrange , and the night before the whole town be illuminate .
Biscuits and gingerbread be throw among the people , the street boys stand on tiptoe cry hurrah and whistle through their finger .
It be all splendid .
` Now I must also give them a treat , ' think the merchant 's son .
And so he buy rocket , cracker , and all the kind of firework you can think of , put them in his trunk , and fly up with them into the air .
Whirr-r-r , how they fizz and blaze !
All the Turks jump so high that their slipper fly above their head ; such a splendid glitter they have never see before .
Now they could quite well understand that it be the god of the Turks himself who be to marry the princess .
As soon a the young merchant come down again into the wood with his trunk he think , ` Now I will just go into the town to see how the show have take . '
And it be quite natural that he should want to do this .
Oh !
what stories the people have to tell !
Each one whom he ask have see it differently , but they have all find it beautiful . '
I saw the Turkish god himself , ' say one .
` He have eye like glitter star , and a beard like foam water . '
` He fly away in a cloak of fire , ' say another .
They be splendid thing that he hear , and the next day be to be his wed day .
Then he go back into the wood to sit in his trunk ; but what have become of it ?
The trunk have be burnt .
A spark of the firework have set it alight , and the trunk be in ash .
He could no longer fly , and could never reach his bride .
She stand the whole day long on the roof and wait ; perhaps she be wait there still .
But he wander through the world and told story ; though they be not so merry a the one he tell about the match .
The Snow-man Translated from the German of Hans Andersen .
` How astonishingly cold it be !
My body be crack all over ! '
say the Snow-man .
` The wind be really cut one 's very life out !
And how that fiery thing up there glare ! '
He mean the sun , which be just set .
` It sha 'n ' t make me blink , though , and I shall keep quite cool and collect . '
Instead of eye he have two large three-cornered piece of slate in his head ; his mouth consist of an old rake , so that he have teeth as well .
He be bear amidst the shout and laughter of the boy , and greet by the jingling bell and crack whip of the sledge .
The sun go down , the full moon rise , large , round , clear and beautiful , in the dark blue sky .
` There it be again on the other side ! '
say the Snow-man , by which he mean the sun be appear again . '
I have become quite accustomed to it glaring .
I hope it will hang there and shine , so that I may be able to see myself .
I wish I know , though , how one ought to see about change one 's position .
I should very much like to move about .
If I only could , I would glide up and down the ice there , a I saw the boy do ; but somehow or other , I do n't know how to run . '
` Bow-wow ! '
bark the old yard-dog ; he be rather hoarse and could n't bark very well .
His hoarseness come on when he be a house-dog and use to lie in front of the stove .
` The sun will soon teach you to run !
I saw that last winter with your predecessor , and far back still with his predecessor !
They have all run away ! ' '
I do n't understand you , my friend , ' say the Snow-man .
` That thing up there be to teach me to run ? '
He mean the moon .
` Well , it certainly do run just now , for I saw it quite plainly over there , and now here it be on this side . '
` You know nothing at all about it , ' say the yard-dog .
` Why , you have only just be make .
The thing you see there be the moon ; the other thing you saw go down the other side be the sun .
He will come up again tomorrow morning , and will soon teach you how to run away down the gutter .
The weather be go to change ; I feel it already by the pain in my left hind-leg ; the weather be certainly go to change . ' '
I ca n't understand him , ' say the Snow-man ; ` but I have an idea that he be speak of something unpleasant .
That thing that glare so , and then disappears , the sun , a he call it , be not my friend .
I know that by instinct . '
` Bow-wow ! '
bark the yard-dog , and walk three time round himself , and then creep into his kennel to sleep .
The weather really do change .
Towards morning a dense damp fog lay over the whole neighbourhood ; later on come an icy wind , which send the frost packing .
But when the sun rise , it be a glorious sight .
The tree and shrub be cover with rime , and look like a wood of coral , and every branch be thick with long white blossom .
The most delicate twig , which be lose among the foliage in summer-time , come now into prominence , and it be like a spider 's web of glisten white .
The lady-birches wave in the wind ; and when the sun shone , everything glitter and sparkle a if it be sprinkle with diamond dust , and great diamond be lie on the snowy carpet .
` Is n't it wonderful ? '
exclaim a girl who be walk with a young man in the garden .
They stop near the Snow-man , and look at the glistening tree .
` Summer can not show a more beautiful sight , ' she say , with her eye shin .
` And one ca n't get a fellow like this in summer either , ' say the young man , point to the Snow-man .
` He 's a beauty ! '
The girl laugh , and nod to the Snow-man , and then they both dance away over the snow .
` Who be those two ? '
ask the Snow-man of the yard-dog .
` You have be in this yard long than I have .
Do you know who they be ? '
` Do I know them indeed ? '
answer the yard-dog .
` She have often stroke me , and he have give me bone .
I do n't bite either of them ! '
` But what be they ? '
ask the Snow-man .
` Lovers ! '
reply the yard-dog .
` They will go into one kennel and gnaw the same bone ! '
` Are they the same kind of being that we be ? '
ask the Snow-man .
` They be our master , ' answer the yard-dog .
` Really people who have only be in the world one day know very little . '
That 's the conclusion I have come to .
Now I have age and wisdom ; I know everyone in the house , and I can remember a time when I be not lie here in a cold kennel .
Bow-wow ! '
` The cold be splendid , ' say the Snow-man .
` Tell me some more .
But do n't rattle your chain so , it make me crack ! '
` Bow-wow ! '
bark the yard-dog .
` They use to say I be a pretty little fellow ; then I lay in a velvet-covered chair in my master 's house .
My mistress use to nurse me , and kiss and fondle me , and call me her dear , sweet little Alice !
But by-and-by I grow too big , and I be give to the housekeeper , and I go into the kitchen .
You can see into it from where you be stand ; you can look at the room in which I be master , for so I be when I be with the housekeeper .
Of course it be a small place than upstairs , but it be more comfortable , for I be n't chase about and tease by the child a I have be before .
My food be just as good , or even good .
I have my own pillow , and there be a stove there , which at this time of year be the most beautiful thing in the world .
I use to creep right under that stove .
Ah me !
I often dream of that stove still !
Bow-wow ! '
` Is a stove so beautiful ? '
ask the Snow-man .
` Is it anything like me ? '
` It be just the opposite of you !
It be coal-black , and have a long neck with a brass pipe .
It eat firewood , so that fire spout out of it mouth .
One have to keep close beside it-quite underneath be the nice of all .
You can see it through the window from where you be stand . '
And the Snow-man look in that direction , and saw a smooth polished object with a brass pipe .
The flicker from the fire reach him across the snow .
The Snow-man felt wonderfully happy , and a feeling come over him which he could not express ; but all those who be not snow-men know about it .
` Why do you leave her ? '
ask the Snow-man .
He have a feeling that such a be must be a lady .
` How could you leave such a place ? ' '
I have to ! '
say the yard-dog .
` They turn me out of door , and chain me up here .
I have bite the young boy in the leg , because he take away the bone I be gnaw ; a bone for a bone , I think !
But they be very angry , and from that time I have be chain here , and I have lose my voice .
Do n't you hear how hoarse I be ?
Bow-wow !
I ca n't speak like other dog .
Bow-wow !
That be the end of happiness ! '
The Snow-man , however , be not listen to him any more ; he be look into the room where the housekeeper live , where the stove stand on it four iron leg , and seem to be just the same size a the Snow-man .
` How something be crack inside me ! '
he say .
` Shall I never be able to get in there ?
It be certainly a very innocent wish , and our innocent wish ought to be fulfil .
I must get there , and lean against the stove , if I have to break the window first ! '
` You will never get inside there ! '
say the yard-dog ; ` and if you be to reach the stove you would disappear .
Bow-wow ! '
` I 'm as good a go already ! '
answer the Snow-man . '
I believe I 'm break up ! '
The whole day the Snow-man look through the window ; towards dusk the room grow still more inviting ; the stove give out a mild light , not at all like the moon or even the sun ; no , a only a stove can shine , when it have something to fee upon .
When the door of the room be open , it flare up-this be one of it peculiarity ; it flicker quite red upon the Snow-man 's white face . '
I ca n't stand it any longer ! '
he say .
` How beautiful it look with it tongue stretch out like that ! '
It be a long night , but the Snow-man do not find it so ; there he stand , wrapt in his pleasant thought , and they freeze , so that he crack .
Next morning the pane of the kitchen window be cover with ice , and the most beautiful ice-flowers that even a snow-man could desire , only they blot out the stove .
The window would not open ; he could n't see the stove which he think be such a lovely lady .
There be a cracking and crack inside him and all around ; there be just such a frost a a snow-man would delight in .
But this Snow-man be different : how could he feel happy ?
` Yours be a bad illness for a Snow-man ! '
say the yard-dog . '
I also suffer from it , but I have get over it .
Bow-wow ! '
he bark .
` The weather be go to change ! '
he add .
The weather do change .
There come a thaw .
When this set in the Snow-man set off .
He do not say anything , and he do not complain , and those be bad sign .
One morning he break up altogether .
And lo !
where he have stand there remain a broomstick stand upright , round which the boy have build him !
` Ah !
now I understand why he love the stove , ' say the yard-dog .
` That be the raker they use to clean out the stove !
The Snow-man have a stove-raker in his body !
That 's what be the matter with him !
And now it 's all over with him !
Bow-wow ! '
And before long it be all over with the winter too !
` Bow-wow ! '
bark the hoarse yard-dog .
But the young girl sang : Woods , your bright green garment don !
Willows , your woolly glove put on !
Lark and cuckoo , daily sing -- February have bring the spring !
My heart join in your song so sweet ; Come out , dear sun , the world to greet !
And no one thought of the Snow-man .
The Shirt-collar Translated from the German of Hans Andersen .
There be once a fine gentleman whose entire worldly possession consist of a boot-jack and a hair-brush ; but he have the most beautiful shirt-collar in the world , and it be about this that we be go to hear a story .
The shirt-collar be so old that he begin to think about marrying ; and it happen one day that he and a garter come into the wash-tub together .
` Hulloa ! '
say the shirt-collar , ` never before have I see anything so slim and delicate , so elegant and pretty !
May I be permit to ask your name ? ' '
I sha n't tell you , ' say the garter .
` Where be the place of your abode ? '
ask the shirt-collar .
But the garter be of a bashful disposition , and do not think it proper to answer .
` Perhaps you be a girdle ? '
say the shirt-collar , ` an under girdle ?
for I see that you be for use as well a for ornament , my pretty miss ! '
` You ought not to speak to me ! '
say the garter ' ` I 'm sure I have n't give you any encouragement ! '
` When anyone be as beautiful a you , ' say the shirt-collar , ` be not that encouragement enough ? '
` Go away , do n't come so close ! '
say the garter .
` You seem to be a gentleman ! '
` So I be , and a very fine one too ! '
say the shirt-collar ; ' I possess a boot-jack and a hair-brush ! '
That be not true ; it be his master who own these thing ; but he be a terrible boaster .
` Do n't come so close , ' say the garter .
` I 'm not accustom to such treatment ! '
` What affectation ! '
say the shirt-collar .
And then they be take out of the wash-tub , starch , and hung on a chair in the sun to dry , and then lay on the ironing-board .
Then come the glowing iron .
` Mistress widow ! '
say the shirt-collar , ` dear mistress widow !
I be become another man , all my crease be come out ; you be burn a hole in me !
Ugh !
Stop , I implore you ! '
` You rag ! '
say the iron , travel proudly over the shirt-collar , for it think it be a steam engine and ought to be at the station draw truck .
` Rag ! '
it say .
The shirt-collar be rather fray out at the edge , so the scissors come to cut off the thread .
` Oh ! '
say the shirt-collar , ` you must be a dancer !
How high you can kick !
That be the most beautiful thing I have ever see !
No man can imitate you ! ' '
I know that ! '
say the scissors .
` You ought to be a duchess ! '
say the shirt-collar .
` My worldly possession consist of a fine gentleman , a boot-jack , and a hair-brush .
If only I have a duchy ! '
` What !
He want to marry me ? '
say the scissors , and she be so angry that she give the collar a sharp snip , so that it have to be cast aside a good for nothing .
` Well , I shall have to propose to the hair-brush ! '
think the shirt-collar .
` It be really wonderful what fine hair you have , madam !
Have you never think of marry ? '
` Yes , that I have ! '
answer the hair-brush ; ` I 'm engage to the boot-jack ! '
` Engaged ! '
exclaim the shirt-collar .
And now there be no one he could marry , so he take to despise matrimony .
Time pass , and the shirt-collar come in a rag-bag to the paper-mill .
There be a large assortment of rag , the fine one in one heap , and the coarse one in another , a they should be .
They have all much to tell , but no one more than the shirt-collar , for he be a hopeless braggart . '
I have have a terrible number of love affair ! '
he say .
` They give me no peace .
I be such a fine gentleman , so stiff with starch !
I have a boot-jack and a hair-brush , which I never use !
You should just have see me then !
Never shall I forget my first love !
She be a girdle , so delicate and soft and pretty !
She throw herself into a wash-tub for my sake !
Then there be a widow , who glow with love for me .
But I leave her alone , till she become black .
Then there be the dancer , who inflict the wound which have cause me to be here now ; she be very violent !
My own hair-brush be in love with me , and lose all her hair in consequence .
Yes , I have experience much in that line ; but I grieve most of all for the garter , -I mean , the girdle , who throw herself into a wash-tub .
I have much on my conscience ; it be high time for me to become white paper ! '
And so he do !
he become white paper , the very paper on which this story be print .
And that be because he have boast so terribly about thing which be not true .
We should take this to heart , so that it may not happen to u , for we can not indeed tell if we may not some day come to the rag-bag , and be make into white paper , on which will be print our whole history , even the most secret part , so that we too go about the world relate it , like the shirt-collar .
The Princess in the Chest Translated from the Danish .
There be once a king and a queen who live in a beautiful castle , and have a large , and fair , and rich , and happy land to rule over .
From the very first they love each other greatly , and live very happily together , but they have no heir .
They have be marry for seven year , but have neither son nor daughter , and that be a great grief to both of them .
More than once it happen that when the king be in a bad temper , he let it out on the poor queen , and say that here they be now , get old , and neither they nor the kingdom have an heir , and it be all her fault .
This be hard to listen to , and she go and cry and vex herself .
Finally , the king say to her one day , ` This ca n't be borne any longer .
I go about childless , and it 's your fault .
I be go on a journey and shall be away for a year .
If you have a child when I come back again , all will be well , and I shall love you beyond all measure , and never more say an angry word to you .
But if the nest be just a empty when I come home , then I must part with you . '
After the king have set out on his journey , the queen go about in her loneliness , and sorrow and vex herself more than ever .
At last her maid say to her one day , ' I think that some help could be find , if your majesty would seek it . '
Then she tell about a wise old woman in that country , who have help many in trouble of the same kind , and could no doubt help the queen as well , if she would send for her .
The queen do so , and the wise woman come , and to her she confide her sorrow , that she , be childless , and the king and his kingdom have no heir .
The wise woman know help for this .
` Out in the king 's garden , ' say she , ` under the great oak that stand on the left hand , just a one go out from the castle , be a little bush , rather brown than green , with hairy leaf and long spike .
On that bush there be just at this moment three bud .
If your majesty go out there alone , fast , before sunrise , and take the middle one of the three bud , and eat it , then in six month you will bring a princess into the world .
As soon a she be bear , she must have a nurse , whom I shall provide , and this nurse must live with the child in a secluded part of the palace ; no other person must visit the child ; neither the king nor the queen must see it until it be fourteen year old , for that would cause great sorrow and misfortune . '
The queen reward the old woman richly , and next morning , before the sun rise , she be down in the garden , find at once the little bush with the three bud , pluck the middle one and eat it .
It be sweet to taste , but afterwards be as bitter a gall .
Six month after this , she bring into the world a little girl .
There be a nurse in readiness , whom the wise woman have provide , and preparation be make for her living with the child , quite alone , in a secluded wing of the castle , look out on the pleasure-park .
The queen do a the wise woman have tell her ; she give up the child immediately , and the nurse take it and live with it there .
When the king come home and heard that a daughter have be bear to him , he be of course very pleased and happy , and want to see her at once .
The queen have then to tell him this much of the story , that it have be foretell that it would cause great sorrow and misfortune if either he or she get a sight of the child until it have complete it fourteenth year .
This be a long time to wait .
The king long so much to get a sight of his daughter , and the queen no less than he , but she know that it be not like other child , for it could speak immediately after it be bear , and be as wise a old folk .
This the nurse have tell her , for with her the queen have a talk now and again , but there be no one who have ever see the princess .
The queen have also see what the wise woman could do , so she insist strongly that her warning should be obey .
The king often lose his patience , and be determine to see his daughter , but the queen always put him off the idea , and so thing go on , until the very day before the princess complete her fourteenth year .
The king and the queen be out in the garden then , and the king say , ` Now I ca n't and I wo n't wait any long .
I must see my daughter at once .
A few hour , more or less , ca n't make any difference . '
The queen beg him to have patience till the morning .
When they have wait so long , they could surely wait a single day more .
But the king be quite unreasonable .
` No nonsense , ' say he ; ` she be just as much mine a yours , and I will see her , ' and with that he go straight up to her room .
He burst the door open , and push aside the nurse , who try to stop him , and there he saw his daughter .
She be the lovely young princess , red and white , like milk and blood , with clear blue eye and golden hair , but right in the middle of her forehead there be a little tuft of brown hair .
The princess go to meet her father , fell on his neck and kiss him , but with that she say , ' O father , father !
what have you do now ?
to-morrow I must die , and you must choose one of three thing : either the land must be smite with the black pestilence , or you must have a long and bloody war , or you must as soon a I be dead , lay me in a plain wooden chest , and set it in the church , and for a whole year place a sentinel beside it every night . '
The king be frighten indeed , and think she be rave , but in order to please her , he say , ` Well , of these three thing I shall choose the last ; if you die , I shall lay you at once in a plain wooden chest , and have it set in the church , and every night I shall place a sentinel beside it .
But you shall not die , even if you be ill now . '
He immediately summon all the best doctor in the country , and they come with all their prescription and their medicine bottle , but next day the princess be stiff and cold in death .
All the doctor could certify to that and they all put their name to this and append their seal , and then they have do all they could .
The king keep his promise .
The princess 's body be lain the same day in a plain wooden chest , and set in the chapel of the castle , and on that night and every night after it , a sentinel be post in the church , to keep watch over the chest .
The first morning when they come to let the sentinel out , there be no sentinel there .
They think he have just get frighten and run away , and next even a new one be post in the church .
In the morning he be also go .
So it go every night .
When they come in the morning to let the sentinel out , there be no one there , and it be impossible to discover which way he have go if he have run away .
And what should they run away for , every one of them , so that nothing more be over heard or see of them , from the hour that they be set on guard beside the princess 's chest ?
It become now a general belief that the princess 's ghost walk , and eat up all those who be to guard her chest , and very soon there be no one left who would be place on this duty , and the king 's soldier desert the service , before their turn come to be her bodyguard .
The king then promise a large reward to the soldier who would volunteer for the post .
This do for some time , a there be find a few reckless fellow , who wish to earn this good payment .
But they never get it , for in the morning , they too have disappear like the rest .
So it have go on for something like a whole year ; every night a sentinel have be place beside the chest , either by compulsion or of his own free will , but not a single one of the sentinel be to be see , either on the following day or any time thereafter .
And so it have also go with one , on the night before a certain day , when a merry young smith come wander to the town where the king 's castle stood .
It be the capital of the country , and people of every king come to it to get work .
This smith , whose name be Christian , have come for that same purpose .
There be no work for him in the place he belong to , and he want now to seek a place in the capital .
There he enter an inn where he sit down in the public room , and get something to eat .
Some under-officers be sit there , who be out to try to get some one enlist to stand sentry .
They have to go in this way , day after day , and hitherto they have always succeed in find one or other reckless fellow .
But on this day they have , a yet , find no one .
It be too well know how all the sentinel disappear , who be set on that post , and all that they have get hold of have refuse with thanks .
These sit down beside Christian , and order drink , and drink along with him .
Now Christian be a merry fellow who like good company ; he could both drink and sing , and talk and boast as well , when he get a little drop in his head .
He tell these under-officers that he be one of that kind of folk who never be afraid of anything .
Then he be just the kind of man they like , say they , and he might easily earn a good penny , before he be a day old , for the king pay a hundred dollar to anyone who would stand a sentinel in the church all night , beside his daughter 's chest .
Christian be not afraid of that he be n't afraid of anything , so they drink another bottle of wine on this , and Christian go with them up to the colonel , where he be put into uniform with musket , and all the rest , and be then shut up in the church , to stand a sentinel that night .
It be eight o'clock when he take up his post , and for the first hour he be quite proud of his courage ; during the second hour he be well pleased with the large reward that he would get , but in the third hour , when it be get near eleven , the effect of the wine pass off , and he begin to get uncomfortable , for he have hear about this post ; that no one have ever escape alive from it , so far a be know .
But neither do anyone know what have become of all the sentinel .
The thought of this ran in his head so much , after the wine be out of it , that he search about everywhere for a way of escape , and finally , at eleven o'clock , he find a little postern in the steeple which be not lock , and out at this he creep , intend to run away .
At the same moment a he put his foot outside the church door , he saw stand before him a little man , who say , ` Good evening , Christian , where be you go ? '
With that he felt a if he be root to the spot and could not move .
` Nowhere , ' say he .
` Oh , yes , ' say the little man , ` You be just about to run away , but you have take upon you to stand sentinel in the church to-night , and there you must stay . '
Christian say , very humbly , that he dare not , and therefore want to get away , and beg to be let go .
` No , ' say the little one , ` you must remain at your post , but I shall give you a piece of good advice ; you shall go up into the pulpit , and remain stand there .
You need never mind what you see or hear , it will not be able to do you any harm , if you remain in your place until you hear the lid of the chest slam down again behind the dead ; then all danger be past , and you can go about the church , wherever you please . '
The little man then push him in at the door again , and lock it after him .
Christian make haste to get up into the pulpit , and stand there , without notice anything , until the clock strike twelve .
Then the lid of the princess 's chest spring up , and out of it there come something like the princess , dress a you see in the picture .
It shriek and howl , ` Sentry , where be you ?
Sentry , where be you ?
If you do n't come , you shall get the most cruel death anyone have ever get . '
It go all round the church , and when it finally catch sight of the smith , up in the pulpit , it come rush thither and mount the step .
But it could not get up the whole way , and for all that it stretch and strain , it could not touch Christian , who meanwhile stand and tremble up in the pulpit .
When the clock strike one , the appearance have to go back into the chest again , and Christian hear the lid slam after it .
After this there be dead silence in the church .
He lay down where he be and fell asleep , and do not awake before it be bright daylight , and he hear step outside , and the noise of the key be put into the lock .
Then he come down from the pulpit , and stand with his musket in front of the princess 's chest .
It be the colonel himself who come with the patrol , and he be not a little surprised when he find the recruit safe and sound .
He want to have a report , but Christian would give him none , so he take him straight up to the king , and announce for the first time that here be the sentinel who have stand guard in the church over-night .
The king immediately get out of bed , and lay the hundred dollar for him on the table , and then want to question him .
` Have you see anything ? '
say he .
` Have you see my daughter ? ' '
I have stand at my post , ' say the young smith , ` and that be quite enough ; I undertake nothing more . '
He be not sure whether he dare tell what he have see and hear , and besides he be also a little conceited because he have do what no other man have be able to do , or have have courage for .
The king profess to be quite satisfied , and ask him whether he would engage himself to stand on guard again the following night .
` No , thank you , ' say Christian , ' I will have no more of that ! '
` As you please , ' say the king , ` you have behave like a brave fellow , and now you shall have your breakfast .
You must be need something to strengthen you after that turn . '
The king have breakfast lay for him , and sit down at the table with him in person ; he keep constantly fill his glass for him and praise him , and drink his health .
Christian need no pressing , but do full justice both to the food and drink , and not least to the latter .
Finally he grow bold , and say that if the king would give him two hundred dollar for it , he be his man to stand sentry next night as well .
When this be arrange , Christian bid him ` Good-day , ' and go down among the guard , and then out into the town along with other soldier and under-officers .
He have his pocket full of money , and treat them , and drank with them and boast and make game of the good-for-nothing who be afraid to stand on guard , because they be frighten that the dead princess would eat them .
See whether she have eat him !
So the day pass in mirth and glee , but when eight o'clock come , Christian be again shut up in the church , all alone .
Before he have be there two hour , he get tire of it , and think only of get away .
He find a little door behind the altar which be not lock , and at ten o'clock he slip out at it , and take to his heel and make for the beach .
He have get half-way thither , when all at once the same little man stand in front of him and say , ` Good evening , Christian , where be you go ? '
` I 've leave to go where I please , ' say the smith , but at the same time he notice that he could not move a foot .
` No , you have undertake to keep guard to-night a well , ' say the little man , ` and you must attend to that . '
He then take hold of him , and however unwilling he be , Christian have to go with him right back to the same little door that he have creep out at .
When they get there , the little man say to him , ` Go in front of the altar now , and take in your hand the book that be lie there .
There you shall stay till you hear the lid of the chest slam down over the dead .
In that way you will come to no harm . '
With that the little man shove him in at the door , and lock it .
Christian then immediately go in front of the altar , and take the book in his hand , and stand thus until the clock strike twelve , and the appearance spring out of the chest .
` Sentry , where be you ?
Sentry , where be you ? '
it shriek , and then rush to the pulpit , and right up into it .
But there be no one there that night .
Then it howl and shriek again , My father have set no sentry in , War and Pest this night begin .
At the same moment , it notice the smith standing in front of the altar , and come rush towards him .
` Are you there ? '
it scream ; ` now I 'll catch you . '
But it could not come up over the step in front of the altar , and there it continue to howl , and scream , and threaten , until the clock strike one , when it have to go into the chest again , and Christian hear the lid slam above it .
That night , however , it have not the same appearance a on the previous one ; it be less ugly .
When all be quiet in the church , the smith lay down before the altar and sleep calmly till the following morning , when the colonel come to fetch him .
He be take up to the king again , and thing go on a the day before .
He get his money , but would give no explanation whether he have see the king 's daughter , and he would not take the post again , he say .
But after he have get a good breakfast , and taste well of the king 's wine , he undertake to go on guard again the third night , but he would not do it for less than the half of the kingdom , he say , for it be a dangerous post , and the king have to agree , and promise him this .
The remainder of the day go like the previous one .
He play the boastful soldier , and the merry smith , and he have comrade and boon-companions in plenty .
At eight o'clock he have to put on his uniform again , and be shut up in the church .
He have not be there for an hour before he have come to his sens , and think , ` It 's best to stop now , while the game be go well . '
The third night , he be sure , would be the bad ; he have be drunk when he promise it , and the half of the kingdom , the king could never have be in earnest about that !
So he decide to leave , without wait so long a on the previous night .
In that way he would escape the little man who have watch him before .
All the door and postern be lock , but he finally though of creep up to a window , and open that , and a the clock strike nine , he creep out there .
It be fairly high in the wall , but he get to the ground with no bone break , and start to run .
He get down to the shore without meet anyone , and there he get into a boat , and push off from land .
He laugh immensely to himself at the thought of how cleverly he have manage and how he have cheat the little man .
Just then he hear a voice from the shore , ` Good evening , Christian , where be you go ? '
He give no answer .
` To-night your leg will be too short , ' he think , and pull at the oar .
But he then felt something lay hold of the boat , and drag it straight in to shore , for all that he sit and struggle with the oar .
The man then lay hold of him , and say , ` You must remain at your post , a you have promise , ' and whether he like it or not , Christian have just to go back with him the whole way to the church .
He could never get in at that window again , Christian say ; it be far too high up .
` You must go in there , and you shall go in there , ' say the little man , and with that he lift him up on to the window-sill .
Then he say to him : ` Notice well now what you have to do .
This evening you must stretch yourself out on the left-hand side of her chest .
The lid open to the right , and she come out to the left .
When she have get out of the chest and pass over you , you must get into it and lie there , and that in a hurry , without her seeing you .
There you must remain lying until day dawn , and whether she threaten you or entreat you , you must not come out of it , or give her any answer .
Then she have no power over you , and both you and she be freed . '
The smith then have to go in at the window , just a he come out , and go and lay himself all his length on the left side of the princess 's chest , close up to it , and there he lay stiff a a rock until the clock strike twelve .
Then the lid spring up to the right , and the princess come out , straight over him , and rush round the church , howl and shriek ` Sentry , where be you ?
Sentry , where be you ? '
She go towards the altar , and right up to it , but there be no one there ; then she scream again , My father have set no sentry in , War and Pest will now begin .
Then she go round the whole church , both up and down , sigh and weep , My father have set no sentry in , War and Pest will now begin .
Then she go away again , and at the same moment the clock in the tower strike one .
Then the smith heard in the church a soft music , which grow louder and louder , and soon fill the whole building .
He hear also a multitude of footstep , a if the church be be fill with people .
He hear the priest go through the service in front of the altar , and there be sing more beautiful than he have ever hear before .
Then he also hear the priest offer up a prayer of thanksgiving because the land have be free from war and pestilence , and from all misfortune , and the king 's daughter deliver from the evil one .
Many voice join in , and a hymn of praise be sing ; then he hear the priest again , and hear his own name and that of the princess , and think that he be be wed to her .
The church be pack full , but he could see nothing .
Then he hear again the many footstep a ol ' folk leave the church , while the music sound fainter and fainter , until it altogether die away .
When it be silent , the light of day begin to break in through the window .
The smith spring up out of the chest and fell on his knee and thank God .
The church be empty , but up in front of the altar lay the princess , white and red , like a human be , but sob and cry , and shake with cold in her white shroud .
The smith take his sentry coat and wrap it round her ; then she dry her tear , and take his hand and thank him , and say that he have now free her from all the sorcery that have be in her from her birth , and which have come over her again when her father break the command against see her until she have complete her fourteenth year .
She say far , that if he who have deliver her would take her in marriage , she would be his .
If not , she would go into a nunnery , and he could marry no other as long a she live , for he be wed to her with the service of the dead , which he have hear .
She be now the most beautiful young princess that anyone could wish to see , and he be now lord of half the kingdom , which have be promise him for stand on guard the third nigh .
So they agree that they would have each other , and love each other all their day .
