To this also the prince say ` Yes . '
When he have go a little way from the castle he meet the fox , and they continue on their journey together .
When they reach the end of it the prince for the third time receive three grain of gold from the fox , with direction to throw one into the guard-chamber , another into the stable , and the third into the horse 's stall .
But the fox tell him that above the horse 's stall hang a beautiful golden saddle , which he must not touch , if he do not want to bring himself into new trouble bad than those he have escape from , for then the fox could help him no longer .
The prince promise to be firm this time .
He throw the grain of gold in the proper place , and untie the horse , but with that he catch sight of the golden saddle , and think that none but it could suit so beautiful a horse , especially a it have golden shoe .
But just a he stretch out his hand to take it he receive from some invisible be so hard a blow on the arm that it be make quite numb .
This recall to him his promise and his danger , so he lead out the horse without look at the golden saddle again .
The fox be wait for him outside the castle , and the prince confess to him that he have very nearly give way to temptation this time as well . '
I know that , ' say the fox , ` for it be I who strike you over the arm . '
As they now go on together the prince say that he could not forget the beautiful princess , and ask the fox whether he do not think that she ought to ride home to his father 's palace on this horse with the golden shoe .
The fox agree that this would be excellent ; if the prince would now go and carry her off he would give him three grain of gold for that purpose .
The prince be quite ready , and promise to keep good command of himself this time , and not kiss her .
He get the grain of gold and enter the castle , where he carry off the princess , set her on the beautiful horse , and hold on his way .
When they come near to the castle where the bird Grip sit in his cage he again ask the fox for three grain of gold .
These he get , and with them he be successful in carry off the bird .
He be now full of joy , for his blind father would now recover his sight , while he himself own the world 's most beautiful princess and the horse with the golden shoe .
The prince and princess travel on together with mirth and happiness , and the fox follow them until they come to the forest where the prince first meet with him .
` Here our way part , ' say the fox .
` You have now get all that your heart desire , and you will have a prosperous journey to your father 's palace if only you do not ransom anyone 's life with money . '
The prince thank the fox for all his help , promise to give heed to his warning , say farewell to him , and rode on , with the princess by his side and the bird Grip on his wrist .
They soon arrive at the inn where the two eldest brother have stay , forget their errand .
But now no merry song or noise of mirth be hear from it .
When the prince come nearer he saw two gallows erect , and when he enter the inn along with the princess he saw that all the room be hang with black , and that everything inside forebode sorrow and death .
He ask the reason of this , and be tell that two prince be to be hang that day for debt ; they have spend all their money in feast and playing , and be now deeply in debt to the host , and a no one could be find to ransom their life they be about to be hang accord to the law .
The prince know that it be his two brother who have thus forfeit their life and it cut him to the heart to think that two prince should suffer such a shameful death ; and , a he have sufficient money with him , he pay their debt , and so ransom their life .
At first the brother be grateful for their liberty , but when they saw the young brother 's treasure they become jealous of his good fortune , and plan how to bring him to destruction , and then take the bird Grip , the princess , and the horse with the golden shoe , and convey them to their blind father .
After they have agree on how to carry out their treachery they entice the prince to a den of lion and throw him down among them .
Then they set the princess on horseback , take the bird Grip , and ride homeward .
The princess weep bitterly , but they tell her that it would cost her her life if she do not say that the two brother have win all the treasure .
When they arrive at their father 's palace there be great rejoicing , and everyone praise the two prince for their courage and bravery .
When the king inquire after the young brother they answer that he have lead such a life in the inn that he have be hang for debt .
The king sorrow bitterly over this , because the young prince be his dear son , and the joy over the treasure soon die away , for the bird Grip would not sing so that the king might recover his sight , the princess weep night and day , and no one dare to venture so close to the horse a to have a look at his golden shoe .
Now when the young prince be throw down into the lion ' den he find the fox sit there , and the lion , instead of tear him to piece , show him the great friendliness .
Nor be the fox angry with him for have forget his last warning .
He only say that son who could so forget their old father and disgrace their royal birth a those have do would not hesitate to betray their brother either .
Then he take the prince up out of the lion 's den and give him directions what to do now so a to come by his right again .
The prince thank the fox with all his heart for his true friendship , but the fox answer that if he have be of any use to him he would now for his own part ask a service of him .
The prince reply that he would do him any service that be in his power . '
I have only one thing to ask of you , ' say the fox , ` and that be , that you should cut off my head with your sword . '
The prince be astonish , and say that he could not bring himself to cut the have off his truest friend , and to this he stick in spite of all the fox 's declaration that it be the great service he could do him .
At this the fox become very sorrowful , and declare that the prince 's refusal to grant his request now compel him to do a deed which he be very unwilling to do -- if the prince would not cut off his head , then he must kill the prince himself .
Then at last the prince draw his good sword and cut off the fox 's head , and the next moment a youth stand before him .
` Thanks , ' say he , ` for this service , which have free me from a spell that not even death itself could loosen .
I be the dead man who lay unburied in the robber 's inn , where you ransom me and give me honourable burial , and therefore I have help you in your journey . '
With this they part and the prince , disguise himself a a horse-shoer , go up to his father 's palace and offer his service there .
The king 's men tell him that a horse-shoer be indeed want at the palace , but he must be one who could lift up the foot of the horse with the golden shoe , and such a one they have not yet be able to find .
The prince ask to see the horse , and as soon a he enter the stable the steed begin to neigh in a friendly fashion , and stand a quiet and still a a lamb while the prince lift up his hoof , one after the other , and show the king 's men the famous golden shoe .
After this the king 's men begin to talk about the bird Grip , and how strange it be that he would not sing , however well he be attend to .
The horse-shoer then say that he know the bird very well ; he have see it when it sit in it cage in another king 's palace , and if it do not sing now it must be because it do not have all that it want .
He himself know so much about the bird 's way that if he only get to see it he could tell at once what it lack .
The king 's men now take counsel whether they ought to take the stranger in before the king , for in his chamber sit the bird Grip along with the weep princess .
It be decide to risk do so , and the horse-shoer be lead into the king 's chamber , where he have no sooner call the bird by it name than it begin to sing and the princess to smile .
Then the darkness clear away from the king 's eye , and the more the bird sing the more clearly do he see , till at last in the strange horse-shoer he recognise his young son .
Then the princess tell the king how treacherously his eldest son have act , and he have them banish from his kingdom ; but the young prince marry the princess , and get the horse with the golden shoe and half the kingdom from his father , who keep for himself so long a he live the bird Grip , which now sing with all it heart to the king and all his court .
Snowflake Slavonic story .
Contes Populaires Slaves , traduits par Louis Leger .
Paris : Leroux , Editeur .
Once upon a time there live a peasant call Ivan , and he have a wife whose name be Marie .
They would have be quite happy except for one thing : they have no child to play with , and a they be now old people they do not find that watch the child of their neighbour at all make up to them for have one of their own .
One winter , which nobody living will ever forget , the snow lay so deep that it come up to the knee of even the tall man .
When it have all fall , and the sun be shin again , the child run out into the street to play , and the old man and his wife sit at their window and gaze at them .
The child first make a sort of little terrace , and stamp it hard and firm , and then they begin to make a snow woman .
Ivan and Marie watch them , the while think about many thing .
Suddenly Ivan 's face brighten , and , look at his wife , he say , ` Wife , why should n't we make a snow woman too ? '
` Why not ? '
reply Marie , who happen to be in a very good temper ; ` it might amuse u a little .
But there be no use make a woman .
Let u make a little snow child , and pretend it be a live one . '
` Yes , let u do that , ' say Ivan , and he take down his cap and go into the garden with his old wife .
Then the two set to work with all their might to make a doll out of the snow .
They shape a little body and two little hand and two little foot .
On top of all they place a ball of snow , out of which the head be to be .
` What in the world be you do ? '
ask a passer-by .
` Ca n't you guess ? '
return Ivan .
` Making a snow-child , ' reply Marie .
They have finish the nose and the chin .
Two hole be leave for the eye , and Ivan carefully shape out the mouth .
No sooner have he do so than he felt a warm breath upon his cheek .
He start back in surprise and look -- and behold !
the eye of the child meet his , and it lip , which be as red a raspberry , smile at him !
` What be it ? '
cry Ivan , cross himself .
` Am I mad , or be the thing bewitch ? '
The snow-child bent it head a if it have be really alive .
It move it little arm and it little leg in the snow that lay about it just a the living child do theirs .
` Ah !
Ivan , Ivan , ' exclaim Marie , tremble with joy , ` heaven have send u a child at last ! '
And she throw herself upon Snowflake -LRB- for that be the snow-child 's name -RRB- and cover her with kiss .
And the loose snow fell away from Snowflake a an egg shell do from an egg , and it be a little girl whom Marie hold in her arm .
` Oh !
my darling Snowflake ! '
cry the old woman , and lead her into the cottage .
And Snowflake grow fast ; each hour as well a each day make a difference , and every day she become more and more beautiful .
The old couple hardly know how to contain themselves for joy , and thought of nothing else .
The cottage be always full of village child , for they amuse Snowflake , and there be nothing in the world they would not have do to amuse her .
She be their doll , and they be continually invent new dress for her , and teach her song or play with her .
Nobody know how clever she be !
She notice everything , and could learn a lesson in a moment .
Anyone would have take her for thirteen at least !
And , besides all that , she be so good and obedient ; and so pretty , too !
Her skin be as white a snow , her eye a blue a forget-me-nots , and her hair be long and golden .
Only her cheek have no colour in them , but be as fair a her forehead .
So the winter go on , till at last the spring sun mount higher in the heaven and begin to warm the earth .
The grass grow green in the field , and high in the air the lark be heard sing .
The village girl meet and dance in a ring , singing , ` Beautiful spring , how come you here ?
How come you here ?
Did you come on a plough , or be it a harrow ? '
Only Snowflake sit quite still by the window of the cottage .
` What be the matter , dear child ? '
ask Marie .
` Why be you so sad ?
Are you ill ?
or have they treat you unkindly ? '
` No , ' reply Snowflake , ` it be nothing , mother ; no one have hurt me ; I be well . '
The spring sun have chase away the last snow from it hide place under the hedge ; the field be full of flower ; nightingale sing in the tree , and all the world be gay .
But the gayer grow the bird and the flower the sadder become Snowflake .
She hide herself from her playmate , and curl herself up where the shadow be deepest , like a lily amongst it leaf .
Her only pleasure be to lie amid the green willow near some sparkling stream .
At the dawn and at twilight only she seem happy .
When a great storm break , and the earth be white with hail , she become bright and joyous a the Snowflake of old ; but when the cloud pass , and the hail melt beneath the sun , Snowflake would burst into tear and weep a a sister would weep over her brother .
The spring pass , and it be the eve of St. John , or Midsummer Day .
This be the great holiday of the year , when the young girl meet in the wood to dance and play .
They go to fetch Snowflake , and say to Marie : ` Let her come and dance with u . '
But Marie be afraid ; she could not tell why , only she could not bear the child to go .
Snowflake do not wish to go either , but they have no excuse ready .
So Marie kiss the girl and say : ` Go , my Snowflake , and be happy with your friend , and you , dear child , be careful of her .
You know she be the light of my eye to me . '
` Oh , we will take care of her , ' cry the girl gaily , and they run off to the wood .
There they wear wreath , gather nosegay , and sing song some sad , some merry .
And whatever they do Snowflake do too .
When the sun set they light a fire of dry grass , and place themselves in a row , Snowflake be the last of all .
` Now , watch u , ' they say , ` and run just a we do . '
And they all begin to sing and to jump one after another across the fire .
Suddenly , close behind them , they hear a sigh , then a groan .
` Ah ! '
They turn hastily and look at each other .
There be nothing .
They look again .
Where be Snowflake ?
She have hide herself for fun , they think , and search for her everywhere .
` Snowflake !
Snowflake ! '
But there be no answer .
` Where can she be ?
Oh , she must have go home . '
They return to the village , but there be no Snowflake .
For day after that they seek her high and low .
They examine every bush and every hedge , but there be no Snowflake .
And long after everyone else have give up hope Ivan and Marie would wander through the wood cry ` Snowflake , my dove , come back , come back ! '
And sometimes they think they hear a call , but it be never the voice of Snowflake .
And what have become of her ?
Had a fierce wild beast seize her and drag her into his lair in the forest ?
Had some bird carry her off across the wide blue sea ?
No , no beast have touch her , no bird have bear her away .
With the first breath of flame that sweep over her when she run with her friend Snowflake have melt away , and a little soft haze float upwards be all that remain of her .
I Know What I Have Learned From the Danish .
There be once a man who have three daughter , and they be all marry to troll , who live underground .
One day the man think that he would pay them a visit , and his wife give him some dry bread to eat by the way .
After he have walk some distance he grow both tired and hungry , so he sit down on the east side of a mound and begin to eat his dry bread .
The mound then open , and his young daughter come out of it , and say , ` Why , father !
why be you not come in to see me ? '
` Oh , ' say he , ` if I have know that you live here , and have see any entrance , I would have come in . '
Then he enter the mound along with her .
The troll come home soon after this , and his wife tell him that her father be come , and ask him to go and buy some beef to make broth with .
` We can get it easy than that ! '
say the troll .
He fix an iron spike into one of the beam of the roof , and run his head against this till he have knock several large piece off his head .
He be just as well a ever after do this , and they get their broth without further trouble .
The troll then give the old man a sackful of money , and laden with this he betook himself homewards .
When he come near his home he remember that he have a cow about to calve , so he lay down the money on the ground , run home as fast a he could , and ask his wife whether the cow have calve yet .
` What kind of a hurry be this to come home in ? '
say she .
` No , the cow have not calve yet . '
` Then you must come out and help me in with a sackful of money , ' say the man . '
A sackful of money ? '
cry his wife .
` Yes , a sackful of money , ' say he .
` Is that so very wonderful ? '
His wife do not believe very much what he tell her , but she humour him , and go out with him .
When they come to the spot where he have leave it there be no money there ; a thief have come along and steal it .
His wife then grow angry and scold him heartily .
` Well , well ! '
say he , ` hang the money !
I know what I have learn . '
` What have you learn ? '
say she .
` Ah !
I know that , ' say the man .
After some time have pass the man have a mind to visit his second eldest daughter .
His wife again give him some dry bread to eat , and when he grow tired and hungry he sit down on the east side of a mound and begin to eat it .
As he sit there his daughter come up out of the mound , and invite him to come inside , which he do very willingly .
Soon after this the troll come home .
It be dark by that time , and his wife bid him go and buy some candle .
` Oh , we shall soon get a light , ' say the troll .
With that he dip his finger into the fire , and they then give light without be burn in the least .
The old man get two sack of money here , and plod away homewards with these .
When he be very nearly home he again think of the cow that be with calf , so he lay down the money , run home , and ask his wife whether the cow have calve yet .
` Whatever be the matter with you ? '
say she .
` You come hurry a if the whole house be about to fall .
You may set your mind at rest : the cow have not calve yet . '
The man now ask her to come and help him home with the two sack of money .
She do not believe him very much , but he continue to assure her that it be quite true , till at last she give in and go with him .
When they come to the spot there have again be a thief there and take the money .
It be no wonder that the woman be angry about this , but the man only say , ` Ah , if you only know what I have learn . '
A third time the man set out -- to visit his eldest daughter .
When he come to a mound he sit down on the east side of it and eat the dry bread which his wife have give him to take with him .
The daughter then come out of the mound and invite her father to come inside .
In a little the troll come home , and his wife ask him to go and buy some fish .
` We can get them much more easily than that , ' say the troll .
` Give me your dough trough and your ladle . '
They seat themselves in the trough , and row out on the lake which be beside the mound .
When they have get out a little way the troll say to his wife , ` Are my eye green ? '
` No , not yet , ' say she .
He row on a little further and ask again , ` Are my eye not green yet ? '
` Yes , ' say his wife , ` they be green now . '
Then the troll sprang into the water and ladle up so many fish that in a short time the trough could hold no more .
They then row home again , and have a good meal off the fish .
The old man now get three sack full of money , and set off home with them .
When he be almost home the cow again come into his head , and he lay down the money .
This time , however , he take his wooden shoe and lay them above the money , think that no one would take it after that .
Then he run home and ask his wife whether the cow have calve .
It have not , and she scold him again for behave in this way , but in the end he persuade her to go with him to help him with the three sack of money .
When they come to the spot they find only the wooden shoe , for a thief have come along in the meantime and take all the money .
The woman be very angry , and break out upon her husband ; but he take it all very quietly , and only say , ` Hang the money !
I know what I have learn . '
` What have you learn I should like to know ? '
say his wife .
` You will see that yet , ' say the man .
One day his wife take a fancy for broth , and say to him , ` Oh , go to the village , and buy a piece of beef to make broth . '
` There 's no need of that , ' say he ; ` we can get it an easy way . '
With that he drive a spike into a beam , and run his head against it , and in consequence have to lie in bed for a long time afterwards .
After he have recover from this his wife ask him one day to go and buy candle , a they have none .
` No , ' he say , ` there 's no need for that ; ' and he stick his hand into the fire .
This also make him take to bed for a good while .
When he have get well again his wife one day want fish , and ask him to go and buy some .
The man , however , wish again to show what he have learn , so he ask her to come along with him and bring her dough trough and a ladle .
They both seat themselves in this , and row upon the lake .
When they have get out a little way the man say , ` Are my eye green ? '
` No , ' say his wife ; ` why should they be ? '
They row a little further out , and he ask again , ` Are my eye not green yet ? '
` What nonsense be this ? '
say she ; ` why should they be green ? '
` Oh , my dear , ' say he , ` ca n't you just say that they be green ? '
` Very well , ' say she , ` they be green . '
As soon a he hear this he spring out into the water with the ladle for the fish , but he just get leave to stay there with them !
The Cunning Shoemaker Sicilianische Mahrchen .
Once upon a time there live a shoemaker who could get no work to do , and be so poor that he and his wife nearly die of hunger .
At last he say to her , ` It be no use wait on here -- I can find nothing ; so I shall go down to Mascalucia , and perhaps there I shall be more lucky . '
So down he go to Mascalucia , and walk through the street cry , ` Who want some shoe ? '
And very soon a window be push up , and a woman 's head be thrust out of it .
` Here be a pair for you to patch , ' she say .
And he sit down on her doorstep and set about patch them .
` How much do I owe you ? '
she ask when they be do . '
A shilling . '
` Here be eighteen penny , and good luck to you . '
And he go his way .
He turn into the next street and set up his cry again , and it be not long before another window be push up and another head appear .
` Here be some shoe for you to patch . '
And the shoemaker sit down on the doorstep and patch them .
` How much do I owe you ? '
ask the woman when the shoe be finish . '
A florin . '
` Here be a crown piece , and good luck to you . '
And she shut the window .
` Well , ' think the shoemaker , ' I have do finely .
But I will not go back to my wife just yet , a , if I only go on at this rate , I shall soon have enough money to buy a donkey . '
Having make up his mind what be best to do , he stay in the town a few day longer till he have four gold piece safe in his purse .
Then he go to the market and for two of them he buy a good strong donkey , and , mount on it back , he ride home to Catania .
But a he enter a thick wood he saw in the distance a band of robber who be come quickly towards him . '
I be lose , ' think he ; ` they be sure to take from me all the money that I have earn , and I shall be as poor a ever I be .
What can I do ? '
However , be a clever little man and full of spirit , he do not lose heart , but , take five florin , he fasten them out of sight under the donkey 's thick mane .
Then he ride on .
Directly the robber come up to him they seize him exactly a he have foretell and take away all his money .
` Oh , dear friend ! '
he cry , wring his hand , ' I be only a poor shoemaker , and have nothing but this donkey leave in the world . '
As he speak the donkey give himself a shake , and down fell the five florin .
` Where do that come from ? '
ask the robber .
` Ah , ' reply the shoemaker , ` you have guess my secret .
The donkey be a golden donkey , and supply me with all my money . '
` Sell him to u , ' say the robber .
` We will give you any price you like . '
The shoemaker at first declare that nothing would induce him to sell him , but at last he agree to hand him over to the robber for fifty gold piece .
` But listen to what I tell you , ' say he .
` You must each take it in turn to own him for a night and a day , or else you will all be fight over the money . '
With these word they part , the robber drive the donkey to their cave in the forest and the shoemaker return home , very pleased with the success of his trick .
He just stop on the way to pick up a good dinner , and the next day spend most of his gain in buy a small vineyard .
Meanwhile the robber have arrive at the cave where they live , and the captain , call them all round him , announce that it a his right to have the donkey for the first night .
His companion agree , and then he tell his wife to put a mattress in the stable .
She ask if he have go out of his mind , but he answer crossly , ` What be that to you ?
Do a you be bid , and to-morrow I will bring you some treasure . '
Very early the captain awoke and search the stable , but could find nothing , and guess that Master Joseph have be make fun of them .
` Well , ' he say to himself , ` if I have be take in , the others shall not come off any good . '
So , when one of his men arrive and ask him eagerly how much money he have get , he answer gaily , ` Oh , comrade , if you only know !
But I shall say nothing about it till everyone have have his turn ! '
One after another they all take the donkey , but no money be forthcoming for anybody .
At length , when all the band have be trick , they hold a council , and resolve to march to the shoemaker 's house and punish him well for his cunning .
Just a before , the shoemaker saw them a long way off , and begin to think how he could outwit them again .
When he have hit upon a plan he call his wife , and say to her , ` Take a bladder and fill it with blood , and bind it round your neck .
When the robber come and demand the money they give me for the donkey I shall shout to you and tell you to get it quickly .
You must argue with me , and decline to obey me , and then I shall plunge my knife into the bladder , and you must fall to the ground a if you be dead .
There you must lie till I play on my guitar ; then get up and begin to dance . '
The wife make haste to do a she be bid , and there be no time to lose , for the robber be draw very near the house .
They enter with a great noise , and overwhelm the shoemaker with reproach for have deceive them about the donkey .
` The poor beast must have lose it power owing to the change of master , ' say he ; ` but we will not quarrel about it .
You shall have back the fifty gold piece that you give for him .
` Aite , ' he cry to his wife , ` go quickly to the chest upstairs , and bring down the money for these gentleman . '
` Wait a little , ' answer she ; ' I must first bake this fish .
It will be spoilt if I leave it now . '
` Go this instant , a you be bid , ' shout the shoemaker , stamp a if he be in a great passion ; but , a she do not stir , he draw his knife , and stab her in the neck .
The blood spurt out freely , and she fell to the ground a if she be dead .
` What have you do ? '
ask the robber , look at him in dismay .
` The poor woman be do nothing . '
` Perhaps I be hasty , but it be easily set right , ' reply the shoemaker , take down his guitar and beginning to play .
Hardly have he strike the first note than his wife sit up ; then get on her foot and dance .
The robber star with open mouth , and at last they say , ` Master Joseph , you may keep the fifty gold piece .
But tell u what you will take for your guitar , for you must sell it to u ? '
` Oh , that be impossible ! '
reply the shoemaker , ` for every time I have a quarrel with my wife I just strike her dead , and so give vent to my anger .
This have become such a habit with me that I do n't think I could break myself of it ; and , of course , if I get rid of the guitar I could never bring her back to life again . '
However , the robber would not listen to him , and at last he consent to take forty gold piece for the guitar .
Then they all return to their cave in the forest , delight with their new purchase , and long for a chance of try it power .
But the captain declare that the first trial belong to him , and after that the others might have their turn .
That evening he call to his wife and say , ` What have you get for supper ? '
` Macaroni , ' answer she .
` Why have you not boil a fish ? '
he cry , and stabber in the neck so that she fell dead .
The captain , who be not in the least angry , seize the guitar and begin to play ; but , let him play as loud a he would , the dead woman never stir .
` Oh , lie shoemaker !
Oh , abominable knave !
Twice have he get the good of me .
But I will pay him out ! '
So he rag and swore , but it do him no good .
The fact remain that he have kill his wife and could not bring her back again .
The next morning come one of the robber to fetch the guitar , and to hear what have happen .
` Well , how have you get on ? '
` Oh , splendidly !
I stab my wife , and then begin to play , and now she be as well a ever . '
` Did you really ?
Then this evening I will try for myself . '
Of course the same thing happen over again , till all the wife have be kill secretly , and when there be no more leave they whisper to each other the dreadful tale , and swore to be avenge on the shoemaker .
The band lose no time in set out for his house , and , a before , the shoemaker saw them come from afar .
He call to his wife , who be wash in the kitchen : ` Listen , Aita : when the robber come and ask for me say I have go to the vineyard .
Then tell the dog to call me , and chase him from the house . '
When he have give these direction he run out of the back door and hid behind a barrel .
A few minute later the robber arrive , and call loudly for the shoemaker .
` Alas !
good gentleman , he be up in the vineyard , but I will send the dog after him at once .
Here !
now quickly to the vineyard , and tell your master some gentleman be here who wish to speak to him .
Go as fast a you can . '
And she open the door and let the dog out .
` You can really trust the dog to call your husband ? '
ask the robber .
` Dear me , yes !
He understand everything , and will always carry any message I give him . '
By-and-bye the shoemaker come in and say , ` Good morning , gentleman ; the dog tell me you wish to speak to me . '
` Yes , we do , ' reply the robber ; ` we have come to speak to you about that guitar .
It be your fault that we have murder all our wife ; and , though we play a you tell u , none of them ever come back to life . '
` You could not have play properly , ' say the shoemaker .
` It be your own fault . '
` Well , we will forget all about it , ' answer the robber , ` if you will only sell u your dog . '
` Oh , that be impossible !
I should never get on without him . '
But the robber offer him forty gold piece , and at last he agree to let them have the dog .
So they depart , take the dog with them , and when they get back to their cave the captain declare that it be his right to have the first trial .
He then call his daughter , and say to her , ' I be go to the inn ; if anybody want me , loose the dog , and send him to call me . '
About an hour after some one arrive on business , and the girl untie the dog and say , ` Go to the inn and call my father ! '
The dog bound off , but run straight to the shoemaker .
When the robber get home and find no dog he think ` He must have go back to his old master , ' and , though night have already fall , he go off after him .
` Master Joseph , be the dog here ? '
ask he .
` Ah !
yes , the poor beast be so fond of me !
You must give him time to get accustom to new way . '
So the captain bring the dog back , and the following morning hand him over to another of the band , just say that the animal really could do what the shoemaker have say .
The second robber carefully keep his own counsel , and fetch the dog secretly back from the shoemaker , and so on through the whole band .
At length , when everybody have suffer , they meet and tell the whole story , and next day they all march off in fury to the man who have make game of them .
After reproach him with have deceive them , they tie him up in a sack , and tell him they be go to throw him into the sea .
The shoemaker lay quite still , and let them do a they would .
They go on till they come to a church , and the robber say , ` The sun be hot and the sack be heavy ; let u leave it here and go in and rest . '
So they put the sack down by the roadside , and go into the church .
Now , on a hill near by there be a swineherd look after a great herd of pig and whistle merrily .
When Master Joseph hear him he cry out as loud a he could , ' I wo n't ; I wo n't , I say . '
` What wo n't you do ? '
ask the swineherd .
` Oh , ' reply the shoemaker .
` They want me to marry the king 's daughter , and I wo n't do it . '
` How lucky you be ! '
sigh the swineherd .
` Now , if it be only me ! '
` Oh , if that 's all ! '
reply the cunning shoemaker , ` get you into this sack , and let me out . '
Then the swineherd open the sack and take the place of the shoemaker , who go gaily off , drive the pig before him .
When the robber be rest they come out of the church , take up the sack , and carry it to the sea , where they throw it in , and it sink directly .
As they come back they meet the shoemaker , and star at him with open mouth .
` Oh , if you only know how many pig live in the sea , ' he cry .
` And the deeper you go the more there be .
I have just bring up these , and mean to return for some more . '
` There be still some left there ? '
` Oh , more than I could count , ' reply the shoemaker . '
I will show you what you must do . '
Then he lead the robber back to the shore .
` Now , ' say he , ` you must each of you tie a stone to your neck , so that you may be sure to go deep enough , for I find the pig that you saw very deep down indeed . '
Then the robber all tie stone round their neck , and jump in , and be drown , and Master Joseph drive his pig home , and be a rich man to the end of his day .
The King Who Would Have a Beautiful Wife Sicilianische Mahrchen .
Fifty year ago there live a king who be very anxious to get married ; but , a he be quite determine that his wife should be as beautiful a the sun , the thing be not so easy a it seem , for no maiden come up to his standard .
Then he command a trusty servant to search through the length and breadth of the land till he find a girl fair enough to be queen , and if he have the good luck to discover one he be to bring her back with him .
The servant set out at once on his journey , and seek high and low-in castle and cottage ; but though pretty maiden be plentiful a blackberry , he felt sure that none of them would please the king .
One day he have wander far and wide , and be feel very tired and thirsty .
By the roadside stand a tiny little house , and here he knock and ask for a cup of water .
Now in this house dwell two sister , and one be eighty and the other ninety year old .
They be very poor , and earn their living by spin .
This have keep their hand very soft and white , like the hand of a girl , and when the water be pass through the lattice , and the servant saw the small , delicate finger , he say to himself : ' A maiden must indeed be lovely if she have a hand like that . '
And he make haste back , and tell the king .
` Go back at once , ' say his majesty , ` and try to get a sight of her . '
The faithful servant depart on his errand without lose any time , and again he knock at the door of the little house and beg for some water .
As before , the old woman do not open the door , but pass the water through the lattice .
` Do you live here alone ? '
ask the man .
` No , ' reply she , ` my sister live with me .
We be poor girl , and have to work for our bread . '
` How old be you ? ' '
I be fifteen , and she be twenty . '
Then the servant go back to the king , and tell him all he know .
And his majesty answer : ' I will have the fifteen-year-old one .
Go and bring her here . '
The servant return a third time to the little house and knock at the door .
In reply to his knock the lattice window be push open , and a voice inquire what it be he want .
` The king have desire me to bring back the young of you to become his queen , ' he reply .
` Tell his majesty I be ready to do his bidding , but since my birth no ray of light have fall upon my face .
If it should ever do so I shall instantly grow black .
Therefore beg , I pray you , his most gracious majesty to send this even a shut carriage , and I will return in it to the castle .
When the king heard this he order his great golden carriage to be prepare , and in it to be place some magnificent robe ; and the old woman wrap herself in a thick veil , and be drive to the castle .
The king be eagerly await her , and when she arrive he beg her politely to raise her veil and let him see her face .
But she answer : ` Here the taper be too bright and the light too strong .
Would you have me turn black under your very eyes ? '
And the king believe her word , and the marriage take place without the veil be once lift .
Afterwards , when they be alone , he raise the corner , and know for the first time that he have wed a wrinkled old woman .
And , in a furious burst of anger , he dash open the window and fling her out .
But , luckily for her , her clothes catch on a nail in the wall , and keep her hanging between heaven and earth .
While she be thus suspend , expect every moment to be dash to the ground , four fairy happen to pass by .
` Look , sister , ' cry one , ` surely that be the old woman that the king sent for .
Shall we wish that her clothes may give way , and that she should be dash to the ground ? '
` Oh no !
no ! '
exclaim another .
` Let u wish her something good .
I myself will wish her youth . '
` And I beauty . '
` And I wisdom . '
` And I a tender heart . '
So spake the fairy , and go their way , leave the most beautiful maiden in the world behind them .
The next morning when the king look from his window he saw this lovely creature hang on the nail .
` Ah !
what have I do ?
Surely I must have be blind last night ! '
And he order long ladder to be bring and the maiden to be rescue .
Then he fell on his knee before her , and pray her to forgive him , and a great feast be make in her honour .
Some day after come the ninety-year-old sister to the palace and ask for the queen .
` Who be that hideous old witch ? '
say the king .
` Oh , an old neighbour of mine , who be half silly , ' she reply .
But the old woman look at her steadily , and know her again , and say : ` How have you manage to grow so young and beautiful ?
I should like to be young and beautiful too . '
This question she repeat the whole day long , till at length the queen lose patience and say : ' I have my old head cut off , and this new head grow in it place . '
Then the old woman go to a barber , and speak to him , say , ' I will give you all you ask if you will only cut off my head , so that I may become young and lovely . '
` But , my good woman , if I do that you will die ! '
But the old woman would listen to nothing ; and at last the barber take out his knife and strike the first blow at her neck .
` Ah ! '
she shriek a she felt the pain .
` Il faut souffrir pour etre belle , ' say the barber , who have be in France .
And at the second blow her head roll off , and the old woman be dead for good and all .
Catherine and Her Destiny Sicilianische Mahrchen von Laura Gonzenbach .
Leipzig , Engelmann , 1870 .
Long ago there live a rich merchant who , besides possess more treasure than any king in the world , have in his great hall three chair , one of silver , one of gold , and one of diamond .
But his great treasure of all be his only daughter , who be call Catherine .
One day Catherine be sit in her own room when suddenly the door fly open , and in come a tall and beautiful woman hold in her hand a little wheel .
` Catherine , ' she say , go up to the girl , ` which would you rather have-a happy youth or a happy old age ? '
Catherine be so take by surprise that she do not know what to answer , and the lady repeat again , ` Which would you rather have-a happy youth or a happy old age ? '
Then Catherine think to herself , ` If I say a happy youth , then I shall have to suffer all the rest of my life .
No , I would bear trouble now , and have something well to look forward to . '
So she look up and reply , ` Give me a happy old age . '
` So be it , ' say the lady , and turn her wheel a she speak , vanish the next moment as suddenly a she have come .
Now this beautiful lady be the Destiny of poor Catherine .
Only a few day after this the merchant hear the news that all his fine ship , laden with the rich merchandise , have be sink in a storm , and he be leave a beggar .
The shock be too much for him .
He take to his bed , and in a short time he be dead of his disappointment .
So poor Catherine be leave alone in the world without a penny or a creature to help her .
But she be a brave girl and full of spirit , and soon make up her mind that the best thing she could do be to go to the near town and become a servant .
She lose no time in get herself ready , and do not take long over her journey ; and a she be pass down the chief street of the town a noble lady saw her out of the window , and , strike by her sad face , say to her : ` Where be you go all alone , my pretty girl ? '
` Ah , my lady , I be very poor , and must go to service to earn my bread . ' '
I will take you into my service , ' say she ; and Catherine serve her well .
Some time after her mistress say to Catherine , ' I be oblige to go out for a long while , and must lock the house door , so that no thief shall get in . '
So she go away , and Catherine take her work and sit down at the window .
Suddenly the door burst open , and in come her Destiny .
` Oh !
so here you be , Catherine !
Did you really think I be go to leave you in peace ? '
And a she speak she walk to the linen press where Catherine 's mistress keep all her fine sheet and underclothes , tear everything in piece , and fling them on the floor .
Poor Catherine wring her hand and wept , for she think to herself , ` When my lady come back and see all this ruin she will think it be my fault , ' and start up , she flee through the open door .
Then Destiny take all the piece and make them whole again , and put them back in the press , and when everything be tidy she too leave the house .
When the mistress reach home she call Catherine , but no Catherine be there .
` Can she have rob me ? '
think the old lady , and look hastily round the house ; but nothing be miss .
She wonder why Catherine should have disappear like this , but she hear no more of her , and in a few day she fill her place .
Meanwhile Catherine wander on and on , without know very well where she be go , till at last she come to another town .
Just a before , a noble lady happen to see her pass her window , and call out to her , ` Where be you go all alone , my pretty girl ? '
And Catherine answer , ` Ah , my lady , I be very poor , and must go to service to earn my bread . ' '
I will take you into my service , ' say the lady ; and Catherine serve her well , and hop she might now be leave in peace .
But , exactly a before , one day that Catherine be leave in the house alone her Destiny come again and speak to her with hard word : ` What !
be you here now ? '
And in a passion she tear up everything she saw , till in sheer misery poor Catherine rush out of the house .
And so it befall for seven year , and directly Catherine find a fresh place her Destiny come and force her to leave it .
After seven year , however , Destiny seem to get tire of persecute her , and a time of peace set in for Catherine .
When she have be chase away from her last house by Destiny 's wicked prank she have take service with another lady , who tell her that it would be part of her daily work to walk to a mountain that overshadow the town , and , climb up to the top , she be to lay on the ground some loaf of freshly bake bread , and cry with a loud voice , ' O Destiny , my mistress , ' three time .
Then her lady 's Destiny would come and take away the offering .
` That will I gladly do , ' say Catherine .
So the year go by , and Catherine be still there , and every day she climb the mountain with her basket of bread on her arm .
She be happy than she have be , but sometimes , when no one saw her , she would weep a she think over her old life , and how different it be to the one she be now lead .
One day her lady saw her , and say , ` Catherine , what be it ?
Why be you always weep ? '
And then Catherine tell her story . '
I have get an idea , ' exclaim the lady .
` To-morrow , when you take the bread to the mountain , you shall pray my Destiny to speak to yours , and entreat her to leave you in peace .
Perhaps something may come of it ! '
At these word Catherine dry her eye , and next morning , when she climb the mountain , she tell all she have suffer , and cry , ' O Destiny , my mistress , pray , I entreat you , of my Destiny that she may leave me in peace . '
And Destiny answer , ` Oh , my poor girl , know you not your Destiny lie bury under seven coverlids , and can hear nothing ?
But if you will come to-morrow I will bring her with me . '
And after Catherine have go her way her lady 's Destiny go to find her sister , and say to her , ` Dear sister , have not Catherine suffer enough ?
It be surely time for her good day to begin ? '
And the sister answer , ` To-morrow you shall bring her to me , and I will give her something that may help her out of her need . '
The next morning Catherine set out early than usual for the mountain , and her lady 's Destiny take the girl by the hand and lead her to her sister , who lay under the seven coverlids .
And her Destiny hold out to Catherine a ball of silk , say , ` Keep this -- it may be useful some day ; ' then pull the covering over her head again .
But Catherine walk sadly down the hill , and go straight to her lady and show her the silken ball , which be the end of all her high hope .
` What shall I do with it ? '
she ask .
` It be not worth sixpence , and it be no good to me ! '
` Take care of it , ' reply her mistress .
` Who can tell how useful it may be ? '
A little while after this grand preparation be make for the king 's marriage , and all the tailor in the town be busy embroider fine clothes .
The wedding garment be so beautiful nothing like it have ever be see before , but when it be almost finish the tailor find that he have no more silk .
The colour be very rare , and none could be find like it , and the king make a proclamation that if anyone happen to possess any they should bring it to the court , and he would give them a large sum .
` Catherine ! '
exclaim the lady , who have be to the tailor and see the wedding garment , ` your ball of silk be exactly the right colour .
Bring it to the king , and you can ask what you like for it . '
Then Catherine put on her best clothes and go to the court , and look more beautiful than any woman there .
` May it please your majesty , ' she say , ' I have bring you a ball of silk of the colour you ask for , a no one else have any in the town . '
` Your majesty , ' ask one of the courtier , ` shall I give the maiden it weight in gold ? '
The king agree , and a pair of scale be bring ; and a handful of gold be place in one scale and the silken ball in the other .
But lo !
let the king lay in the scale a many gold piece a he would , the silk be always heavy still .
Then the king take some large scale , and heap up all his treasure on one side , but the silk on the other outweigh them all .
At last there be only one thing leave that have not be put in , and that be his golden crown .
And he take it from his head and set it on top of all , and at last the scale move and the ball have found it balance .
` Where got you this silk ? '
ask the king .
` It be give me , royal majesty , by my mistress , ' reply Catherine .
` That be not true , ' say the king , ` and if you do not tell me the truth I will have your head cut off this instant . '
So Catherine tell him the whole story , and how she have once be as rich a he .
Now there live at the court a wise woman , and she say to Catherine , ` You have suffer much , my poor girl , but at length your luck have turn , and I know by the weighing of the scale through the crown that you will die a queen . '
` So she shall , ' cry the king , who overheard these word ; ` she shall die my queen , for she be more beautiful than all the lady of the court , and I will marry no one else . '
And so it fell out .
The king send back the bride he have promise to wed to her own country , and the same Catherine be queen at the marriage feast instead , and live happy and content to the end of her life .
How the Hermit Helped to Win the King 's Daughter Sicilianische Mahrchen Long ago there live a very rich man who have three son .
When he felt himself to be die he divide his property between them , make them share alike , both in money and land .
Soon after he die the king set forth a proclamation through the whole country that whoever could build a ship that should float both on land and sea should have his daughter to wife .
The eldest brother , when he hear it , say to the other , ' I think I will spend some of my money in try to build that ship , a I should like to have the king for my father-in-law . '
So he call together all the shipbuilder in the land , and give them order to begin the ship without delay .
And tree be cut down , and great preparation make , and in a few day everybody know what it be all for ; and there be a crowd of old people press round the gate of the yard , where the young man spend the most of his day .
` Ah , master , give u work , ' they say , ` so that we may earn our bread . '
But he only give them hard word , and speak roughly to them .
` You be old , and have lose your strength ; of what use be you ? '
And he drive them away .
Then come some boy and pray him , `` master , give u work , ' but he answer them , ` Of what use can you be , weakling a you be !
Get you go ! '
And if any presented themselves that be not skilled workman he would have none of them .
At last there knock at the gate a little old man with a long white beard , and say , ` Will you give me work , so that I may earn my bread ? '
But he be only driven away like the rest .
The ship take a long while to build , and cost a great deal of money , and when it be launch a sudden squall rise , and it fell to piece , and with it all the young man 's hope of win the princess .
By this time he have not a penny left , so he go back to his two brother and tell his tale .
And the second brother say to himself a he listen , ` Certainly he have manage very badly , but I should like to see if I ca n't do good , and win the princess for my own self . '
So he call together all the shipbuilder throughout the country , and give them order to build a ship which should float on the land as well a on the sea .
But his heart be no soft than his brother 's , and every man that be not a skilled workman be chase away with hard word .
Last come the white-bearded man , but he fare no good than the rest .
When the ship be finish the launch take place , and everything seem go smoothly when a gale sprang up , and the vessel be dash to piece on the rock .
The young man have spend his whole fortune on it , and now it be all swallow up , be force to beg shelter from his young brother .
When he tell his story the young say to himself , ' I be not rich enough to support u all three .
I have well take my turn , and if I manage to win the princess there will be her fortune as well a my own for u to live on . '
So he call together all the shipbuilder in the kingdom , and give order that a new ship should be build .
Then all the old people come and ask for work , and he answer cheerfully , ` Oh , yes , there be plenty for everybody ; ' and when the boy beg to be allow to help he find something that they could do .
And when the old man with the long white beard stand before him , pray that he might earn his bread , he reply , ` Oh , father , I could not suffer you to work , but you shall be overseer , and look after the rest . '
Now the old man be a holy hermit , and when he saw how kind-hearted the youth be he determine to do all he could for him to gain the wish of his heart .
By-and-bye , when the ship be finish , the hermit say to his young friend , ` Now you can go and claim the king 's daughter , for hte ship will float both by land and sea . '
` Oh , good father , ' cry the young man , ` you will not forsake me ?
Stay with me , I pray you , and lead me to the king ! '
` If you wish it , I will , ' say the hermit , ` on condition that you will give me half of anything you get . '
` Oh , if that be all , ' answer he , ` it be easily promise ! '
And they set out together on the ship .
After they have go some distance they saw a man stand in a thick fog , which he be try to put into a sack .
` Oh , good father , ' exclaim the youth , ` what can he be do ? '
` Ask him , ' say the old man .
` What be you do , my fine fellow ? ' '
I be put the fog into my sack .
That be my business . '
` Ask him if he will come with u , ' whisper the hermit .
And the man answer : ` If you will give me enough to eat and drink I will gladly stay with you . '
So they take him on their ship , and the youth say , a they start off again , ` Good father , before we be two , and now we be three ! '
After they have travel a little further they meet a man who have tear up half the forest , and be carry all the tree on his shoulder .
` Good father , ' exclaim the youth , ` only look !
What can he have do that for ? '
` Ask him why he have tear up all those tree . '
And the man reply , ` Why , I 've merely be gather a handful of brushwood . '
` Beg him to come with u , ' whisper the hermit .
And the strong man answer : ` Willingly , as long a you give me enough to eat and drink . '
And he come on the ship .
And the youth say to the hermit , ` Good father , before we be three , and now we be four . '
The ship travel on again , and some mile far on they saw a man drink out of a stream till he have nearly drunk it dry .
` Good father , ' say the youth , ` just look at that man !
Did you ever see anybody drink like that ? '
` Ask him why he do it , ' answer the hermit .
` Why , there be nothing very odd in take a mouthful of water ! '
reply the man , stand up .
` Beg him to come with u . '
And the youth do so .
` With pleasure , as long a you give me enough to eat and drink . '
And the youth whisper to the hermit , ` Good father , before we be four , and now we be five . '
A little way along they notice another man in the middle of a stream , who be shoot into the water .
` Good father , ' say the youth , ` what can he be shoot at ? '
` Ask him , ' answer the hermit .
` Hush , hush ! '
cry the man ; ` now you have frighten it away .
In the Underworld sit a quail on a tree , and I want to shoot it .
That be my business .
I hit everything I aim at . '
` Ask him if he will come with u . '
And the man reply , ` With all my heart , as long a I get enough to eat and drink . '
So they take him into the ship , and the young man whisper , ` Good father , before we be five , and now we be six . '
Off they go again , and before they have go far they meet a man stride towards them whose step be so long that while one foot be on the north of the island the other be right down in the south .
` Good father , look at him !
What long step he take ! '
` Ask him why he do it , ' reply the hermit .
` Oh , I be only go out for a little walk , ' answer he .
` Ask him if he will come with u . '
` Gladly , if you will give me as much a I want to eat and drink , ' say he , climb up into the ship .
And the young man whisper , ` Good father , before we be six , and now we be seven . '
But the hermit know what he be about , and why he gather these strange people into the ship .
After many day , at last they reach the town where live the king and his daughter .
They stop the vessel right in front of the palace , and the young man go in and bow low before the king . '
O Majesty , I have do your bidding , and now be the ship build that can travel over land and sea .
Give me my reward , and let me have your daughter to wife . '
But the king say to himself , ` What !
be I to wed my daughter to a man of whom I know nothing .
Not even whether he be rich or poor -- a knight or a beggar . '
And aloud he spake : It be not enough that you have manage to build the ship .
You must find a runner who shall take this letter to the ruler of the Underworld , and bring me the answer back in an hour . '
` That be not in the bond , ' answer the young man .
` Well , do a you like , ' reply the king , ` only you will not get my daughter . '
The young man go out , sorely troubled , to tell his old friend what have happen .
` Silly boy ! '
cry the hermit , ` Accept his term at once .
And send off the long-legged man with the letter .
He will take it in no time at all . '
So the youth 's heard leapt for joy , and he return to the king .
` Majesty , I accept your term .
HEre be the messenger who will do what you wish . '
The king have no choice but to give the man the letter , and he stride off , make short work of the distance that lay between the palace and the Underworld .
He soon find the ruler , who look at the letter , and say to him , ` Wait a little while i write the answer ; ' but the man be soo tire with his quick walk that he go sound asleep and forget all about his errand .
All this time the youth be anxiously count the minute till he could get back , and stand with his eye fix on the road down which his messenger must come .
` What can be keep him , ' he say to the hermit when the hour be nearly up .
Then the hermit send for the man who could hit everything he aim at , and say to him , ` Just see why the messenger stay so long . '
` Oh , he be sound asleep in the palace of the Underworld .
However , I can wake him . '
Then he draw his bow , and shoot an arrow straight into the man 's knee .
The messenger awake with such a start , and when he saw that the hour have almost run out he snatch up the answer and rush back with such speed that the clock have not yet strike when he enter the palace .
Now the young man think he be sure of his bride , but the king say , `` Still you have not do enough .
Before I give you my daughter you must find a man who can drink half the content of my cellar in one day . '
` That be not in the bond , ' complain the poor youth .
` Well , do a you like , only you will not get my daughter . '
The young man go sadly out , and ask the hermit what he be to do .
` Silly boy ! '
say he .
` Why , tell the man to do it who drink up everything . '
So they send for the man and say , ` Do you think you be able to drink half the royal cellar in one day ? '
` Dear me , yes , and as much more a you want , ' answer he . '
I be never satisfy . '
The king be not please at the young man agree so readily , but he have no choice , and order the servant to be take downstairs .
Oh , how he enjoy himself !
All day long he drink , and drank , and drank , till instead of half the cellar , he have drink the whole , and there be not a cask but what stand empty .
And when the king saw this he say to the youth , ` You have conquer , and I can no longer withhold my daughter .
But , a her dowry , I shall only give so much a one man can carry away . '
` But , ' answer he , ` let a man be ever so strong , he can not carry more than a hundredweight , and what be that for a king 's daughter ? '
` Well , do a you like ; I have say my say .
It be your affair -- not mine . '
The young man be puzzle , and do not know what to reply , for , though he would gladly have marry the princess without a sixpence , he have spend all his money in build the ship , and know he could not give her all she want .
So he go to the hermit and say to him , ` The king will only give for her dowry as much a a man can carry .
I have no money of my own left , and my brother have none either . '
` Silly boy !
Why , you have only get to fetch the man who carry half the forest on his shoulder . '
And the youth be glad , and call the strong man , and tell him what he must do .
` Take everything you can , till you be bent double .
Never mind if you leave the palace bare . '
The strong man promise , and nobly keep his word .
He pile all he could see on his back -- chair , table , wardrobe , chest of gold and silver -- till there be nothing leave to pile .
At last he take the king 's crown , and put it on the top .
He carry his burden to the ship and stow his treasure away , and the youth follow , lead the king 's daughter .
But the king be leave rag in his empty palace , and he call together his army , and get ready his ship of war , in order that he might go after the vessel and bring back what have be take away .
And the king 's ship sail very fast , and soon catch up the little vessel , and the sailor all shout for joy .
Then the hermit look out and saw how near they be , and he say to the youth , ` Do you see that ? '
The youth shriek and cry , ` Ah , good father , it be a fleet of ship , and they be chase u , and in a few moment they will be upon u . '
But the hermit bid him call the man who have the fog in his sack , and the sack be open and the fog fly out , and hung right round the king 's ship , so that they could see nothing .
So they sail back to the palace , and tell the king what strange thing have happen .
Meanwhile the young man 's vessel reach home in safety .
` Well , here you be once more ' say the hermit ; ` and now you can fulfil the promise you make me to give me the half of all you have . '
` That will I do with all my heart , ' answer the youth , and begin to divide all his treasure , put part on one side for himself and set aside the other for his friend .
` Good father , it be finish , ' say he at length ; ` there be nothing more left to divide . '
` Nothing more left ! '
cry the hermit .
` Why , you have forget the best thing of all ! '
` What can that be ? '
ask he .
` We have divide everything . '
` And the king 's daughter ? '
say the hermit .
Then the young man 's heart stand still , for he love her dearly .
But he answer , ` It be well ; I have swear , and I will keep my word , ' and draw his sword to cut her in piece .
When the hermit saw that he hold his honour dearer than his wife he lift his hand and cry , ` Hold !
she be yours , and all the treasure too .
I give you my help because you have pity on those that be in need .
And when you be in need yourself , call upon me , and I will come to you . '
As he speak he softly touch their head and vanished .
The next day the wedding take place , and the two brother come to the house , and they all live happily together , but they never forget the holy man who have be such a good friend .
The Water of Life Cuentos Populars Catalans , per lo Dr. D. Francisco de S. Maspous y Labros .
Barcelona , 1885 .
Three brother and one sister live together in a small cottage , and they love one another dearly .
One day the eldest brother , who have never do anything but amuse himself from sunrise to sunset , say to the rest , ` Let u all work hard , and perhaps we shall grow rich , and be able to build ourselves a palace . '
And his brother and sister answer joyfully , ` Yes , we will all work ! '
So they fell to work with all their might , till at last they become rich , and be able to build themselves a beautiful palace ; and everyone come from mile round to see it wonder , and to say how splendid it be .
No one thought of find any fault , till at length an old woman , who have be walk through the room with a crowd of people , suddenly exclaim , ` Yes , it be a splendid palace , but there be still something it need ! '
` And what may that be ? ' '
A church . '
When they hear this the brother set to work again to earn some more money , and when they have get enough they set about build a church , which should be a large and beautiful a the palace itself .
And after the church be finish great number of people than ever flock to see the palace and the church and vast garden and magnificent hall .
But one day , a the brother be as usual do the honour to their guest , an old man turn to them and say , ` Yes , it be all most beautiful , but there be still something it need ! '
` And what may that be ? ' '
A pitcher of the water of life , a branch of the tree the smell of whose flower give eternal beauty , and the talk bird . '
` And where be I to find all those ? '
` Go to the mountain that be far off yonder , and you will find what you seek . '
After the old man have bow politely and take farewell of them the eldest brother say to the rest , ' I will go in search of the water of life , and the talk bird , and the tree of beauty . '
` But suppose some evil thing befalls you ? '
ask his sister .
` How shall we know ? '
` You be right , ' he reply ; ' I have not think of that ! '
Then they follow the old man , and say to him , ` My eldest brother wish to seek for the water of life , and the tree of beauty , and the talk bird , that you tell him be needful to make our palace perfect .
But how shall we know if any evil thing befall him ? '
So the old man take them a knife , and give it to them , say , ` Keep this carefully , and as long a the blade be bright all be well ; but if the blade be bloody , then know that evil have befall him . '
The brother thank him , and depart , and go straight to the palace , where they find the young man make ready to set out for the mountain where the treasure he long for lay hid .
And he walk , and he walk , and he walk , till he have go a great way , and there he meet a giant .
` Can you tell me how much further I have still to go before I reach that mountain yonder ? '
` And why do you wish to go there ? ' '
I be seek the water of life , the talk bird , and a branch of the tree of beauty . '
` Many have pass by seek those treasure , but none have ever come back ; and you will never come back either , unless you mark my word .
Follow this path , and when you reach the mountain you will find it covered with stone .
Do not stop to look at them , but keep on your way .
As you go you will hear scoff and laugh behind you ; it will be the stone that mock .
Do not heed them ; above all , do not turn round .
If you do you will become a one of them .
Walk straight on till you get to the top , and then take all you wish for . '
The young man thank him for his counsel , and walk , and walk , and walk , till he reach the mountain .
And a he climb he hear behind him scoff and jeer , but he keep his ear steadily close to them .
At last the noise grow so loud that he lose patience , and he stoop to pick up a stone to hurl into the midst of the clamour , when suddenly his arm seem to stiffen , and the next moment he be a stone himself !
That day his sister , who think her brother 's step be long in returning , take out the knife and find the blade be red a blood .
Then she cry out to her brother that something terrible have come to pass . '
I will go and find him , ' say the second .
And he go .
And he walk , and he walk , and he walk , till he meet the giant , and ask him if he have see a young man travel towards the mountain .
And the giant answer , ` Yes , I have see him pas , but I have not see him come back .
The spell must have work upon him . '
` Then what can I do to disenchant him , and find the water of life , the talk bird , and a branch of the tree of beauty ? '
` Follow this path , and when you reach the mountain you will find it covered with stone .
Do not stop to look at them , but climb steadily on .
Above all , heed not the laugh and scoff that will arise on all side , and never turn round .
And when you reach the top you can then take all you desire . '
The young man thank him for his counsel , and set out for the mountain .
But no sooner do he reach it than loud jest and gibe break out on every side , and almost deafen him .
For some time he let them rail , and push boldly on , till he have pass the place which his brother have gain ; then suddenly he think that among the scoff sound he hear his brother 's voice .
He stop and look back ; and another stone be add to the number .
Meanwhile the sister leave at home be count the day when her two brother should return to her .
The time seem long , and it would be hard to say how often she take out the knife and look at it polished blade to make sure that this one at least be still safe .
The blade be always bright and clear ; each time she look she have the happiness of know that all be well , till one evening , tire and anxious , a she frequently be at the end of the day , she take it from it drawer , and behold !
the blade be red with blood .
Her cry of horror bring her young brother to her , and , unable to speak , she hold out the knife ! '
I will go , ' he say .
So he walk , and he walk , and he walk , until he meet the giant , and he ask , ` Have two young men , make for yonder mountain , pass this way ? '
And the giant answer , ` Yes , they have pass by , but they never come back , and by this I know that the spell have fall upon them . '
` Then what must I do to free them , and to get the water of life , and the talk bird , and the branch of the tree of beauty ? '
` Go to the mountain , which you will find so thickly cover with stone that you will hardly be able to place your foot , and walk straight forward , turn neither to the right hand nor to the left , and pay no heed to the laugh and scoff which will follow you , till you reach the top , and then you may take all that you desire . '
The young man thank the giant for his counsel , and set forth to the mountain .
And when he begin to climb there burst forth all around him a storm of scoff and jeer ; but he think of the giant 's word , and look neither to the right hand nor to the left , till the mountain top lay straight before him .
A moment now and he would have gain it , when , through the groan and yell , he hear his brother ' voice .
He turn , and there be one stone the more .
And all this while his sister be pace up and down the palace , hardly let the knife out of her hand , and dread what she know she would see , and what she do see .
The blade grow red before her eye , and she say , ` Now it be my turn . '
So she walk , and she walk , and she walk till she come to the giant , and pray him to tell her if he have see three young men pass that way seek the distant mountain . '
I have see them pas , but they have never return , and by this I know that the spell have fall upon them . '
` And what must I do to set them free , and to find the water of life , and the talk bird , and a branch of the tree of beauty ? '
` You must go to that mountain , which be so full of stone that your foot will hardly find a place to tread , and a you climb you will hear a noise a if all the stone in the world be mock you ; but pay no heed to anything you may hear , and , once you gain the top , you have gain everything . '
The girl thank him for his counsel , and set out for the mountain ; and scarcely have she go a few step upwards when cry and scream break forth around her , and she felt a if each stone she tread on be a living thing .
But she remember the word of the giant , and know not what have befall her brother , and keep her face steadily towards the mountain top , which grow near and near every moment .
But a she mount the clamour increase sevenfold : high above them all ring the voice of her three brother .
But the girl take no heed , and at last her foot stand upon the top .
Then she look round , and saw , lie in a hollow , the pool of the water of life .
And she take the brazen pitcher that she have bring with her , and fill it to the brim .
By the side of the pool stand the tree of beauty , with the talk bird on one of it bough ; and she catch the bird , and place it in a cage , and break off one of the branch .
After that she turn , and go joyfully down the hill again , carry her treasure , but her long climb have tire her out , and the brazen pitcher be very heavy , and a she walk a few drop of the water spilt on the stone , and a it touch them they change into young men and maiden , crowd about her to give thanks for their deliverance .
So she learn by this how the evil spell might be break , and she carefully sprinkle every stone till there be not one left -- only a great company of youth and girl who follow her down the mountain .
When they arrive at the palace she do not lose a moment in plant the branch of the tree of beauty and water it with the water of life .
And the branch shot up into a tree , and be heavy with flower , and the talk bird nestle in it branch .
Now the fame of these wonder be noise abroad , and the people flock in great number to see the three marvel , and the maiden who have win them ; and among the sightseer come the king 's son , who would not go till everything be show him , and till he have hear how it have all happen .
And the prince admire the strangeness and beauty of the treasure in the palace , but more than all he admire the beauty and courage of the maiden who have bring them there .
So he go home and tell his parent , and gain their consent to wed her for his wife .
Then the marriage be celebrate in the church adjoin the palace .
Then the bridegroom take her to his own home , where they live happy for ever after .
The Wounded Lion Cuentos Populars Catalans .
There be once a girl so poor that she have nothing to live on , and wander about the world ask for charity .
One day she arrive at a thatched cottage , and inquire if they could give her any work .
The farmer say he want a cowherd , a his own have leave him , and if the girl like the place she might take it .
So she become a cowherd .
One morning she be drive her cow through the meadow when she hear near by a loud groan that almost sound human .
She hasten to the spot from which the noise come , and find it proceed from a lion who lay stretch upon the ground .
You can guess how frightened she be !
But the lion seem in such pain that she be sorry for him , and draw near and near till she saw he have a large thorn in one foot .
She pull out the thorn and bind up the place , and the lion be grateful , and lick her hand by way of thanks with his big rough tongue .
When the girl have finish she go back to find the cow , but they have go , and though she hunt everywhere she never find them ; and she have to return home and confess to her master , who scold her bitterly , and afterwards beat her .
Then he say , ` Now you will have to look after the ass . '
So every day she have to take the ass to the wood to fee , until one morning , exactly a year after she have find the lion , she hear a groan which sound quite human .
She go straight to the place from which the noise come , and , to her great surprise , behold the same lion stretch on the ground with a deep wound across his face .
This time she be not afraid at all , and run towards him , wash the wound and lay soothe herb upon it ; and when she have bound it up the lion thank her in the same manner a before .
After that she return to her flock , but they be nowhere to be see .
She search here and she search there , but they have vanish completely !
Then she have to go home and confess to her master , who first scold her and afterwards beat her .
` Now go , ' he end , ` and look after the pig ! '
So the next day she take out the pig , and find them such good feeding ground that they grow fat every day .
Another year pass by , and one morning when the maiden be out with her pig she hear a groan which sound quite human .
She run to see what it be , and find her old friend the lion , wound through and through , fast die under a tree .
She fell on her knee before him and wash his wound one by one , and lay heal herb upon them .
And the lion lick her hand and thank her , and ask if she would not stay and sit by him .
But the girl say she have her pig to watch , and she must go and see after them .
So she run to the place where she have leave them , but they have vanish a if the earth have swallow them up .
She whistle and call , but only the bird answer her .
Then she sink down on the ground and weep bitterly , not dare to return home until some hour have pass away .
And when she have have her cry out she get up and search all up and down the wood .
But it be no use ; there be not a sign of the pig .
At last she think that perhaps if she climb a tree she might see far .
But no sooner be she seat on the high branch than something happen which put the pig quite out of her head .
This be a handsome young man who be come down the path ; and when he have almost reach the tree he pull aside a rock and disappear behind it .
The maiden rub her eye and wonder if she have be dream .
Next she think , ' I will not stir from here till I see him come out , and discover who he be . '
Accordingly she wait , and at dawn the next morning the rock move to one side and a lion come out .
When he have go quite out of sight the girl climb down from the tree and go to the rock , which she push aside , and enter the opening before her .
The path lead to a beautiful house .
She go in , swept and dust the furniture , and put everything tidy .
Then she eat a very good dinner , which be on a shelf in the corner , and once more clamber up to the top of her tree .
As the sun set she saw the same young man walk gaily down the path , and , a before , he push aside the rock and disappear behind it .
Next morning out come the lion .
He look sharply about him on all side , but saw no one , and then vanish into the forest .
The maiden then come down from the tree and do exactly a she have do the day before .
Thus three day go by , and every day she go and tidy up the palace .
At length , when the girl find she be no nearer to discover the secret , she resolve to ask him , and in the evening when she catch sight of him come through the wood she come down from the tree and beg him to tell her his name .
The young man look very pleased to see her , and say he think it must be she who have secretly keep his house for so many day .
