And he add that he be a prince enchant by a powerful giant , but be only allow to take his own shape at night , for all day he be force to appear a the lion whom she have so often help ; and , more than this , it be the giant who have steal the ox and the ass and the pig in revenge for her kindness .
And the girl ask him , ` What can I do to disenchant you ? '
But he say he be afraid it be very difficult , because the only way be to get a lock of hair from the head of a king 's daughter , to spin it , and to make from it a cloak for the giant , who live up on the top of a high mountain .
` Very well , ' answer the girl , ' I will go to the city , and knock at the door of the king 's palace , and ask the princess to take me a a servant . '
So they part , and when she arrive at the city she walk about the street cry , ` Who will hire me for a servant ?
Who will hire me for a servant ? '
But , though many people like her look , for she be clean and neat , the maiden would listen to none , and still continue cry , ` Who will hire me for a servant ?
Who will hire me for a servant ? '
At last there come the waiting-maid of the princess .
` What can you do ? '
she say ; and the girl be force to confess that she could do very little .
` Then you will have to do scullion 's work , and wash up dish , ' say she ; and they go straight back to the palace .
Then the maiden dress her hair afresh , and make herself look very neat and smart , and everyone admire and praise her , till by-and-bye it come to the ear of the princess .
And she send for the girl , and when she saw her , and how beautifully she have dress her hair , the princess tell her she be to come and comb out hers .
Now the hair of the princess be very thick and long , and shone like the sun .
And the girl comb it and comb it till it be brighter than ever .
And the princess be pleased , and bid her come every day and comb her hair , till at length the girl take courage , and beg leave to cut off one of the long , thick lock .
The princess , who be very proud of her hair , do not like the idea of part with any of it , so she say no .
But the girl could not give up hope , and each day she entreat to be allow to cut off just one tress .
At length the princess lose patience , and exclaim , ` You may have it , then , on condition that you shall find the handsome prince in the world to be my bridegroom ! '
And the girl answer that she would , and cut off the lock , and weave it into a coat that glitter like silk , and bring it to the young man , who tell her to carry it straight to the giant .
But that she must be careful to cry out a long way off what she have with her , or else he would spring upon her and run her through with his sword .
So the maiden depart and climb up the mountain , but before she reach the top the giant heard her footstep , and rush out breathe fire and flame , have a sword in one hand and a club in the other .
But she cry loudly that she have bring him the coat , and then he grow quiet , and invite her to come into his house .
He try on the coat , but it be too short , and he throw it off , and declare it be no use .
And the girl pick it up sadly , and return quite in despair to the king 's palace .
The next morning , when she be comb the princess 's hair , she beg leave to cut off another lock .
At first the princess say no , but the girl beg so hard that at length she give in on condition that she should find her a prince a bridegroom .
The maiden tell her that she have already find him , and spin the lock into shin stuff , and fasten it on to the end of the coat .
And when it be finish she carry it to the giant .
This time it fit him , and he be quite pleased , and ask her what he could give her in return .
And she say that the only reward he could give her be to take the spell off the lion and bring him back to his own shape .
For a long time the giant would not hear of it , but in the end he give in , and tell her exactly how it must all be do .
She be to kill the lion herself and cut him up very small ; then she must burn him , and cast his ash into the water , and out of the water the prince would come free from enchantment for ever .
But the maiden go away weep , l the giant should have deceive her , and that after she have kill the lion she would find she have also slay the prince .
Weeping she come down the mountain , and weep she join the prince , who be await her at the bottom ; and when he have hear her story he comfort her , and bid her be of good courage , and to do the bidding of the giant .
And the maiden believe what the prince tell her ; and in the morning when he put on his lion 's form she take a knife and slew him , and cut him up very small , and burn him , and cast his ash into the water , and out of the water come the prince , beautiful a the day , and a glad to look upon a the sun himself .
Then the young man thank the maiden for all she have do for him , and say she should be his wife and none other .
But the maiden only weep sore , and answer that that she could never be , for she have give her promise to the princess when she cut off her hair that the prince should wed her and her only .
But the prince reply , ` If it be the princess , we must go quickly .
Come with me . '
So they go together to the king 's palace .
And when the king and queen and princess saw the young man a great joy fill their heart , for they know him for the eldest son , who have long ago be enchant by a giant and lose to them .
And he ask his parent ' consent that he might marry the girl who have save him , and a great feast be make , and the maiden become a princess , and in due time a queen , and she richly deserve all the honour shower upon her .
The Man Without a Heart Once upon a time there be seven brother , who be orphan , and have no sister .
Therefore they be oblige to do all their own housework .
This they do not like at all ; so after much deliberation they decide to get marry .
There be , unfortunately , no young girl to be find in the place where they live ; but the elder brother agree to go out into the world and seek for bride , promise to bring back a very pretty wife for the young also if he would meanwhile stay at home and take care of the house .
He consent willingly , and the six young men set off in good spirit .
On their way they come to a small cottage stand quite by itself in a wood ; and before the door stand an old , old man , who accost the brother say , ` Hullo , you young fellow !
Whither away so fast and cheerily ? '
` We be go to find bonny bride for ourselves , and one for our young brother at home , ' they reply .
` Oh !
dear youth , ' say the old man , ' I be terribly lonely here ; pray bring a bride for me also ; only remember , she must be young and pretty . '
` What do a shrivelled old grey thing like that want with a pretty young bride ? '
think the brother , and go on their way .
Presently they come to a town where be seven sister , a young and as lovely a anyone could wish .
Each brother choose one , and the young they keep for their brother at home .
Then the whole party set out on the return journey , and again their path lead through the wood and past the old man 's cottage .
There he stand before the door , and cry : ` Oh !
you fine fellow , what a charming bride you have bring me ! '
` She be not for you , say the young men .
` She be for our young brother , a we promise . '
` What ! '
say the old man , ` promise !
I 'll make you eat your promise ! '
And with that he take his magic wand , and , murmur a charm , he touch both brother and bride , and immediately they be turn into grey stone .
Only the young sister he have not bewitch .
He take her into the cottage , and from that time she be oblige to keep house for him .
She be not very unhappy , but one thought trouble her .
What if the old man should die and leave her here alone in the solitary cottage deep in the heart of the wood !
She would be a ` terribly lonely ' a he have formerly be .
One day she tell him of her fear .
` Do n't be anxious , ' he say .
` You need neither fear my death nor desire it , for I have no heart in my breast !
However , if I should die , you will find my wand above the door , and with it you can set free your sister and their lover .
Then you will surely have company enough . '
` Where in all the world do you keep your heart , if not in your breast ? '
ask the girl .
` Do you want to know everything ? '
her husband say .
` Well , if you must know , my heart be in the bed-cover . '
When the old man have go out about his business his bride pass her time in embroider beautiful flower on the bed quilt to make his heart happy .
The old man be much amuse .
He laugh , and say to her : ` You be a good child , but I be only joke .
My heart be really in -- in -- ' ` Now where be it , dear husband ? '
` It be in the doorway , ' he reply .
Next day , while he be out , the girl decorate the door with gay feather and fresh flower , and hung garland upon it .
And on his return the old fellow ask what it all mean . '
I do it to show my love for your heart , ' say the girl .
And again the old man smile , say , ` You be a dear child , but my heart be not in the doorway . '
Then the poor young bride be very vexed , and say , ` Ah , my dear !
you really have a heart somewhere , so you may die and leave me all alone . '
The old man do his best to comfort her by repeat all he have say before , but she beg him afresh to tell her truly where his heart be and at last he tell her .
` Far , far from here , ' say he , ` in a lonely spot , stand a great church , as old a old can be .
Its door be of iron , and round it run a deep moat , span by no bridge .
Within that church be a bird which fly up and down ; it never eat , and never drink , and never dy .
No one can catch it , and while that bird live so shall I , for in it be my heart . '
It make the little bride quite sad to think she could do nothing to show her love for the old man 's heart .
She use to think about it a she sit all alone during the long day , for her husband be almost always out .
One day a young traveller come past the house , and see such a pretty girl he wish her ` Good day . '
She return his greeting , and a he draw near she ask him whence he come and where he be go .
` Alas ! '
sigh the youth , ' I be very sorrowful .
I have six brother , who go away to find bride for themselves and one for me ; but they have never come home , so now I be go to look for them . '
` Oh , good friend , ' say the girl , ` you need go no farther .
Come , sit down , eat and drink , and afterwards I 'll tell you all about it . '
She give him food , and when he have finish his meal she tell him how his brother have come to the town where she live with her sister , how they have each choose a bride , and , take herself with them , have start for home .
She weep a she tell how the others be turn to stone , and how she be keep a the old man 's bride .
She leave out nothing , even tell him the story of her husband 's heart .
When the young man heard this he say : ' I shall go in search of the bird .
It may be that God will help me to find and catch it . '
` Yes , do go , ' she say ; ` it will be a good deed , for then you can set your brother and my sister free . '
Then she hide the young man , for it be now late , and her husband would soon be home .
Next morning , when the old man have go out , she prepare a supply of provision for her guest , and send him off on his travel , wish him good luck and success .
He walk on and on till he think it must be time for breakfast ; so he open his knapsack , and be delight to find such a store of good thing .
` What a feast ! '
he exclaim ; ` will anyone come and share it ? '
` Moo-oo , ' sound close behind him , and look round he saw a great red ox , which say , ' I have much pleasure in accept your kind invitation . '
` I 'm delighted to see you .
Pray help yourself .
All I have be at your service , ' say the hospitable youth .
And the ox lay down comfortably , lick his lip , and make a hearty meal .
` Many thanks to you , ' say the animal a it rise up .
` When you be in danger or necessity call me , even if only by a thought , ' and it disappear among the bush .
The young man pack up all the food that be leave , and wander on till the shortening shadow and his own hunger warn him that it be midday .
he lay the cloth on the ground and spread out his provision , say at the same time : ` Dinner be ready , and anyone who wish to share it be welcome . '
Then there be a great rustling in the undergrowth , and out run a wild boar , grunt , ` Umph , umph , umph ; someone say dinner be ready .
Was it you ?
and do you mean me to come ? '
` By all mean .
Help yourself to what I have , ' say the young traveller .
And the two enjoy their meal together .
Afterwards the boar get up , say , ` Thank you ; when in need you be you must quickly call for me , ' and he roll off .
For a long time the youth walk on .
By even he be mile away .
He felt hungry again , and , have still some provision leave , think he have well make ready his supper .
When it be all spread out he cry a before , ` Anyone who care to share my meal be welcome . '
He hear a sound overhead like the flapping of wing , and a shadow be cast upon the ground .
Then a huge griffin appear , say : ' I hear someone give an invitation to eat ; be there anything for me ? '
` Why not ? '
say the youth .
` Come down and take all you want .
There wo n't be much leave after this . '
So the griffin alight and eat his fill , say , a he fly away , ` Call me if you need me . '
` What a hurry he be in ! '
the youth say to himself .
` He might have be able to direct me to the church , for I shall never find it alone . '
He gather up his thing , and start to walk a little farther before rest .
He have not go far when all of a sudden he saw the church !
He soon come to it , or rather to the wide and deep moat which surround it without a single bridge by which to cross .
It be too late to attempt anything now ; and , besides , the poor youth be very tired , so he lay down on the ground and fell fast asleep .
Next morning , when he awake , he begin to wish himself over the moat ; and the thought occur to him that if only the red ox be there , and thirsty enough to drink up all the water in the moat , he might walk across it dry shod .
Scarcely have the thought cross his brain before the ox appear and begin to drink up the water .
The grateful youth hasten across as soon a the moat be dry , but find it impossible to penetrate the thick wall and strong iron door of the church . '
I believe that big boar would be of more use here than I be , ' he think , and lo !
at the wish the wild boar come and begin to push hard against the wall .
He manage to loosen one stone with his tusk , and , have make a beginning , stone after stone be poke out till he have make quite a large hole , big enough to let a man go through .
The young man quickly enter the church , and saw a bird fly about , but he could not catch it .
` Oh ! '
he exclaim , ` if only the griffin be here , he would soon catch it . '
At these word the griffin appear , and , seize the bird , give it to the youth , who carry it off carefully , while the griffin fly away .
The young man hurry home as fast a possible , and reach the cottage before evening .
He tell his story to the little bride , who , after give him some food and drink , hide him with his bird beneath the bed .
Presently the old man come home , and complain of feeling ill .
Nothing , he say , would go well with him any more : his ` heart bird ' be catch .
The youth under the bed heard this , and think , ` This old fellow have do me no particular harm , but then he have bewitch my brother and their bride , and have keep my bride for himself , and that be certainly bad enough . '
So he pinch the bird , and the old man cry , ` Ah !
I feel death grip me !
Child , I be die ! '
With these word he fell faint from his chair , and a the youth , before he know what he be do , have squeeze the bird to death , the old man die also .
Out crept the young man from under the bed , and the girl take the magic wand -LRB- which she find where the old man have tell her -RRB- , and , touch the twelve grey stone , transform them at once into the six brother and their bride .
Then there be great joy , and kiss and embrace .
And there lay the old man , quite dead , and no magic wand could restore him to life , even have they wish it .
After that they all go away and be marry , and live many year happily together .
The Two Brothers Sicilianische Malirchen .
L. Gonzenbach .
Long ago there live two brother , both of them very handsome , and both so very poor that they seldom have anything to eat but the fish which they catch .
One day they have be out in their boat since sunrise without a single bite , and be just think of put up their line and go home to bed when they felt a little feeble tug , and , draw in hastily , they find a tiny fish at the end of the hook .
` What a wretched little creature ! '
cry one brother .
` However , it be well than nothing , and I will bake him with bread crumb and have him for supper . '
` Oh , do not kill me yet ! '
beg the fish ; ' I will bring you good luck -- indeed I will ! '
` You silly thing ! '
say the young man ; ` I 've catch you , and I shall eat you . '
But his brother be sorry for the fish , and put in a word for him .
` Let the poor little fellow live .
He would hardly make one bite , and , after all , how do we know we be not throw away our luck !
Put him back into the sea .
It will be much well . '
` If you will let me live , ' say the fish , ` you will find on the sand to-morrow morning two beautiful horse splendidly saddle and bridle , and on them you can go through the world a knight seek adventure . '
` Oh dear , what nonsense ! '
exclaim the elder ; ` and , besides , what proof have we that you be speak the truth ? '
But again the young brother interpose : ` Oh , do let him live !
You know if he be lie to u we can always catch him again .
It be quite worth while try . '
At last the young man give in , and throw the fish back into the sea ; and both brother go supperless to bed , and wonder what fortune the next day would bring .
At the first streak of dawn they be both up , and in a very few minute be run down to the shore .
And there , just a the fish have say , stand two magnificent horse , saddle and bridle , and on their back lay suit of armour and under-dresses , two sword , and two purse of gold .
` There ! '
say the young brother .
` Are you not thankful you do not eat that fish ?
He have bring u good luck , and there be no know how great we may become !
Now , we will each seek our own adventure .
If you will take one road I will go the other . '
` Very well , ' reply the elder ; ` but how shall we let each other know if we be both live ? '
` Do you see this fig-tree ? '
say the younger .
` Well , whenever we want news of each other we have only to come here and make a slit with our sword in the back .
If milk flow , it be a sign that we be well and prosperous ; but if , instead of milk , there be blood , then we be either dead or in great danger . '
Then the two brother put on their armour , buckle their sword , and pocket their puree ; and , after take a tender farewell of each other , they mount their horse and go their various way .
The elder brother rode straight on till he reach the border of a strange kingdom .
He cross the frontier , and soon find himself on the bank of a river ; and before him , in the middle of the stream , a beautiful girl sit chain to a rock and weep bitterly .
For in this river dwell a serpent with seven head , who threaten to lay waste the whole land by breathe fire and flame from his nostril unless the king send him every morning a man for his breakfast .
This have go on so long that now there be no men leave , and he have be oblige to send his own daughter instead , and the poor girl be wait till the monster get hungry and felt incline to eat her .
When the young man saw the maiden weeping bitterly he say to her , ` What be the matter , my poor girl ? '
` Oh ! '
she answer , ' I be chain here till a horrible serpent with seven head come to eat me .
Oh , sir , do not linger here , or he will eat you too . ' '
I shall stay , ' reply the young man , ` for I mean to set you free . '
` That be impossible .
You do not know what a fearful monster the serpent be ; you can do nothing against him . '
` That be my affair , beautiful captive , ' answer he ; ` only tell me , which way will the serpent come ? '
` Well , if you be resolve to free me , listen to my advice .
Stand a little on one side , and then , when the serpent rise to the surface , I will say to him , `` O serpent , to-day you can eat two people .
But you have good begin first with the young man , for I be chain and can not run away . ''
When he hear this most likely he will attack you . '
So the young man stand carefully on one side , and by-and-bye he hear a great rushing in the water ; and a horrible monster come up to the surface and look out for the rock where the king 's daughter be chain , for it be get late and he be hungry .
But she cry out , ' O serpent , to-day you can eat two people .
And you have good begin with the young man , for I be chain and can not run away . '
Then the serpent make a rush at the youth with wide open jaw to swallow him at one gulp , but the young man leap aside and draw his sword , and fought till he have cut off all the seven head .
And when the great serpent lay dead at his foot he loose the bond of the king 's daughter , and she fling herself into his arm and say , ` You have save me from that monster , and now you shall be my husband , for my father have make a proclamation that whoever could slay the serpent should have his daughter to wife . '
But he answer , ' I can not become your husband yet , for I have still far to travel .
But wait for me seven year and seven month .
Then , if I do not return , you be free to marry whom you will .
And in case you should have forget , I will take these seven tongue with me so that when I bring them forth you may know that I be really he who slew the serpent . '
So say he cut out the seven tongue , and the princess give him a thick cloth to wrap them in ; and he mount his horse and ride away .
Not long after he have go there arrive at the river a slave who have be send by the king to learn the fate of his beloved daughter .
And when the slave saw the princess stand free and safe before him , with the body of the monster lie at her foot , a wicked plan come into his head , and he say , ` Unless you promise to tell your father it be I who slew the serpent , I will kill you and bury you in this place , and no one will ever know what befell . '
What could the poor girl do ?
This time there be no knight to come to her aid .
So she promise to do a the slave wish , and he take up the seven head and bring the princess to her father .
Oh , how enchant the king be to see her again , and the whole town share his joy !
And the slave be call upon to tell how he have slay the monster , and when he have end the king declare that he should have the princess to wife .
But she fling herself at her father 's foot , and pray him to delay .
` You have pass your royal word , and can not go back from it Yet grant me this grace , and let seven year and seven month go by before you wed me .
When they be over , then I will marry the slave . '
And the king listen to her , and seven year and seven month she look for her bridegroom , and weep for him night and day .
All this time the young man be rid through the world , and when the seven year and seven month be over he come back to the town where the princess live -- only a few day before the wedding .
And he stand before the king , and say to him : ` Give me your daughter , O king , for I slew the seven-headed serpent .
And a a sign that my word be true , look on these seven tongue , which I cut from his seven head , and on this embroidered cloth , which be give me by your daughter . '
Then the princess lift up her voice and say , ` Yes , dear father , he have speak the truth , and it be he who be my real bridegroom .
Yet pardon the slave , for he be sorely tempt . '
But the king answer , ` Such treachery can no man pardon .
Quick , away with him , and off with his head ! '
So the false slave be put to death , that none might follow in his footstep , and the wedding feast be hold , and the heart of all rejoice that the true bridegroom have come at last .
These two live happy and contentedly for a long while , when one evening , a the young man be look from the window , he saw on a mountain that lay out beyond the town a great bright light .
` What can it be ? '
he say to his wife .
` Ah !
do not look at it , ' she answer , ` for it come from the house of a wicked witch whom no man can manage to kill . '
But the princess have well have keep silence , for her word make her husband 's heart burn within him , and he long to try his strength against the witch 's cunning .
And all day long the feeling grow strong , till the next morning he mount his horse , and in spite of his wife 's tear , he ride off to the mountain .
The distance be great than he think , and it be dark before he reach the foot of the mountain ; indeed , he could not have find the road at all have it not be for the bright light , which shine like the moon on his path .
At length he come to the door of a fine castle , which have a blaze stream from every window .
He mount a flight of step and enter a hall where a hideous old woman be sit on a golden chair .
She scowl at the young man and say , ` With a single one of the hair of my head I can turn you into stone . '
` Oh , what nonsense ! '
cry he .
` Be quiet , old woman .
What could you do with one hair ? '
But the witch pull out a hair and lay it on his shoulder , and his limb grow cold and heavy , and he could not stir .
Now at this very moment the young brother be think of him , and wonder how he have get on during all the year since they have part . '
I will go to the fig-tree , ' he say to himself , ` to see whether he be alive or dead . '
So he ride through the forest till he come where the fig-tree stood , and cut a slit in the bark , and wait .
In a moment a little gurgling noise be hear , and out come a stream of blood , run fast .
` Ah , woe be me ! '
he cry bitterly .
` My brother be dead or die !
Shall I ever reach him in time to save his life ? '
Then , leap on his horse , he shout , ` Now , my steed , fly like the wind ! '
and they ride right through the world , till one day they come to the town where the young man and his wife live .
Here the princess have be sit every day since the morning that her husband have leave her , weep bitter tear , and listen for his footstep .
And when she saw his brother ride under the balcony she mistake him for her own husband , for they be so alike that no man might tell the difference , and her heart bound , and , lean down , she call to him , ` At last !
